ideas about "natural" life had become fashionable, even amongst the
aristocrats. And what could be nicer than to have a bit of "natural" life in
between the ceremony and glitter of the court.

他深愛的妻子也幫不上大忙。Marie Antoinette 王后是一位 Austria 公主，Maria Theresa 的女兒。她活潑、喜歡華服和歡樂的宴會，但她並不聰明。Marie Antoinette 也有一個嗜好。你看，到了這個時候，Rousseau 關於「自然」生活的思想已經變得時髦了，甚至在貴族中間也是如此。在宮廷的典禮和光華之間來一點「自然」的生活，有什麼比這更好的呢？

And so, Queen Marie Antoinette had a little farm complete with a
cow-shed arranged for her in the vast parks of Versailles. And she and
her court ladies would dress up as peasant women, and go down to the
little farm and milk the cows and sing country-songs - and pretend they
were country women for a couple of hours.

於是，Marie Antoinette 王后在 Versailles 廣闊的園林中安排了一個小農場，配有一間牛棚。她和宮廷的女士們會打扮成農婦，走到小農場去擠牛奶、唱鄉村歌謠——假裝自己當幾個小時的鄉下女人。

Poor Marie Antoinette had no idea that the real peasants of France,
hardworking, hungry, and in rags, looked at her "game" as an insult, as if
she was making fun of their misery and poverty. But Marie Antoinette
was only thoughtless and silly.

可憐的 Marie Antoinette 完全不知道，法國真正的農民——辛勤勞作、飢腸轆轆、衣衫襤褸——把她的「遊戲」視為一種侮辱，彷彿她在嘲弄他們的苦難和貧窮。但 Marie Antoinette 只是不經大腦、愚蠢罷了。

There is a story (I don't know if it is true) that when Marie Antoinette
was told one day that peasants were rebellious because they had no
bread, she asked astonished "But, if they have no bread, why don't they
eat cakes?"

有一個故事（我不知道是否屬實），有一天當 Marie Antoinette 被告知農民因為沒有麵包而叛亂時，她驚訝地問：「可是，如果他們沒有麵包，為什麼不吃蛋糕呢？」

France was in a state when such a king and such a queen were of no
use at all!

法國正處在這樣一個國王和這樣一個王后完全派不上用場的境地！

The Seven Years' War had left France desperately poor, and then
France had fought another war against Britain to help America, and this
war had also cost money and brought no benefits to France.

七年戰爭使法國窮困潦倒，接著法國又打了一場對抗英國的戰爭來幫助美國，這場戰爭同樣花了大筆金錢卻沒有給法國帶來任何好處。

The working people - the peasants and the middle-classes - had been
taxed and taxed until they could not be taxed any more, but the rich
aristocrats as well as the bishops, who had money and vast estates, were
not taxed at all. Since the Middle Ages the Church and the noblemen had
been exempt from taxes, and it seemed as if the time had come that the
Church and the noblemen, too, should make a contribution to the taxes.

勞動人民——農民和中產階級——被一而再、再而三地課稅，直到再也不能再課了。但富有的貴族和那些擁有金錢和大片莊園的主教們卻根本不用繳稅。自中世紀以來教會和貴族就免稅，現在看來，教會和貴族也該為稅收做出貢獻的時候到了。

But the bishops and noblemen of France were not willing to give up
their ancient privileges to be free from taxation.

但法國的主教和貴族們不願意放棄他們自古以來的免稅特權。

And then in 1788 there was a terribly bad harvest in France followed
by an abnormally long and hard winter. There was a disastrous foodshortage all over France, and the only way to save thousands from starvation was to buy corn from other countries; but to buy corn - thousands of tons - money was required, and there was no money in the
treasury for such a big purchase.

然後在 1788 年，法國遭遇了極其嚴重的歉收，緊接著是一個異常漫長而嚴酷的冬天。法國全境出現了災難性的糧食短缺，拯救成千上萬人免於餓死的唯一辦法是從其他國家購買穀物；但購買數千噸穀物需要資金，國庫裡卻沒有錢來進行如此大的採購。

In this desperate situation Louis XVI could and should have ordered
the noblemen and the Church to pay taxes, but he failed to take this
radical action. Instead he called a meeting of the Estates General, the
"three estates." The bishops of the Church were the first estate, the aristocrats were the second estate, and the middle-class were the third estate. And all three "estates" sent their representatives to this meeting at
Versailles in 1789.

在這個絕望的處境中，Louis 十六本可以也本應該命令貴族和教會繳稅，但他沒能採取這個激進的行動。相反，他召集了三級會議——「三個等級」。教會的主教是第一等級，貴族是第二等級，中產階級是第三等級。三個「等級」都派出了代表參加 1789 年在 Versailles 舉行的這次會議。

Louis XVI hoped that at this meeting the three estates would find by
agreement a way to solve the desperate problem of feeding the French
people. But the only answer would have been for the Church and the
aristocrats to give up their privilege and to pay taxes. And this was exactly what they did not want to do. There was a lot of bickering and argument - but no agreement on anything.

Louis 十六希望在這次會議上三個等級能通過協議找到解決法國人民飢餓問題的辦法。但唯一的答案本該是教會和貴族放棄特權、開始繳稅。而這恰恰是他們不願做的事。爭吵和辯論不斷——但什麼都達不成共識。

And then something quite unexpected happened. The "deputies" of
the third estate declared that they stood for ninety-five per cent of the
population, that they were therefore the true representatives of the
French nation - and they were the true parliament of France and would
make the laws which France needed.

接著發生了完全出乎意料的事。第三等級的「代表」宣布，他們代表了百分之九十五的人口，因此他們才是法蘭西民族的真正代表——他們才是法國真正的議會，並將制定法國所需的法律。

They did not use the word "parliament" - they called it "National
Assembly" but it meant the same thing. The deputies of the third estate
simply declared they were going to make new laws, without asking the
King, or the aristocracy or the bishops for agreement.

他們沒有用「議會」這個詞——他們稱之為「國民議會」，但意思是一樣的。第三等級的代表們乾脆宣布，他們要制定新的法律，不需要徵求國王、貴族或主教的同意。

King Louis XVI had not expected that such a thing could happen in
France, that commoners would take over government and make their
own laws.
He gave
orders that the deputies should disband
and go
home. The bishops and noblemen obeyed - but the deputies of the commoners replied: "We are here by the will of the people and we shall not
go unless we are forced by the bayonets of your soldiers."

Louis 十六國王沒有料到這樣的事會在法國發生——平民竟然接管政府，制定自己的法律。他下令代表們解散回家。主教和貴族們服從了——但平民代表們回答：「我們是憑人民的意志來到這裡的，除非你的士兵用刺刀逼我們，否則我們不會離開。」

Another king might have used soldiers against them, but Louis XVI, up
to the end of his life, wanted to avoid bloodshed. He did not send soldiers, and the National Assembly stayed and defied his orders.

另一位國王可能會動用軍隊對付他們，但 Louis 十六直到生命的最後都想避免流血。他沒有派出士兵，國民議會留了下來，公然違抗他的命令。

In the meantime, Paris, which is only a short distance from Versailles,
was in a fever of excitement. In the open squares, in the streets crowds
of thousands listened to speakers who exhorted them to stand by their
deputies and to come and fight for them if the King used force against
them.

與此同時，離 Versailles 不遠的 Paris 陷入了狂熱的興奮之中。在開放的廣場上、在街道上，成千上萬的群眾聆聽演說家們激勵他們支持自己的代表，如果國王對代表動武就前去為他們而戰。

Suddenly there were rumours (quite false, of course) that the King
had sent soldiers to arrest the deputies. It is quite certain that these
rumours were spread
deliberately by men who wanted
a revolution
against the King. And these rumours turned the exited crowds into an
angry and howling mob. In one public square, a young man, Camille
Desmoulins by name, jumped on a table, fired a pistol into the air and
shouted: "To arms, citizens - fight for freedom!"

突然間傳出謠言（當然完全是假的），說國王派了士兵去逮捕代表們。毫無疑問，這些謠言是由想要發動反對國王的革命的人蓄意散布的。這些謠言把激動的群眾變成了憤怒咆哮的暴民。在一個公共廣場上，一個叫 Camille Desmoulins 的年輕人跳上一張桌子，向空中開了一槍，高喊：「拿起武器，公民們——為自由而戰！」

And like waves in a storm, the crowds surged through the streets of
Paris, they plundered the shops of gunsmiths, they stole knives from
butchers' shops, they stormed the Arsenal, the weapon-store of the
French army.

像暴風中的巨浪一樣，群眾湧過 Paris 的街道，他們搶劫槍械店，從肉舖偷走刀子，衝進了法國軍隊的武器庫——兵工廠。

It is quite certain that this crazy, howling, rioting mob was directed by
people who knew exactly what they wanted all along - and used the rabble for their own purposes. And once the crowds were armed they
surged to a huge prison-fortress in the East of Paris, called the Bastille.

完全可以確定的是，這群瘋狂咆哮的暴亂群眾是被一些人在幕後指揮著——這些人從一開始就清楚知道自己要什麼，利用暴民來達到自己的目的。群眾一旦武裝起來，就湧向 Paris 東部一座巨大的監獄堡壘——Bastille。

The officer in charge of the Bastille wanted to avoid bloodshed. He offered to open the gates and to surrender the Bastille if he and his soldiers were allowed to leave unharmed. The promise was given - but as
soon as the gates were opened the mob stormed in and killed the officer
and his men without mercy. Then the mob with great cheers set free the
seven prisoners they found in the jails of the Bastille. Five of them were
common thieves, one was a madman and only one man claimed he was
imprisoned without reason.

Bastille 的指揮官想要避免流血。他提出打開大門投降 Bastille，條件是允許他和他的士兵安全離開。承諾被給出了——但大門一打開，暴民就衝了進去，毫不留情地殺死了軍官和他的手下。然後暴民在一片歡呼聲中釋放了他們在 Bastille 牢房裡找到的七名囚犯。其中五個是普通小偷，一個是瘋子，只有一個人聲稱自己是無故被囚禁的。

This storming of the Bastille on July 14, 1789 was the beginning of the
French Revolution. It is still a national holiday in France.

1789 年 7 月 14 日攻占 Bastille 是法國大革命的開端。這一天至今仍是法國的國定假日。
Chapter 26
Liberty - Equality - Fraternity

第二十六章
自由、平等、博愛

The French Revolution began with the storming of the Bastille, when a mad crowd, excited by false rumours, stormed the old prison-fortress for no good reason at all. It was a sudden explosion, this revolution, but the gun-powder which exploded was the ideas of Rousseau and Voltaire. For years and years these ideas had spread amongst the people. More and more Frenchmen had come to think of monarchy and of aristocracy as a swindle; as useless remnants of the past that should be swept away. Even amongst the aristocrats themselves there were many who sympathized with the new ideas, and who looked forward to a world without the old privileges.

法國大革命始於攻佔 Bastille 監獄——一群被假消息煽動的瘋狂群眾，毫無正當理由地衝進這座古老的監獄要塞。這場革命如同一次突如其來的爆炸，而引爆的火藥正是 Rousseau 與 Voltaire 的思想。多年以來，這些思想在民間不斷擴散。越來越多法國人開始認為君主制與貴族制不過是一場騙局，是過時的殘餘，理當被掃除。甚至在貴族階層中，也有許多人同情這些新思想，期待一個沒有舊特權的世界。

Over many years revolutionary secret societies had been forming in France. In these secret societies men of high birth and commoners, lawyers, doctors and journalists came together and laid their plans to do away with the false things, with royalty and nobility as well as with the Church. And they also spoke in these secret meetings of the new order that should come after they had got rid of kings and aristocrats.

多年來，法國各地陸續成立了革命秘密結社。在這些秘密社團中，出身高貴者與平民、律師、醫生和記者齊聚一堂，共同謀劃要廢除那些虛偽之物——王權、貴族，以及教會。他們也在秘密集會中談論，當國王和貴族被推翻之後，應該建立怎樣的新秩序。

Again and again three words came up when they spoke of the future, three words which they believed would bring a new and better order not only to France but to humanity as a whole. The first one who used these three words and explained their meaning was one of those unknown messengers of the secret brotherhood of Rosicrucians. These three words were: liberty, equality and brotherhood.

每當他們談論未來時，三個詞語一再被提起——他們相信這三個詞不僅能為法國帶來嶄新而更好的秩序，更能惠及全人類。最早使用這三個詞並闡述其意義的人，是 Rosicrucians 秘密兄弟會中一位不知名的信使。這三個詞就是：自由、平等、博愛。

The meaning of these three words is this: In religion, in science, in art, there should be absolute liberty or freedom, everyone should be free to have their own opinion and to express it in words or in writing.

這三個詞的意義如下：在宗教、科學、藝術領域中，應當有絕對的自由——每個人都應該自由擁有自己的見解，並以言語或文字表達出來。

Human beings don't live in isolation, they live together with each other so there must be laws to regulate life together. But these laws must be the same for all, there cannot be special laws for the rich and other laws for the poor, or special laws for clever people and other laws for stupid ones. Before the law there must be equality.

人不是孤立生活的，人與人必須共同生活，因此需要法律來規範共同生活。但這些法律必須對所有人一視同仁——不能有專為富人設的法律和另一套給窮人的法律，也不能有給聰明人的法律和給愚笨者的法律。在法律面前，必須人人平等。

But there is still the work we do, and in our work we depend on each other. The scientist in his laboratory needs the farmer who grows the food and they both need the iron-worker to fashion their tools for them. In the end all people need each other - and that is the fraternity or brotherhood of work.

還有我們所從事的工作，在工作中我們彼此依賴。實驗室裡的科學家需要種植糧食的農夫，而他們倆都需要鐵匠為他們打造工具。歸根結柢，所有人都彼此需要——這就是工作中的博愛，也就是勞動的兄弟情誼。

In our thoughts we must have freedom, before the law, there must be equality, in our work there is - whether we are aware of it or not - brotherhood, for we all depend on other peoples' work as they depend on ours.

在思想上，我們必須擁有自由；在法律面前，必須有平等；在工作中——不論我們是否意識到——存在著博愛，因為我們都依賴他人的勞動，正如他人也依賴我們的勞動。

But these three - freedom, equality, brotherhood - must never get into the wrong place. A painter of little talent is, as a painter, not the equal of Leonardo. Or, if I have my own opinion about, let us say, music I don't have to change it for the sake of brotherhood, and agree with others. Freedom, equality and brotherhood each have their own place - and if any of them is put in the wrong place, the result is chaos.

然而這三者——自由、平等、博愛——絕不能放錯位置。一個才華平庸的畫家，作為畫家來說，並不等同於 Leonardo。又或者，如果我對音樂有自己的見解，我不必為了博愛而改變立場去附和他人。自由、平等、博愛各有其所屬的領域——如果其中任何一個被放到錯誤的位置，結果就是混亂。

This is what was originally said about the three ideas which should build a new order when the old order of kings and aristocracy had gone. But as time passed this original meaning of the three words was forgotten. When the conspirators who planned the French Revolution came together, they talked about freedom, equality and fraternity (or brotherhood) as if it did not matter where each belonged.

這就是關於這三個理念的原始論述——它們應當在舊的國王與貴族秩序消亡之後，建立起新的秩序。但隨著時間推移，這三個詞的原始意涵被遺忘了。當策劃法國大革命的密謀者聚在一起時，他們談論自由、平等、博愛，彷彿它們各自歸屬的領域毫不重要。

It was these conspirators, these plotters who roused the crowds by false rumours on July 14, 1789, who turned the mob against the Bastille and so started the French Revolution.

正是這些密謀者、這些策劃者，在 1789 年 7 月 14 日以假消息煽動群眾，驅使暴民衝向 Bastille，從而揭開了法國大革命的序幕。

And it was these conspirators who proclaimed to the people that the nations of the world should no longer be ruled by kings and noblemen, but by freedom, equality and fraternity, by liberté, egalité, fraternité as it is in French.

也正是這些密謀者向人民宣告：世界各國不應再由國王和貴族統治，而應以自由、平等、博愛來治理——用法語來說，就是 liberté, egalité, fraternité。

And these three words had an enormous effect. They roused people, it was as if they had been waiting to hear them - they shouted them, they roared them, they wrote them on their banners. But no one gave much thought to their real meaning and to their true place in life - and so the French Revolution which began with great hopes took a very tragic and terrible course.

這三個詞產生了巨大的效果。它們激起了人們的熱情，彷彿人們一直在等待聽到這些話——他們高喊著、怒吼著，將這些詞寫在旗幟上。但沒有人深思這些詞的真正含義，以及它們在生活中真正的位置——因此，這場以偉大希望開端的法國大革命，走上了極其悲慘而可怕的道路。

The National Assembly, the deputies of the common people, stayed together in defiance of King Louis XVI and made new laws. The new laws still recognized the King, but only as a servant of the will of the people. His own wishes no longer counted.

國民議會——平民的代表們——團結一致，不顧 Louis XVI 的反對，制定了新法律。新法律仍然承認國王的存在，但僅僅視他為人民意志的僕人。他本人的意願不再算數。

And of course, they made laws that from now on the Church and the aristocrats had to pay taxes, just like the bourgeois and the peasants.

當然，他們也立法規定，從今以後教會和貴族必須像資產階級和農民一樣繳稅。

And they made another law that everybody was free to speak or to write what he believed was true.

他們還制定了另一條法律，規定每個人都有自由去說出或寫下自己認為是真實的事情。

These laws made by the National Assembly became famous as the Declaration of the Rights of Man. They were received with joy in Paris, in the whole of France, and by freedom-loving people all over the world.

國民議會制定的這些法律，以《人權宣言》之名而聞名於世。這份宣言在 Paris、在整個法國，以及全世界熱愛自由的人們之間，都受到了歡欣鼓舞的接納。

But while the deputies made all these wise and just laws, the Parisian mob, goaded and incited by rabble-rousers, hunted for people who had made themselves unpopular in the old days: aristocrats who had ill-treated their servants, tax-collectors who had been too harsh, and when they found them they hanged them on lamp-posts in the streets.

然而，就在議員們制定這些明智且公正的法律的同時，Paris 的暴民在煽動者的唆使下，到處搜捕那些在舊時代不得人心的人：虐待僕人的貴族、過於嚴苛的稅吏——一旦找到這些人，就把他們吊死在街頭的路燈柱上。

And in the countryside bands of peasants burnt down the mansions and castles and murdered noblemen and their families - they even killed servants who remained loyal to their masters.

在鄉間，成群的農民燒毀莊園和城堡，殺害貴族及其家人——他們甚至殺死那些仍然忠於主人的僕人。

The aristocrats who could escape were fortunate. Disguised as common people they fled to Italy, Germany and England; many of the courtiers of Louis XVI fled, including his two brothers.

那些能夠逃走的貴族算是幸運的。他們偽裝成平民，逃往 Italy、Germany 和 England；Louis XVI 的許多廷臣都逃走了，包括他的兩個兄弟。

But neither the wise laws of the National Assembly nor the riots of the peasants were any help against the food-shortage. By October of this fateful year 1789, the people of Paris were famished. Once again rumours started, blaming the King for the food-shortage. The starving rabble of the slums, armed with pikes and knives and muskets marched to Versailles. During the day they only shouted and screamed outside the Palace, but when darkness fell they stormed inside. The Queen, Marie Antoinette, just got out of her room in time before the invaders broke in and slashed her bed with cutlasses believing she was still in it.

然而，國民議會的明智法律也好，農民的暴動也罷，都無法解決糧食短缺的問題。到了這命運之年 1789 年的十月，Paris 人民已經飢腸轆轆。謠言再次四起，把糧荒歸咎於國王。貧民窟中飢餓的暴民手持長矛、刀子和火槍，向 Versailles 進發。白天，他們只是在宮殿外面叫喊尖叫；但當夜幕降臨，他們便衝進了宮殿。王后 Marie Antoinette 及時逃離了自己的房間，入侵者隨即破門而入，用彎刀砍劈她的床鋪，以為她還躺在裡面。

In the end the mob was driven out of the palace by the National Guard, a kind of police force commanded by Lafayette, the hero of the American War of Independence, who was very popular.

最終，暴民被國民衛隊趕出了宮殿。國民衛隊是一支類似警察的武裝力量，由 Lafayette 指揮——他是美國獨立戰爭中的英雄，深受人民愛戴。

But the mob did not go away. They demanded now that the King and the whole royal family should come with them back to Paris to see for himself how the people suffered.

但暴民並沒有離去。他們要求國王和整個王室跟他們回 Paris，讓國王親眼看看人民遭受的苦難。

In order to avoid bloodshed, the King agreed. So he and his wife and children were put in a coach and surrounded by the rabble they left Versailles; they were never to see it again.

為了避免流血，國王同意了。於是他和妻子、孩子們被安置在一輛馬車裡，在暴民的包圍下離開了 Versailles——他們再也沒有回來過。

On they way the procession met carts taking flour to Paris - which put the mob in a happy mood. They shouted "We bring the baker and his

在途中，隊伍遇到了運送麵粉前往 Paris 的推車——這讓暴民心情大好。他們高喊：「我們把麵包師傅和他的

Chapter 27
The Tuileries

第二十七章
Tuileries 宮

wanted to crush the French Revolution before its ideas spread to their own countries. Powerful enemies were getting ready to attack France, and if Louis XVI tried to flee to join these enemies of France, he would be seen as a traitor, as a man who was on the side of Austria and Prussia against his own people.

想要在法國大革命的思想傳播到他們自己國家之前，將其扼殺。強大的敵人正準備進攻法國，而如果 Louis XVI 試圖逃跑去投靠這些法國的敵人，他將被視為叛徒——一個站在 Austria 和 Prussia 一邊、背叛自己人民的人。

That is why the deputies who wanted France to be a monarchy warned the King not to make any attempt to escape. If he tried and was caught his life would no longer be safe and even the deputies who were for him would then become his enemies.

正因如此，那些希望法國維持君主制的議員們警告國王，不要有任何逃跑的企圖。如果他嘗試逃跑並被抓住，他的生命將不再安全，甚至連支持他的議員們也會轉而成為他的敵人。

Louis XVI was warned repeatedly not to try to flee. It was good advice, but Louis was not a clever man and when some courtiers who still remained with him, told him they had arranged an escape for him and his family, he agreed.

Louis XVI 被一再警告不要嘗試逃跑。這是好的忠告，但 Louis 並不是個聰明人。當身邊仍然跟隨他的一些廷臣告訴他，他們已經為他和家人安排了逃亡計畫時，他同意了。

And so, at midnight on July 20, 1791, the royal family crept out of the Tuileries and set out in a coach drawn by six horses. Through the night and into the next day the coach travelled through France, nearer and nearer to the frontier.

就這樣，在 1791 年 7 月 20 日午夜，王室一家悄悄溜出 Tuileries 宮，坐上一輛由六匹馬拉的馬車出發了。馬車在夜色中穿越法國，一路行進到第二天，越來越接近邊境。

About midday the coach passed through a little village and a young man named Dronet saw the faces of the passengers as the coach rolled by. The young man had some years before been a soldier in Paris, and had seen King Louis XVI, and now recognized his face in the coach. He immediately mounted a horse and, taking a short-cut through the woods, reached the next village where the mayor took quick action. The road was blocked with farm-carts piled together and when the coach came it had to stop. The coach was surrounded by peasants armed with pitchforks and the royal passengers had to get out and were kept as prisoners in the village until Government troops arrived and took them on the sad return journey to Paris.

大約中午時分，馬車經過一個小村莊，一個名叫 Dronet 的年輕人在馬車駛過時看到了車內乘客的面容。這個年輕人幾年前曾在 Paris 當過兵，見過 Louis XVI 國王，此刻認出了馬車裡的那張臉。他立刻跨上馬，抄近路穿過樹林，趕到下一個村莊，那裡的村長迅速採取行動。道路被堆疊在一起的農車堵死，馬車來到時不得不停下。馬車被手持草叉的農民包圍，王室乘客被迫下車，在村中被扣為人質，直到政府軍隊抵達，帶他們踏上悲傷的回程，返回 Paris。

The story of this unsuccessful escape shows that the people of France no longer had any love for the King. And as the story of the escape became known, the French turned against the King with hatred. They regarded him as a traitor who had tried to join the enemies of France.

這次失敗的逃亡故事表明，法國人民已經不再對國王抱有任何愛戴。隨著逃亡事件傳開，法國人帶著仇恨轉而反對國王。他們把他視為試圖投靠法國敵人的叛徒。

One day a mob of twenty thousand - roused and maddened by agitators - broke into the gardens outside the Tuileries in Paris. The guards in the gardens did not know what to do and instead of driving the rabble out, let them rush on, through the gardens and into the palace.

某一天，兩萬人的暴民——被煽動者激怒和激發——闖入了 Paris Tuileries 宮外的花園。花園裡的衛兵不知所措，非但沒有驅趕暴民，反而任由他們一路衝過花園，闖進了宮殿。

But in the palace the mob faced a different kind of guard, the King's personal Swiss body-guard. These were hand-picked men, Swiss mercenaries who had sworn a solemn oath to defend the royal family. This Swiss body-guard drew their swords, ready to fight the invaders, but at that moment the King appeared, "Put back your swords," he said, "I have nothing to fear from Frenchmen."

但在宮殿裡，暴民面對的是另一種衛兵——國王的瑞士近衛隊。這些是精挑細選的瑞士傭兵，他們曾莊嚴宣誓要保衛王室。這支瑞士近衛隊拔出佩劍，準備迎戰入侵者，但就在那一刻，國王出現了。「收起你們的劍，」他說，「我無需畏懼法國人。」

Faced with the calm dignity of the King, the ruffians who had stormed in, felt ill at ease. They all wore red caps which were the sign of all fierce republicans. One of the ruffians held out his red cap to the King and the King put it on his own head - whereupon the men cheered. They asked that the Queen and her little son should also put on these "freedom-caps" - and when this was done, they left the palace and persuaded the mob outside to go home. The calmness and dignity of King Louis had prevented a battle between his guards and the mob.

面對國王沉著的尊嚴，那些闖入的暴徒感到不自在。他們都戴著紅帽——那是所有激進共和派的標誌。一個暴徒把自己的紅帽遞給國王，國王把它戴在自己頭上——眾人隨即歡呼起來。他們要求王后和她的小兒子也戴上這些「自由帽」——當這些都做完之後，他們離開了宮殿，並說服外面的暴民回家。Louis 國王的沉著與尊嚴，阻止了他的衛兵與暴民之間的一場血戰。

A young officer of the French army had watched with a friend when the mob stormed into the palace-gardens. And this young officer said; "You know, one cannon-shot would have made this crowd run." The name of the young officer was Napoleon Bonaparte; he was one day to become master of France - a master who would not worry about bloodshed as Louis XVI worried.

一位年輕的法國軍官和朋友一起目睹了暴民衝進宮殿花園的場景。這位年輕軍官說：「你知道嗎，一發砲彈就能讓這群人四散奔逃。」這位年輕軍官的名字叫 Napoleon Bonaparte；他日後將成為法國的主宰者——一個不會像 Louis XVI 那樣顧慮流血的主宰者。

This invasion of the royal palace by the mob came as a great shock to people outside France. Was it possible that a king should be treated in this fashion?

暴民入侵王宮一事，讓法國以外的人們大為震驚。一個國王竟然會被如此對待，這可能嗎？

A Prussian prince, the Duke of Brunswick, was so enraged that he sent a message to France: "If there should be any more acts of violence against king or queen, the armies of Austria and Prussia will come and make the people of France pay with their blood for the insults against royalty." If the noble Duke expected that his message would frighten the French, he was mistaken. All Frenchmen, even those who were friendly to the king and queen - felt that this was an insult to the honour of France. Did these foreigners think France was afraid of them? There was only one way to show them France was not afraid of Prussia or Austria - that was to declare war on them.

Prussia 的王子 Brunswick 公爵憤怒至極，向法國發出一則訊息：「如果再有任何針對國王或王后的暴力行為，Austria 和 Prussia 的軍隊將前來，讓法國人民用鮮血為侮辱王權付出代價。」如果這位高貴的公爵以為他的訊息會嚇倒法國人，那他就錯了。所有法國人——甚至那些對國王和王后友好的人——都覺得這是對法國榮譽的侮辱。這些外國人以為法國怕他們嗎？只有一種方式能讓他們知道法國不怕 Prussia 或 Austria——那就是向他們宣戰。

And so, France did not wait for Austria or Prussia to invade her, but declared war against them.

就這樣，法國沒有等 Austria 或 Prussia 來入侵，而是主動向他們宣戰。

But for the mob of Paris, the King and Queen were to blame for the war, it was their friends - the Emperor of Austria, the King of Prussia, the Duke of Brunswick - who had forced the war on France.

但對 Paris 的暴民來說，國王和王后才是這場戰爭的罪魁禍首——是他們的朋友——Austria 皇帝、Prussia 國王、Brunswick 公爵——把戰爭強加給了法國。

Once again the mob marched to the Tuileries, shouting for the blood of the King and Queen. This time the King was warned in time that he and his family were no longer safe in the palace, that the mob would kill without mercy. Where could he go? The only place which the ruffians would respect was the National Assembly, their parliament. And so the royal family secretly made their way to the National Assembly.

暴民再次向 Tuileries 宮進發，叫喊著要國王和王后的血。這一次，國王及時得到警告——他和家人在宮殿裡已不再安全，暴民會毫不留情地殺人。他能去哪裡？唯一一個那些暴徒會尊重的地方，就是國民議會——他們的議會。於是王室一家秘密前往國民議會。

The faithful Swiss guards had not been told that the King and Queen had left. They killed every Swiss guard. They died - obedient to their oath - without defending themselves. And the invaders rushed into the palace trampling over their bodies, looting and plundering and drinking themselves senseless with wine they found in the cellars.

忠誠的瑞士近衛隊並不知道國王和王后已經離開。暴民殺死了每一名瑞士衛兵。他們忠於誓言而死——沒有為自己辯護。入侵者踩踏著他們的屍體衝進宮殿，搶掠劫奪，用地窖裡找到的葡萄酒喝得不省人事。

If the King and Queen thought they were safe in the National Assembly, they were mistaken. In the National Assembly the enemies of the King, the Republicans now had the upper hand. They passed a law which ended the monarchy, declared France a republic and the royal family was arrested and put in a gloomy prison called "The Temple" because it had once been a castle of the Knights Templar.

如果國王和王后以為他們在國民議會裡是安全的，那他們就錯了。在國民議會中，國王的敵人——共和派——如今已佔上風。他們通過了一項法律，終結了君主制，宣布法國為共和國，王室一家被逮捕，關進了一座陰暗的監獄，名為「聖殿」——因為它曾是 Knights Templar 聖殿騎士團的城堡。

It was a King of France who had once caused the downfall of the Knights Templar, it was now a castle of the Knights Templar that saw the downfall of the last King of France.

當年，是法國國王導致了聖殿騎士團的覆滅；如今，卻是聖殿騎士團的城堡見證了法國最後一位國王的覆滅。

---

Chapter 28
Danton, Robespierre and Marat

第二十八章
Danton、Robespierre 與 Marat

In 1792 France had answered the threats of the Duke of Brunswick by declaring war on Prussia and Austria. But Prussia and Austria had long prepared for this war, they had an army of eighty thousand trained soldiers ready, as well as a twenty-thousand strong army of the French noblemen and their followers who had escaped from France and hoped to regain their possessions and privileges. This great army now invaded France, led by the sworn enemy of the French Revolution, the Duke of Brunswick.

1792 年，法國以向 Prussia 和 Austria 宣戰來回應 Brunswick 公爵的威脅。但 Prussia 和 Austria 早已為這場戰爭做好了準備，他們有八萬訓練有素的士兵待命，此外還有兩萬人的軍隊，由逃離法國的法國貴族及其追隨者組成——這些人希望奪回他們的財產和特權。這支龐大的軍隊現在入侵了法國，由法國大革命的死敵 Brunswick 公爵率領。

And France - who started the war - was not at all prepared for it. There was only a small number of trained officers and men and they could not hope to hold up the avalanche of enemy troops now rolling into France.

而法國——這場戰爭的發起者——卻完全沒有做好準備。只有少數受過訓練的軍官和士兵，他們根本無法指望阻擋如雪崩般湧入法國的敵軍。

At that moment - when it seemed that France had lost the war before it even started, when the deputies of the National Assembly who so light-heartedly declared war, trembled with fear - at this moment, one deputy took the lead and saved France. His name was Georges Jacques Danton.

就在那個時刻——看起來法國在戰爭開始之前就已經輸了，那些輕率宣戰的國民議會議員們嚇得發抖——就在這個時刻，一位議員站了出來，拯救了法國。他的名字叫 Georges Jacques Danton。

Danton was one of the great orators, a speaker whose words could move the hearts of his listeners. And his fiery speeches put new heart into his fellow deputies, they roused the national pride of all French citizens. Danton called on the French to volunteer for the army, to come and fight for the great ideals - for liberty, equality and fraternity - and the French responded to his call. They came in thousands and tens of thousands to fight for France and for these ideals.

Danton 是偉大的演說家之一，他的言辭能打動聽眾的心。他慷慨激昂的演說為同僚議員們注入了新的勇氣，喚起了所有法國公民的民族自豪感。Danton 號召法國人自願參軍，為偉大的理想——自由、平等、博愛——而戰，法國人響應了他的號召。他們成千上萬地前來，為法國和這些理想而戰。

In the city of Strasbourg, near the German frontier, a company of French officers sat one night together. In the distance they could hear the rumbling of the Prussian guns. Soon it would be their turn to meet the enemy in battle. But they were not worried, they were cheerful, laughing, joking and drinking.

在靠近德國邊界的 Strasbourg 城中，一群法國軍官某晚聚在一起。遠處傳來 Prussia 大砲的隆隆聲。很快就輪到他們在戰場上迎敵了。但他們並不擔心，他們心情愉快，有說有笑，邊喝邊聊。

One of these officers, Rouget de Lisle, was fond of music and had even composed a few songs. One of his friends turned to him saying: "We have heard some pretty songs by you, songs about spring, songs about love, but what we would like tonight is a good marching-song, a song for men who go into battle, a song for men who fight against tyrants, for freedom."

其中一位軍官 Rouget de Lisle 熱愛音樂，甚至創作過幾首歌曲。一位朋友轉向他說：「我們聽過你寫的一些好歌，有關於春天的、關於愛情的，但今晚我們想要的是一首好的行軍歌，一首給上戰場的人唱的歌，一首給為了自由而對抗暴君的人唱的歌。」

Rouget de Lisle thought for a moment and then replied: "Yes, I think I have the right tune in my mind, and some lyrics also. If you fellows will excuse me, I'll go up to my room and try and put the song on paper."

Rouget de Lisle 想了一下，然後回答：「是的，我想我腦海中有合適的旋律，也有一些歌詞。如果各位不介意，我上樓到房間去，試著把這首歌寫下來。」

The hours passed and Rouget sat in his room, trying a few bars on his fiddle, then writing them down by the flickering light of a candle, while the guns rumbled out in the darkness. At sunrise he had his song ready. He sang it to his friends - and there was a storm of applause; yes, this was the kind of song they wanted. And the next day the regiments led by these officers marched into battle with this song on their lips.

幾個小時過去了，Rouget 坐在房間裡，用小提琴試了幾個小節，然後在搖曳的燭光下寫下來，而外面黑暗中砲聲隆隆作響。日出時分，他的歌已經完成。他唱給朋友們聽——迎來了暴風雨般的掌聲；沒錯，這正是他們想要的那種歌。第二天，由這些軍官率領的部隊，嘴裡唱著這首歌走上了戰場。

Marseille is five hundred miles (800 km) from Strasbourg where the song was composed. Yet, a week later a Marseille newspaper printed the words and the music of this song. The volunteers who joined the army in Marseille liked the song so much that they made it their marching song.

Marseille 距離這首歌的創作地 Strasbourg 有五百英里（八百公里）之遙。然而一週後，Marseille 的一家報紙就刊登了這首歌的歌詞和樂譜。在 Marseille 入伍的志願兵們非常喜愛這首歌，把它定為他們的行軍歌。

The volunteers from Marseille were sent to Paris - and as they marched through the city, the people of Paris heard it for the first time. They, too, liked it, sang it and called it "the song from Marseille," the Marseillaise. And under that name this stirring song by Rouget de Lisle has remained the French national anthem to this day.

來自 Marseille 的志願兵被派往 Paris——當他們行軍穿過這座城市時，Paris 人民第一次聽到了這首歌。他們也很喜歡，跟著唱起來，並稱它為「來自 Marseille 的歌」，即《La Marseillaise》。以這個名字，Rouget de Lisle 這首激昂的歌曲至今仍是法國國歌。

It was this song which inspired the untrained volunteers who had to fight the best-trained soldiers in Europe; it was this song which filled their hearts with courage to fight the foreign invaders.

正是這首歌激勵了那些未經訓練的志願兵，他們必須面對歐洲訓練最精良的士兵；正是這首歌讓他們的心中充滿勇氣，去對抗外國入侵者。

And the Prussian and Austrian soldiers saw to their amazement that these untrained, poorly armed men - "a rabble" as they call them - marched singing into battle, they marched singing into the most deadly hail of bullets, they stormed strong positions which the Prussians thought could not be taken. Whole regiments of the French were mown down, but new regiments came to take their place and fight with a contempt for death, that the trained and drilled soldiers of Prussia and Austria had never seen before.

Prussia 和 Austria 的士兵驚訝地看到，這些未經訓練、裝備簡陋的人——他們所謂的「烏合之眾」——唱著歌走上戰場，唱著歌衝進最致命的彈雨，攻下了 Prussia 人認為不可能攻克的堅固陣地。法軍的整團整團人馬被掃倒，但新的部隊又接替上來，以一種 Prussia 和 Austria 訓練有素的士兵從未見過的視死如歸的精神繼續戰鬥。

The Prussians and Austrians were not cowards - they fought because they were ordered to fight, they obeyed orders, but they had no ideas, no beliefs to fight for. However, the untrained young men of the French army had deep and strong beliefs. They fought not only for France - but for the ideas that would enlighten the whole of humanity, for liberty, equality and fraternity. It was this spirit of the French volunteers - young men and youngsters of fifteen, sixteen - it was this spirit which, in the end, proved stronger than the well-drilled armies of the Prussians and Austrians.

Prussia 人和 Austria 人並非懦夫——他們戰鬥是因為接到命令要戰鬥，他們服從命令，但他們沒有理念、沒有信仰可以為之而戰。然而，法國軍隊中那些未經訓練的年輕人卻有著深沉而堅定的信念。他們不僅為法國而戰——更為那些將啟迪全人類的理念而戰，為自由、平等、博愛而戰。正是法國志願兵的這種精神——那些十五、十六歲的年輕人和少年——正是這種精神，最終證明比 Prussia 和 Austria 訓練有素的軍隊更加強大。

The invaders had come as far as Valmy, only a hundred and twenty miles from Paris (200 km). But at Valmy, the raw, untrained recruits of the French inflicted such a crushing defeat on the well-trained soldiers of the Duke of Brunswick, that the invaders gave up and retreated hastily to Germany. The battle of Valmy in 1792 is one of the most important battles in history - like the battle of Thermopylae, or the battle of Hastings. It was a battle which showed the world that the spirit of the French Revolution could not be crushed by force.

入侵者已經推進到 Valmy，距 Paris 僅一百二十英里（兩百公里）。但在 Valmy，法國那些生澀、未經訓練的新兵給 Brunswick 公爵訓練有素的士兵以毀滅性的打擊，入侵者放棄了進攻，倉促撤退回 Germany。1792 年的 Valmy 戰役是歷史上最重要的戰役之一——堪比 Thermopylae 之戰或 Hastings 之戰。這場戰役向世界表明，法國大革命的精神不是武力可以摧毀的。

But this same year of 1792 in which the Marseillaise was born, and in which France defeated the invaders at Valmy, also saw sad and terrible things done in the name of liberty, equality and fraternity.

然而，同在 1792 這一年——《La Marseillaise》誕生之年，法國在 Valmy 擊敗入侵者之年——也以自由、平等、博愛之名，發生了令人悲傷和可怕的事情。

When the Prussian and Austrian armies approached Paris, the fanatical Republicans in the National Assembly decided that all aristocrats still in France were dangerous, they were only waiting to help the foreign invaders, so orders were given to kill them. On four days two thousand people - who had done nothing wrong - were arrested and shot.

當 Prussia 和 Austria 的軍隊逼近 Paris 時，國民議會中狂熱的共和派決定，所有仍留在法國的貴族都是危險分子，他們只是在等待時機幫助外國入侵者，於是下令處決他們。在四天之內，兩千名無辜的人被逮捕和槍決。

In the same year one of the deputies, Dr Joseph Guillotin, who thought that the execution of the aristocrats by shooting or hanging was barbaric and messy, invented a quick and clean device. He showed his fellow deputies a little model of his invention: a broad and heavy knife-blade between two posts, released by a cord. It would cut off a head faster and surer than any axe.

同年，一位名叫 Joseph Guillotin 博士的議員認為用槍決或絞刑處決貴族過於野蠻而混亂，因此發明了一種快速而乾淨的裝置。他向同僚議員們展示了這項發明的小模型：在兩根柱子之間有一片寬大而沉重的刀刃，由一根繩索釋放。它斬首的速度和準確度超過任何斧頭。

Many deputies laughed when Dr Guillotin said: "This will cut off your head so fast you won't even feel it." Little did these laughing deputies know that many of them would find out for themselves if Dr Guillotin was right. The machine, called guillotine was accepted and became the means of execution in France.

當 Guillotin 博士說「這東西砍你的頭快到你根本感覺不到」時，許多議員笑了起來。這些大笑的議員們萬萬沒想到，他們中的許多人日後將親身驗證 Guillotin 博士說得對不對。這台被稱為「斷頭台」的機器被採納，成為法國的行刑工具。

The year 1792 was therefore a year of glory and of shame for France - the glory of Valmy and the shame of the murder of the aristocrats. The next year, 1793, could only be called the year of madness.

因此，1792 年對法國來說，既是光榮之年，也是恥辱之年——Valmy 的光榮與屠殺貴族的恥辱。而接下來的 1793 年，只能稱為瘋狂之年。

The fierce, fanatical republicans gained the upper hand in the National Assembly; they called themselves "Jacobins" because the party headquarters used to be a church hall, belonging to the Church of St Jacques. But, as you will see, these fanatical republicans, the Jacobins, cared little for churches, or religion or saints.

激進而狂熱的共和派在國民議會中佔了上風。他們自稱「Jacobins」，因為黨部曾設在一座教堂的大廳裡，那座教堂屬於 St Jacques 教堂。但正如你將看到的，這些狂熱的共和派——Jacobins——對教堂、宗教或聖人毫不在乎。

The leaders of this fanatical party were three men. One of them was Danton, the eloquent speaker who roused the pride and patriotism of the French to fight the foreign invaders. Danton was a veritable mountain of a man, large and enormously tall, with a voice like thunder. But if you saw his red face, and his great paunch, you knew that this was a man who enjoyed the pleasures of life, food and drink. If Danton had lived 150 years earlier in England he would have fitted well amongst the Cavaliers!

這個狂熱政黨的領袖有三個人。其中一位是 Danton，那位以雄辯激起法國人的自豪感和愛國心、去對抗外國入侵者的演說家。Danton 真可說是一座人山——高大魁梧，聲如洪鐘。但如果你看到他紅潤的臉龐和碩大的肚子，你就知道這是一個享受生活樂趣、好吃好喝的人。如果 Danton 早生一百五十年在 England，他一定能和保皇黨騎士們打成一片！

The second leader of the Jacobins was Maximilien Robespierre. He was the very opposite of Danton: a little man, thin, his face so pale it was almost green. He spoke with a dry rasping voice, but his mind was the most cunning in France. This pale, clever little man had no weaknesses like Danton; he never drank anything but water, and only ate the simplest food, and very little of it. Robespierre would have made an excellent Puritan - but an utterly heartless Puritan; Robespierre was a man who never loved anybody or anything in his life.

Jacobins 的第二位領袖是 Maximilien Robespierre。他與 Danton 截然相反：一個矮小、消瘦的人，臉色蒼白得幾乎發綠。他說話聲音乾澀刺耳，但他的頭腦是全法國最狡猾的。這個蒼白、聰明的小個子沒有 Danton 那樣的弱點；他除了水什麼都不喝，只吃最簡單的食物，而且吃得極少。Robespierre 本會是個優秀的清教徒——但是一個完全冷酷無情的清教徒；Robespierre 是一個一生從未愛過任何人或任何事物的人。

The third Jacobin leader was Jean-Paul Marat - who was a gifted but completely dishonest journalist. Marat was one of the first men who discovered that a newspaper has the power to influence the minds of people. A newspaper can make and shape the opinions of people - and they don't even notice that their so-called "own opinions" are only what a newspaper has put into their minds. Marat called his newspaper L'Ami du People (The People's Friend); it was a very popular newspaper and the mob of Paris swallowed every lie Marat printed, every distortion and exaggeration, as gospel truth.

Jacobins 的第三位領袖是 Jean-Paul Marat——一個有才華但完全不誠實的記者。Marat 是最早發現報紙有能力影響人們思想的人之一。報紙可以製造和塑造人們的意見——而人們甚至沒有注意到，他們所謂的「自己的觀點」不過是報紙灌輸給他們的。Marat 把自己的報紙命名為《L'Ami du People》（人民之友）；這是一份非常受歡迎的報紙，Paris 的暴民把 Marat 印出的每一個謊言、每一個歪曲和誇大，都當作福音般的真理來吞食。

These three men, Danton, Robespierre and Marat, the leaders of the Jacobins, held the fate of France in their hands, in that year of madness, 1793.

這三個人——Danton、Robespierre 和 Marat——Jacobins 的領袖，在那瘋狂的一年 1793 年，掌握著法國的命運。

---

Chapter 29
The Reign of Terror

第二十九章
恐怖統治

Each of the three men, Danton, Robespierre, Marat, the leaders of the Jacobins, the masters of France in the year of madness, 1793, was really a caricature, a distortion, of one of the great ideals of the Revolution. Danton used his eloquence to play upon the peoples' love of freedom; Robespierre used or rather misused peoples' desire for equality for his own purpose; and Marat, the "friend of the people," appealed through his writing to peoples' sense of brotherhood, of unity, but only to rouse their cruelty.

這三個人——Danton、Robespierre、Marat——Jacobins 的領袖、瘋狂之年 1793 年法國的主宰者——每一個人其實都是大革命偉大理想的一幅漫畫、一種扭曲。Danton 用他的雄辯來利用人民對自由的熱愛；Robespierre 利用——或者說濫用——人民對平等的渴望來達到他自己的目的；而 Marat，這位「人民之友」，透過他的文字訴諸人民的兄弟情誼和團結意識，但只是為了煽動他們的殘忍。

The first step in this distortion of liberté, egalité, fraternité was the disposal of the King, Louis XVI. Danton, Robespierre and Marat demanded the death of the King as a traitor to France and they received a majority of 53 (387 for, 334 against) in the National Assembly for the execution of the King.

在這場對 liberté, egalité, fraternité 的扭曲中，第一步就是處置國王 Louis XVI。Danton、Robespierre 和 Marat 要求以叛國罪處死國王，他們在國民議會中以 53 票的多數（387 票贊成，334 票反對）通過了處決國王的決議。

On January 20, 1793, fifteen thousand soldiers lined the streets through which the tumbril, the two-wheeled cart, with the King rolled to the great square where the guillotine was waiting. The entire population of Paris was in the streets; windows and even roof-tops were crowded with people.

1793 年 1 月 20 日，一萬五千名士兵沿街列隊，載著國王的囚車——一輛兩輪推車——緩緩駛向那座斷頭台等候的大廣場。Paris 全城的人都湧上了街頭；窗戶上甚至屋頂上都擠滿了人。

Louis XVI was, perhaps, too simple-minded for his task as King, but he never lacked courage and he remained calm and fearless to the last. He mounted the wooden steps of the guillotine firmly. Before he put his head under the great knife he wanted to say some final words to the people but - as happened at the execution of Charles I in England - the soldiers beat their drums to drown his voice.

Louis XVI 作為國王也許心思過於單純，但他從不缺乏勇氣，直到最後一刻仍然鎮定無懼。他穩步走上斷頭台的木階。在他將頭伸入巨大的刀刃之下前，他想對人民說幾句最後的話——但就像當年在 England 處決 Charles I 時一樣——士兵們擊鼓淹沒了他的聲音。

And then the King knelt down, laid his head under the knife, the knife dropped, the head fell into a basket, and the executioner, Sanson by name, held up the head and shouted "Vive la République". And "Vive la République" the people shouted, throwing their red caps into the air, dancing and singing round the guillotine to the tune of a new popular song: Ça ira - "This will go."

然後國王跪下，將頭放在刀刃下，刀落下，頭顱落入籃中，劊子手——名叫 Sanson——舉起頭顱高喊「Vive la République」。人群也高喊「Vive la République」，把紅帽拋向空中，圍著斷頭台載歌載舞，唱著一首新流行歌曲的曲調：Ça ira——「一切都會成的。」

Louis was not a bad king - but he paid with his life for the conceit and the stupidity of the kings before him, Louis XV, Louis XIV, right back to Catherine de Medici, who thought she could preserve the royal power by the Massacre of St Bartholomew's Night.

Louis 並不是一個壞國王——但他用生命為他之前那些國王的自負和愚蠢付出了代價，從 Louis XV、Louis XIV，一直追溯到 Catherine de Medici——她以為自己可以靠 St Bartholomew's Night 的大屠殺來保住王權。

Goddess of Reason. It was a cold day and the poor "goddess" fell ill with pneumonia the next day.

理性女神。那天天氣寒冷，這位可憐的「女神」第二天就得了肺炎。

All titles - baron, duke, lord - were abolished, even the polite Monsieur and Madame was no longer allowed. People had to call each other Citoyen and Citoyenne (citizen).

所有頭銜——男爵、公爵、勛爵——都被廢除了，甚至連禮貌的「Monsieur」和「Madame」也不再被允許使用。人們必須互稱 Citoyen 和 Citoyenne（公民）。

To wipe out even the memory of royalty, the bodies of the former kings and queens of France were taken from their tombs and thrown into quicklime so that nothing was left of them. Even playing cards had to be changed. Instead of kings, queens, knaves, there were now pictures of ladies supposed to represent liberty, equality, fraternity.

為了抹去對王權的一切記憶，歷代法國國王和王后的遺體從陵墓中被取出，丟入生石灰中，直到什麼都不剩。甚至撲克牌都必須更改。國王、王后、騎士的圖案不見了，取而代之的是據說代表自由、平等、博愛的女性圖像。

The rest of the world was shocked by the executions and by these mad laws. Britain, Austria, Spain, Italy, declared war against France. And in France itself whole provinces, cities like Lyons and Toulon, rose in rebellion against the mad fanatics in Paris.

世界其他國家對這些處決和瘋狂的法律感到震驚。Britain、Austria、Spain、Italy 向法國宣戰。而在法國國內，整個省份、像 Lyons 和 Toulon 這樣的城市，紛紛起義反抗 Paris 的瘋狂狂熱分子。

France was threatened by powerful enemies outside and by rebellions inside. In this desperate situation, the leaders, Danton, Robespierre, Marat, decide that the first task was to crush their enemies inside France. Marat wrote in his newspaper: "two hundred thousand enemies are in our midst - they must die. Two hundred thousand heads must roll to save the Republic."

法國面臨著外有強敵、內有叛亂的威脅。在這種絕望的局面下，領袖們——Danton、Robespierre、Marat——決定首要任務是鎮壓法國內部的敵人。Marat 在他的報紙上寫道：「二十萬敵人潛伏在我們中間——他們必須死。為了拯救共和國，二十萬顆人頭必須滾落。」

In the city of Caen, in Normandy, a young girl, Charlotte Corday read Marat's newspaper every day. She was a Republican with all her heart, she believed wholeheartedly in the great ideals of freedom, equality and brotherhood - but she felt that to demand the death of two hundred thousand fellow-Frenchmen was wrong, was evil. She felt that this man, Marat, was a bloodthirsty monster who must not be allowed to sway the minds of the French people.

在 Normandy 的 Caen 城中，一位年輕女子 Charlotte Corday 每天閱讀 Marat 的報紙。她全心全意是一個共和派，她由衷地相信自由、平等、博愛的偉大理想——但她覺得要求處死二十萬法國同胞是錯誤的、是邪惡的。她認為 Marat 這個人是一個嗜血的怪物，絕不能讓他繼續左右法國人民的思想。

And this young girl, who could easily have lived a happy life in her little town in Normandy, came to a terrible decision: that it was her task to rid France of this monster, Marat.

而這位年輕女子，本可以在 Normandy 的小鎮上輕鬆過著幸福的生活，卻做出了一個可怕的決定：她要承擔起使命，為法國除掉 Marat 這個怪物。

Charlotte Corday planned the deed carefully. She was known as a fervent Republican and so Marat was not surprised when he received a letter from her in which she said she had discovered a conspiracy against the government and was coming to Paris to give him a list of the wicked plotters. Having written this letter, Charlotte Corday set out for Paris.

Charlotte Corday 仔細地策劃了這個行動。她以狂熱的共和派聞名，因此當 Marat 收到她的信時並不感到意外——信中她說自己發現了一個反政府的陰謀，正要來 Paris 把那些邪惡密謀者的名單交給他。寫完這封信後，Charlotte Corday 便動身前往 Paris。

Now Marat suffered from an unpleasant skin disease and the only way in which he could find relief from the itching red spots on his body was in a hot bath. As people had no bathrooms in those days, Marat kept a small bathtub - just large enough to sit in - in his bedroom. He used to sit for hours in this little tub and even wrote his newspaper articles sitting in the bath.

Marat 患有一種令人不快的皮膚病，唯一能讓他從身上搔癢的紅斑中得到緩解的方法就是泡熱水澡。由於那個年代的人家裡沒有浴室，Marat 在臥室裡擺了一個小浴缸——剛好能坐進去。他常常在這個小浴缸裡一坐就是好幾個小時，甚至坐在浴缸裡撰寫報紙文章。

When Charlotte Corday arrived, the doorkeeper would not let her in: he told her Marat was in his bath. But the girl said: "Tell him that Charlotte Corday wants to see him. It is urgent. The safety of France is at stake."

當 Charlotte Corday 到達時，門房不肯讓她進去，告訴她 Marat 正在洗澡。但這位女子說：「告訴他 Charlotte Corday 要見他。事情很緊急。事關法國的安危。」

When Marat heard who the visitor was, he remembered her letter and said: "Well, if she does not mind seeing me in my bath, let her come in."

當 Marat 聽到訪客是誰時，他想起了她的信，說道：「好吧，如果她不介意看到我在洗澡的樣子，就讓她進來。」

When she entered, Marat peered at her through wisps of steam, rising from his bath. "Well," he said, "let us have the names of the traitors you have discovered."

當她走進去時，Marat 透過浴缸升起的蒸氣端詳著她。「好吧，」他說，「把你發現的那些叛徒的名字告訴我。」

Charlotte Corday began to dictate a list of names and while Marat was writing them down, she drew a knife from her dress and suddenly stepped forwards and plunged it into his breast. He gave one outcry and died. The cry brought people from outside, and Charlotte Corday was held and taken to prison.

Charlotte Corday 開始唸出一串名字，當 Marat 正在寫下這些名字時，她從裙中抽出一把刀，突然向前一步，將刀刺入他的胸膛。他發出一聲慘叫便死去了。這聲喊叫引來了外面的人，Charlotte Corday 被抓住並送進了監獄。

At her trial she said, "I killed Marat because men of his kind are the true enemies of freedom." And she calmly went to the guillotine.

在審判中她說：「我殺了 Marat，因為像他這樣的人才是自由真正的敵人。」然後她平靜地走向斷頭台。

The assassination of Marat frightened and infuriated the Jacobin leaders, Danton and Robespierre. Danton held speeches in which he roared: "Death to all aristocrats, death to anyone who shows by a single word he is not wholeheartedly Republican!" And Robespierre would speak in his monotonous, rasping voice for two hours of the duties of a good citizen, and then end by reading a list of a few hundred names: people who were not good citizens and who therefore, much to his regret, had to be sentenced to death.

Marat 的遇刺使 Jacobin 領袖 Danton 和 Robespierre 既驚恐又憤怒。Danton 發表了咆哮般的演說：「處死所有貴族，處死任何以一個字表明自己不是全心全意共和派的人！」而 Robespierre 則用他單調刺耳的嗓音，花兩個小時講述一個好公民的職責，然後以宣讀幾百個人名的名單作結：這些人不是好公民，因此——他深表遺憾地說——必須被判處死刑。

The time from 1793 to 1794 is called the "Reign of Terror," the time when Marat's wish was fulfilled and hundreds of thousands of heads rolled.

從 1793 年到 1794 年的這段時期被稱為「恐怖統治」——Marat 的願望實現了，成千上萬顆人頭滾落的時代。

First all the remaining aristocrats were killed - even those who were Republicans and Jacobins - it was enough that they had been born with a title.

首先，所有剩餘的貴族都被處死了——即便是那些身為共和派和 Jacobins 的貴族也不能倖免——光是他們生來帶有貴族頭銜就足夠了。

Then came the people who had expressed sympathy or pity for the King; they too had to die. A wrong word could cost a man his life.

接著輪到那些曾對國王表示同情或憐憫的人；他們也必須死。一句說錯的話就可能要了一個人的命。

A soldier who got drunk and shouted: "France is a great country whether she is a republic or a monarchy," was arrested and his head rolled.

一個喝醉了的士兵高喊：「法國是偉大的國家，不管她是共和國還是君主國。」他被逮捕了，人頭落地。

Then came all the deputies who had once voted against the death sentence for Louis XVI. Faithful republicans though they were, they had shown sympathy for the King, and now they had to die. They went to their death singing the Marseillaise.

接著輪到了所有曾投票反對處死 Louis XVI 的議員。儘管他們是忠實的共和派，卻因為曾對國王表示同情而必須赴死。他們唱著《La Marseillaise》走向死亡。

And the priests, monks and nuns of the closed churches and monasteries, were seen as enemies of the Republic. They, too, were led to the guillotine.

被關閉的教堂和修道院中的神父、修士和修女，被視為共和國的敵人。他們也被押上了斷頭台。

By then Danton, the great Danton, became sick of the bloodshed. He appealed to his fellow deputies to stop the executions. But Robespierre had been waiting for this. He accused Danton and his friends of being traitors, and Danton was sentenced to death and his head rolled.

到了此時，Danton——偉大的 Danton——已經厭倦了這場殺戮。他呼籲同僚議員們停止處決。但 Robespierre 一直在等待這一刻。他指控 Danton 和他的朋友們是叛徒，Danton 被判處死刑，人頭落地。

Now Robespierre, the Puritan, was master of France. He was a great believer in equality. To have better brains than other people was a crime

如今 Robespierre——這個清教徒——成了法國的主宰。他是平等的忠實信徒。擁有比別人更聰明的頭腦就是一種罪行

---

Chapter 30
Napoleon

第三十章
Napoleon

Robespierre was certainly a heartless monster, but in his own crazy way he had been sincere in his belief that he was doing his best for France. He himself was convinced that he was a selfless servant of France. The men who had brought about his downfall - a lawyer named Paul Barras and his friends - were not in any sense selfless. They had only stopped the "Reign of Terror" because they feared for their own lives, and once they were in power and installed as the "Directorate," they used their position to make themselves rich.

Robespierre 無疑是個冷酷無情的怪物，但以他自己瘋狂的方式，他確實真誠地相信自己在為法國盡最大的努力。他自己深信不疑，認為自己是法國無私的僕人。那些導致他倒台的人——一個名叫 Paul Barras 的律師和他的朋友們——在任何意義上都談不上無私。他們之所以終結「恐怖統治」，只是因為擔心自己的性命；一旦掌權並以「督政府」之名就位，他們就利用職位為自己謀取財富。

And things looked quite promising for these "directors" of France. The rebellions in the provinces, in Lyons, in Toulon, had been crushed by the French army, killing many thousands of rebels, so the directors had no fear of any more upheavals in the provinces. In Paris they had disposed of Robespierre and also of a number of other fanatical Jacobins, so they need not fear any enemies from this quarter. And the outside enemies - Britain, Italy, Austria - were in no hurry to invade France, with the Battle of Valmy fresh in their minds.

事情看起來對這些法國的「督政官」頗為樂觀。各省的叛亂——在 Lyons、在 Toulon——都已被法國軍隊鎮壓，殺死了數千名叛軍，所以督政官們不必擔心各省再有動亂。在 Paris，他們除掉了 Robespierre 以及其他一些狂熱的 Jacobins，因此也不必擔心來自這方面的敵人。而外部敵人—— Britain、Italy、Austria——由於 Valmy 戰役的記憶猶新，並不急於入侵法國。

All seemed good for Barras and his fellow directors; good, that was, for the pleasant task of amassing a fortune. But things did not work out so well. The year 1795 again brought a poor harvest and a long, hard winter; food became scarce and the price of flour increased, and the poor could no longer pay for bread. And then the people of Paris did what they had done before - they rioted.

對 Barras 和他的督政官同僚們來說，一切似乎都很順利——順利到可以愉快地大撈一筆。但事情並沒有發展得這麼好。1795 年又遇上了歉收和漫長而嚴酷的冬天；食物變得稀缺，麵粉價格上漲，窮人再也買不起麵包。於是 Paris 的人民做了他們從前做過的事——暴動。

But the "directors" of France were not going to allow any riots in Paris. And Barras and his friends thought of a very capable young general who had already shown that he could deal with rebellious crowds: he had crushed the rebellion in Toulon. And so Barras sent for this promising young general and gave him the task of disbanding the mob. The name of this young general was Napoleon Bonaparte.

但法國的「督政官」們不打算容許 Paris 發生任何暴動。Barras 和他的朋友們想到了一位非常能幹的年輕將軍，他已經證明了自己有能力對付叛亂的群眾：他曾鎮壓了 Toulon 的叛亂。於是 Barras 把這位前途無量的年輕將軍召來，交給他驅散暴民的任務。這位年輕將軍的名字叫 Napoleon Bonaparte。

General Bonaparte brought peace and order to Paris in his own way. His troops marched at night into Paris and surrounded the gardens of the Tuileries with forty cannons.

Bonaparte 將軍以他自己的方式為 Paris 帶來了和平與秩序。他的部隊在夜間開進 Paris，用四十門大砲包圍了 Tuileries 宮的花園。

Next morning the rioters were out again, streaming from the poor suburbs of Paris to the centre, to the Tuileries, crowding the gardens and shouting: "Bread, bread, give us bread!" When the yelling crowd approached the soldiers General Bonaparte shouted a warning to the people in front. But they only laughed. Who would dare shoot at the people of Paris? And in any case they were not going to take orders from this little man, so they came nearer. When they advanced further, Bonaparte shouted "Fire." The cannons wreaked havoc on the packed mass of people; hundreds were killed by one volley and the rest fled in terror.

第二天早上，暴動者再次出動，從 Paris 的貧民區湧向市中心、湧向 Tuileries，擠滿花園，高喊：「麵包！麵包！給我們麵包！」當叫喊的人群逼近士兵時，Bonaparte 將軍向前方的人群發出了警告。但他們只是嘲笑。誰敢向 Paris 人民開槍？何況他們才不會聽從這個矮個子的命令，於是繼續靠近。當他們進一步推進時，Bonaparte 喊道「開火。」大砲在擁擠的人群中造成了大屠殺；一輪齊射就有數百人喪命，其餘的人驚恐地四散逃竄。

General Bonaparte was the same man who, as an officer, had seen the mob invade the Tuileries and who had said to a friend: "One cannon-shot would make them run." He had remembered his words and had acted accordingly. And that was how he brought order to Paris.

Bonaparte 將軍就是當年身為軍官時目睹暴民入侵 Tuileries 宮、並對朋友說「一發砲彈就能讓他們跑」的那個人。他記住了自己的話，並付諸行動。這就是他為 Paris 帶來秩序的方式。

Barras and his fellow directors thanked General Bonaparte, but thought it would be wise to get this ruthless and ambitious young man away from Paris and away from France. So they put him in command of the French troops that had invaded Italy, and it was in Italy that Bonaparte first proved himself as one of the greatest generals in history.

Barras 和他的督政官同僚們感謝了 Bonaparte 將軍，但覺得明智之舉是把這個冷酷而野心勃勃的年輕人送離 Paris、送離法國。於是他們讓他指揮已入侵 Italy 的法國軍隊，而正是在 Italy，Bonaparte 首次證明了自己是歷史上最偉大的將領之一。

Napoleon Bonaparte was born on the island of Corsica in the Mediterranean. The people of Corsica are actually Italian and their language is an Italian dialect, but France had bought the island from Italy and so Corsica had come under the rule of France. Napoleon was born on this island in 1769, when Louis XV and Madame de Pompadour were still ruling France. The Bonaparte family was large - Napoleon had four brothers and three sisters. The father, a lawyer, was only too glad when the French Governor of Corsica offered a "scholarship" for one of his sons - he would be given a free education at a military academy in France where boys were educated and trained to become officers in the French army. The father was relieved to not have to worry about the education of one of his eight children, and so young Napoleon was sent to this boarding school, the Military Academy.

Napoleon Bonaparte 出生在地中海上的 Corsica 島。Corsica 人其實是 Italy 人，他們的語言是一種 Italy 方言，但法國從 Italy 手中買下了這座島嶼，因此 Corsica 就歸屬了法國。Napoleon 於 1769 年出生在這座島上，當時 Louis XV 和 Pompadour 夫人仍在統治法國。Bonaparte 家是個大家庭——Napoleon 有四個兄弟和三個姊妹。他的父親是一名律師，當 Corsica 的法國總督提出為他的一個兒子提供「獎學金」時，他求之不得——這個兒子將在法國的一所軍事學院免費接受教育，那裡的男孩們被培養和訓練成為法國軍隊的軍官。父親很慶幸不必再為八個孩子中的一個操心教育問題，於是年幼的 Napoleon 就被送進了這所寄宿學校——軍事學院。

Napoleon had a tough time at this school. The other boys teased him because he spoke French with an Italian accent and he made no friends amongst them. But this pale boy from Corsica did not seem to need any friends, he seemed quite content to be alone with his thoughts, and, through time the other boys learned to respect him. When there was snow, the boys used to split up into two teams fighting each other with snow-balls. But the team in which this Corsican boy always ended up, took him as their commander and leader - even older boys simply accepted him as leader - and his team always won.

Napoleon 在這所學校裡日子很不好過。其他男孩取笑他講法語帶著 Italy 口音，他在他們中間交不到朋友。但這個來自 Corsica 的蒼白男孩似乎不需要任何朋友，他似乎很滿足於獨處和自己的思緒為伴。隨著時間推移，其他男孩學會了尊重他。下雪時，男孩們通常會分成兩隊打雪仗。而這個 Corsica 男孩所在的那一隊，總是推他當指揮官和領袖——甚至比他年長的男孩也理所當然地接受他做領袖——而他的隊伍總是贏。

Napoleon Bonaparte finished school and became a lieutenant. But even as an officer he had no close friends. The other officers came from noble and rich families and had plenty of money from home besides their army pay. Bonaparte only had his army pay which was not much and the young aristocrats tended to look down on the lieutenant because he was not of their own class. But Napoleon Bonaparte was reading the books of enlightenment; he read about the natural rights of man, he heard of the great ideas of freedom, equality and brotherhood and he dreamed of a time when a man's own ability rather than privileges of birth would decide his career in life. And he was sure of his own abilities - he was sure he was destined for greatness.

Napoleon Bonaparte 完成學業，成為一名中尉。但即使身為軍官，他也沒有親密的朋友。其他軍官出身貴族和富裕家庭，除了軍餉之外還有大量的家庭匯款。Bonaparte 只有微薄的軍餉，年輕的貴族們傾向於看不起這位中尉，因為他不屬於他們的階級。但 Napoleon Bonaparte 正在閱讀啟蒙書籍；他讀到了關於人的天賦權利，聽聞了自由、平等、博愛的偉大思想，他夢想著有一天，一個人的才能——而非出身的特權——將決定他的人生道路。他對自己的才能充滿信心——他確信自己注定要成就偉業。

When the Revolution came, Lieutenant Bonaparte was not interested in the fate of the unhappy King Louis XVI, he was not interested in the Republican Government - in men like Danton, Robespierre, Marat - for Bonaparte realized that these men were only distorting the ideals of liberty, equality and fraternity. But, at least, this Republican Government did away with the old privileges and this would give him a chance for advancement, for promotion which the old regime would not have given him. That is why Bonaparte served the Republican Government faithfully, and bombarded the rebels of Toulon.

當革命來臨時，Bonaparte 中尉對不幸的 Louis XVI 國王的命運毫無興趣，他對共和政府也不感興趣——對 Danton、Robespierre、Marat 這些人也不感興趣——因為 Bonaparte 意識到這些人不過是在扭曲自由、平等、博愛的理想。但至少，這個共和政府廢除了舊的特權，這將給他晉升和提拔的機會——這是舊制度不會給予他的。正因如此，Bonaparte 忠實地服務於共和政府，砲轟了 Toulon 的叛軍。

As a reward he had a rapid promotion and was already a general when Barras called him to Paris to quell the riots. For General Bonaparte this was only another step on the ladder to greatness and fame and, as you have heard, he quelled the riots with one shot from his cannons. His reward was to be given command of the troops fighting in Italy.

作為獎賞，他迅速晉升，當 Barras 召他到 Paris 平息暴動時，他已經是一名將軍了。對 Bonaparte 將軍來說，這不過是通往偉大和榮耀的階梯上的又一步——如你所知，他用一輪砲火就平息了暴動。他的獎賞是被任命指揮在 Italy 作戰的軍隊。

By that time Napoleon had married a widow, Josephine Beauharnais. And when he left his wife he said: "My sword is at my side and with it I shall go far."

那時 Napoleon 已經娶了一位寡婦 Josephine Beauharnais。當他離開妻子時，他說：「我的劍在我身旁，帶著它我將走得很遠。」

In the year 1795, France was at war with Britain, Prussia, Austria, Spain, Italy. What chance did she have to win against all these enemies? None at all - had it not been for this man from Corsica, Napoleon Bonaparte.

1795 年，法國同時與 Britain、Prussia、Austria、Spain、Italy 交戰。她有什麼機會打贏所有這些敵人呢？完全沒有——如果不是因為這個來自 Corsica 的人，Napoleon Bonaparte。

The French troops in Italy were poorly equipped, badly clothed and in poor spirit. But with his mere presence Bonaparte created a new spirit amongst them. They initially defeated an Italian army - and then came up against a great army the Austrians had sent into Italy. The battle against the Austrians took place in November 1796, near a village called Arcole in northern Italy.

在 Italy 的法軍裝備簡陋、衣衫襤褸、士氣低落。但 Bonaparte 僅憑他的到來就在他們之中創造了一種新的精神。他們首先擊敗了一支 Italy 軍隊——然後遭遇了 Austria 派往 Italy 的一支龐大軍隊。與 Austria 軍隊的戰鬥發生在 1796 年 11 月，地點在 Italy 北部一個叫 Arcole 的村莊附近。

The Austrians were on the other side of the River Alpone and the French could only get at them by crossing a bridge. But the Austrians had trained their cannons on the bridge and every time the French came upon the bridge they were mown down by the Austrian guns.

Austria 軍隊在 Alpone 河的對岸，法軍只能通過一座橋才能到達他們那邊。但 Austria 人已將大砲對準了這座橋，每當法軍踏上橋面，就被 Austria 的砲火掃倒。

Three times the French advanced on the bridge - and then retreated under a hail of fire from the Austrians, leaving their dead and wounded behind. Then General Bonaparte himself took the French flag, and shouting "Follow me," ran onto the bridge, and his faithful soldiers followed him. They reached the middle of the bridge, but now the cannon fire was so heavy that the soldiers turned back. In the confusion Bonaparte fell from the bridge into the mud and swamp below and Austrian soldiers came running towards him. The French soldiers saw it, and with the shout, "Forward, save the General!" they stormed across the bridge, drove the Austrians away and, at the end of the day, had gained a decisive victory.

法軍三次衝上橋面——然後在 Austria 人的火力傾瀉下撤退，留下了他們的死傷者。這時 Bonaparte 將軍親自拿起法國軍旗，高喊「跟我來！」衝上了橋面，忠誠的士兵們緊隨其後。他們衝到了橋的中央，但此時砲火實在太猛烈，士兵們又退了回去。在混亂中，Bonaparte 從橋上跌入下方的泥沼中，Austria 士兵朝他跑來。法國士兵們看到了這一幕，高呼「前進！救將軍！」他們強渡過橋，趕走了 Austria 人，在這一天結束時，取得了決定性的勝利。

Within a short time the whole of Italy was in the hands of General Bonaparte and the people of Paris received him in triumph. The shooting in the Tuileries Gardens was forgotten - he was their beloved hero.

不久之後，整個 Italy 都落入了 Bonaparte 將軍的手中，Paris 人民以凱旋的姿態迎接他。Tuileries 花園的屠殺已被遺忘——他是他們深愛的英雄。

---

Chapter 31
Egypt

第三十一章
埃及

Napoleon Bonaparte was not tall; he was short and stout and his soldiers used to speak of him affectionately as "our little corporal." But in this little, stout man there lived an iron will, a drive and energy which made all the taller people feel dwarfed in his presence.

Napoleon Bonaparte 個子不高；他矮胖結實，士兵們常常親切地稱他為「我們的小伍長」。但在這個矮胖的人體內住著鋼鐵般的意志、一股驅動力和精力，讓所有比他高大的人在他面前都自覺渺小。

And this little man was, indeed, a giant in his mental capacities. He was, first of all, a giant for work - he could dictate five letters at the same time. For most of his life he never slept more than three hours a day. The planning and preparing of battles and whole campaigns, the discussions with his officers, the inspections of troops, these were only a part of his work. When he had conquered a region he laid down the rules of government, the laws for this region and these rules and laws were in the spirit of the French Revolution: equality of justice, equal opportunities for all.

而這個小個子的心智能力確實是巨人級的。首先，他是工作的巨人——他能同時口述五封信。在他生命中的大部分時間裡，他每天的睡眠從未超過三小時。規劃和準備戰役以及整個戰局、與軍官們討論、檢閱部隊——這些只是他工作的一部分。當他征服了一個地區，他就為這個地區制定治理規則和法律，而這些規則和法律是秉持法國大革命的精神：司法平等、人人機會均等。

He was not only a giant in the amount of work he got done in a day, he was also a giant in his plans for the future. His great dream, his great ambition was to unite all the nations of Europe in one great nation. He wanted to do away with the dozens of nationalities and kingdoms of Europe which were for ever bickering and warring amongst themselves. But as they showed no inclination to join together of their own free will, they should be made to come together - and he was the man to make them into one nation.

他不僅在每天完成的工作量上是巨人，在他對未來的規劃上也是巨人。他的偉大夢想、他的宏大野心，是將歐洲所有的國家統一為一個偉大的國家。他想消除歐洲那幾十個永遠在彼此爭吵和交戰的民族和王國。但既然它們沒有自願聯合的傾向，那就應該被迫走到一起——而他就是那個要把它們合併為一個國家的人。

He was also a giant in the way he impressed people. From his pale face there blazed a pair of black eyes which had a magnetic power. If he looked at you in anger, you felt as if you were struck by lightning, but if he looked at you with praise and approval you felt your soul lifted with joy.

他給人留下深刻印象的方式也是巨人級的。在他蒼白的臉龐上，閃耀著一對具有磁性力量的黑色眼睛。如果他憤怒地看著你，你會覺得自己像被閃電擊中；但如果他以讚許和認可的目光看著你，你會感到靈魂因喜悅而升騰。

His soldiers - from the lowest private to the highest officer - not only loved him, they almost worshipped him. He was a kind of god for them. He could demand any hardship, any sacrifice from them and they were happy to serve him, to march for him, to fight for him, and even to die for him.

他的士兵們——從最低等的列兵到最高階的軍官——不僅愛戴他，幾乎是崇拜他。對他們來說，他就是某種神。他可以要求他們承受任何艱苦、做出任何犧牲，而他們都樂於為他效勞、為他行軍、為他戰鬥，甚至為他赴死。

It may sound quite incredible to us, but on one occasion when he gave a regiment the order to wade into a river and cross to the other side, many men were swept away by the strong current and drowned, but the drowning men cried, "Long live Napoleon," with their last breath.

這聽起來可能令人難以置信，但有一次他命令一個團涉水過河到對岸，許多人被湍急的水流沖走溺水身亡，而那些溺水的人用最後一口氣喊道：「Napoleon 萬歲。」

He was like a higher being, a superhuman being to his soldiers, and even other people in his presence felt as if a more than human force had taken possession of the body of this man and worked through him. It was not a truly divine force, like the one that guided humble Joan of Arc, neither was it an evil, devilish force, like the one which drove the monster, Robespierre; it was like a force of nature, a thunderstorm, or a hurricane. It was certainly not like the forces of an ordinary human being.

對他的士兵們來說，他就像一個高等的存在、一個超人般的存在，甚至其他人在他面前也會感覺到，彷彿有一股超越人類的力量佔據了這個人的身體，並通過他運作。這不是真正的神聖力量——不像引導謙卑的 Joan of Arc 的那種力量；也不是邪惡的、魔鬼般的力量——不像驅使怪物 Robespierre 的那種力量；它更像一股自然的力量，一場雷暴，或一場颶風。它絕對不是一個普通人所具有的力量。

General Bonaparte's victory in Italy came as a shock and surprise to the enemies of France. Austria quickly asked for peace, and so did Prussia and Spain. Only one country was not shaken and continued the war, and that was Britain. But this was only a war at sea, a war between ships, and was no real danger to France.

Bonaparte 將軍在 Italy 的勝利讓法國的敵人們大感震驚和意外。Austria 迅速求和，Prussia 和 Spain 也是如此。只有一個國家不為所動，繼續戰爭，那就是 Britain。但這只是一場海上的戰爭、船艦之間的戰爭，對法國並無真正的威脅。

For the French people, General Napoleon Bonaparte had with one stroke brought peace and glory to France and he was their beloved hero.

對法國人民來說，Napoleon Bonaparte 將軍一舉為法國帶來了和平與榮耀，他是他們深愛的英雄。

The Directorate, Barras and his fellow directors, were not very happy about the popularity of General Bonaparte. He was loved by the people, loved by the soldiers, he was ambitious - he might well have ideas about making himself master of France. And so the Directors of France were well pleased when Napoleon Bonaparte himself came to them with a proposal that would take him away from France for a long time.

督政府的 Barras 和他的督政官同僚們對 Bonaparte 將軍的人氣並不太高興。他受人民愛戴、受士兵擁護、又野心勃勃——他很可能有讓自己成為法國主宰者的想法。因此，當 Napoleon Bonaparte 自己帶著一個將讓他長期遠離法國的提案來找他們時，法國的督政官們甚為滿意。

By this time Britain had established a large colony in Asia - the great subcontinent of India had come under British rule. France did not have enough ships to attack India by sea, but India could also be reached by land. Had Alexander the Great not done that?

那時 Britain 已在亞洲建立了龐大的殖民地——偉大的 India 次大陸已落入英國統治之下。法國沒有足夠的船艦從海上進攻 India，但 India 也可以從陸路到達。Alexander the Great 不就是那樣做的嗎？

What General Bonaparte proposed was this: he would first conquer Egypt, and then he would go on to conquer Turkey and Persia and march through into India and take it from the British.

Bonaparte 將軍的提議是這樣的：他先征服 Egypt，然後繼續征服 Turkey 和 Persia，再進軍 India，從英國人手中奪取它。

It was a madly ambitious idea. Even a modern army with tanks and aeroplanes could hardly cope with such a task. But the Directors agreed because it would, at least, keep this dangerous man away from France, a long way away.

這是一個瘋狂而野心勃勃的計畫。即使是擁有坦克和飛機的現代軍隊也很難完成這樣的任務。但督政官們同意了，因為這至少能讓這個危險人物遠離法國，而且是非常遙遠。

And so, in 1798, Napoleon sailed from Toulon with a large fleet, carrying an army of forty thousand soldiers. With this army there came a second little army of scientists, artists, archaeologists. They hoped to make valuable discoveries in the lands of the East.

就這樣，1798 年，Napoleon 率領一支龐大的艦隊從 Toulon 出航，載著四萬名士兵的大軍。伴隨這支軍隊的還有另一支小小的「軍隊」——由科學家、藝術家和考古學家組成。他們希望在東方的土地上做出珍貴的發現。

As a matter of fact, at least one great discovery was made on this fantastic expedition. The writing of ancient Egypt, the hieroglyphs, could not be read by anybody in the world. The knowledge of what these pictures meant had completely disappeared. But on this expedition the French scholars discovered a stone in Egypt, the famous Rosetta Stone on which the names of kings and queens was written in Greek letters as well as in hieroglyphs. The discovery of the Rosetta Stone made it possible to decipher all the writing of ancient Egypt. This Rosetta Stone is now in the British Museum in London.

事實上，這次不可思議的遠征中至少有一項偉大的發現。古 Egypt 的文字——象形文字——世界上沒有任何人能夠閱讀。關於這些圖形符號的含義的知識已經完全消失。但在這次遠征中，法國學者們在 Egypt 發現了一塊石碑——著名的 Rosetta Stone——上面用希臘文字和象形文字寫著國王和王后的名字。Rosetta Stone 的發現使破譯古 Egypt 所有文字成為可能。這塊 Rosetta Stone 現在收藏在 London 的 British Museum。

But this important discovery came much later. To begin with, the French fleet with all the soldiers aboard might easily not have reached Egypt at all, because a great British fleet was in the Mediterranean on the lookout for the French and ready to send them to the bottom of the sea. This British fleet was under the command of Horatio Nelson who became the most famous of British naval heroes.

但這項重要的發現是後來才實現的。首先，這支載著所有士兵的法國艦隊很可能根本到不了 Egypt，因為一支強大的英國艦隊正在地中海上搜尋法國人，隨時準備把他們送入海底。這支英國艦隊由 Horatio Nelson 指揮——他後來成為最著名的英國海軍英雄。

On this occasion, luck was with Napoleon and his fleet. The British never caught sight of the French ships which landed safely, without meeting any resistance, on the Egyptian coast not far from Alexandria.

在這次出征中，幸運站在了 Napoleon 和他的艦隊這邊。英國人始終沒有發現法國艦隊，法軍安全地、未遭遇任何抵抗地登陸了 Egypt 海岸，就在 Alexandria 不遠處。

At that time Egypt was not an independent country but was under Turkish dominion as part of the Ottoman Empire. The Turks, however, were completely taken by surprise by the invasion, and so Napoleon not only landed his troops but occupied the city of Alexandria without encountering Turkish soldiers. From Alexandria Napoleon marched his army towards the capital of Egypt, towards Cairo.

那時 Egypt 並非一個獨立國家，而是作為 Ottoman Empire 的一部分，處於土耳其的統治之下。然而土耳其人完全被這次入侵打了個措手不及，因此 Napoleon 不僅成功登陸了軍隊，還在未遭遇土耳其士兵的情況下佔領了 Alexandria 城。從 Alexandria，Napoleon 率軍向 Egypt 的首都 Cairo 進發。

They reached Gizah on the outskirts of Cairo, and there they saw the Pyramids and the Sphinx. But there they saw also a great Turkish army rapidly approaching. This was to be the decisive battle for Egypt. Napoleon addressed his soldiers before the battle and in his speech he said, "Soldiers of France, you are going to fight in front of the Pyramids. Four thousand years of history look down on you from these monuments. Be worthy of this great occasion." And the Battle of the Pyramids ended with a great French victory.

他們到達了 Cairo 郊外的 Gizah，在那裡他們看到了金字塔和人面獅身像。但他們也看到一支龐大的土耳其軍隊正在迅速逼近。這將是決定 Egypt 命運的戰役。Napoleon 在戰前向他的士兵們發表了講話，他說：「法國的士兵們，你們即將在金字塔前作戰。四千年的歷史從這些紀念碑上俯視著你們。要無愧於這個偉大的時刻。」金字塔之戰以法軍的一場大勝告終。

After this victory Napoleon ordered the ships of his fleet to remain at anchor at a port called Aboukir while he and the army marched on to strike against Turkey. But while they were on the march the British fleet under Nelson - at long last - found the French ships. Nelson sailed his fleet to the port of Aboukir and, in a overnight battle that lasted eighteen hours, the French ships were destroyed and sunk. This event of August 1-2, 1798 became known as the Battle of the Nile.

在這場勝利之後，Napoleon 命令他的艦隊停泊在一個名叫 Aboukir 的港口，而他和軍隊繼續進軍攻打 Turkey。但在行軍途中，Nelson 率領的英國艦隊——終於——找到了法國艦船。Nelson 率艦隊駛入 Aboukir 港，在一場持續十八個小時的通宵激戰中，法國艦船被摧毀和擊沉。1798 年 8 月 1 日至 2 日的這場事件，後來被稱為 Nile 河之戰。

When the news of the loss of his fleet reached Napoleon he realized that without ships his great plan was doomed. He would need supplies, he would need more troops, and he could not get them without a fleet. He left his army in Egypt and sailed back to France in a little vessel that had been left. And he was once again lucky because this little ship was not caught by the British and arrived safely in France.

當艦隊覆滅的消息傳到 Napoleon 那裡，他意識到沒有船艦，他的宏大計畫注定要失敗。他需要補給、需要更多的軍隊，而沒有艦隊就無法得到這些。他把軍隊留在 Egypt，乘坐一艘殘留的小船返回法國。他再次幸運——這艘小船沒有被英國人截獲，安全抵達了法國。

The poor soldiers left behind in Egypt, were later defeated by the British, taken prisoner and, eventually, sent back to France. The British had spoiled Napoleon's great plan to imitate Alexander the Great. It was Nelson who had spoiled it. The Rosetta Stone, which the French had discovered, was part of the booty the British took from the French troops in Egypt, and that is why the stone is not in Paris but in London.

留在 Egypt 的可憐士兵們後來被英軍打敗、俘虜，最終被送回法國。英國人破壞了 Napoleon 效法 Alexander the Great 的宏偉計畫。正是 Nelson 破壞了這個計畫。法國人發現的 Rosetta Stone 成了英國人從 Egypt 法軍手中繳獲的戰利品的一部分，這就是為什麼這塊石碑不在 Paris 而在 London 的原因。

You might think the French people gave Napoleon a poor welcome after the disaster of this expedition. Far from it; they cheered him as if he had conquered India, and they were pleased to have him back. In his absence Austria had again declared war on France, and the war was going badly for the French. Napoleon Bonaparte was the only man who could turn defeat into victory.

你可能以為法國人民在這次遠征的慘敗之後會冷淡地對待 Napoleon。但恰恰相反——他們為他歡呼，彷彿他征服了 India，他們很高興他回來了。在他不在的期間，Austria 再次向法國宣戰，而戰事對法國極為不利。Napoleon Bonaparte 是唯一能夠轉敗為勝的人。

---

Chapter 32
Emperor Napoleon and Trafalgar

第三十二章
Napoleon 皇帝與 Trafalgar 海戰

The French people welcomed Napoleon on his return from Egypt because they hoped he would save them from the Austrian armies. But there was also another reason. The Directorate, Barras and his friends, had never been very popular and their policy of using government mainly to make themselves rich had not endeared them to the people. Many in France said quite openly they would sooner be ruled by Bonaparte than by these men who only wanted to fill their own pockets. In addition the Army, the French soldiers, admired Napoleon and despised the Directors.

法國人民在 Napoleon 從 Egypt 回來時歡迎他，因為他們希望他能拯救他們免受 Austria 軍隊的侵害。但還有另一個原因。督政府的 Barras 和他的朋友們從來就不怎麼受歡迎，他們利用政府為自己撈錢的政策並沒有讓人民喜愛。許多法國人公開表示，他們寧願被 Bonaparte 統治，也不願被這些只想中飽私囊的人統治。此外，軍隊——法國的士兵們——敬仰 Napoleon，鄙視那些督政官。

Bonaparte himself was always keenly aware of public opinion, and as things were going in his favour, he was not a man to miss an opportunity. One day in November 1799, he strode into a meeting of the French deputies (Members of Parliament), told them that the Directorate was finished and that he would take over the government under the title "First Consul" - a title the ancient Romans had used when Rome was still a republic.

Bonaparte 本人對公眾輿論向來極為敏銳，而既然形勢對他有利，他可不是會錯失良機的人。1799 年 11 月的某一天，他大步走進法國議員（國會議員）的會議，告訴他們督政府已經完蛋了，他將以「第一執政」的頭銜接管政府——這是古 Rome 人在 Rome 還是共和國時使用的頭銜。

The deputies objected; they shouted at him; they called him a "dictator." Napoleon walked out of the hall where a company of his soldiers was waiting. "Send this rabble away!" he said. And with the cry, "Long live Napoleon," the soldiers stormed in and a few minutes later the hall was cleared. France had a new government: the Consul Napoleon Bonaparte.

議員們反對；他們對他大喊大叫；他們稱他為「獨裁者」。Napoleon 走出大廳，那裡有一隊他的士兵等候著。「把這幫烏合之眾趕走！」他說。士兵們高喊「Napoleon 萬歲！」衝了進去，幾分鐘後大廳就被清空了。法國有了新政府：執政官 Napoleon Bonaparte。

The first task of the new Consul was to deal with the Austrian threat. After the Battle of Arcole (when he stormed over the bridge) Napoleon had conquered Italy. But while he was away in Egypt, the Austrians had reoccupied Northern Italy so he had to drive them out again. However, by this time it was January, deep winter, and no general in his senses would move an army through ice and snow, at least that's what the Austrians thought; they expected Napoleon to come and attack them in spring.

新任執政官的首要任務是對付 Austria 的威脅。在 Arcole 戰役（他強渡橋樑的那次）之後，Napoleon 已經征服了 Italy。但在他遠征 Egypt 期間，Austria 人重新佔領了 Italy 北部，所以他必須再次驅逐他們。然而，此時已是一月，隆冬時節，任何神志正常的將軍都不會在冰天雪地中行軍——至少 Austria 人是這麼想的；他們預期 Napoleon 會在春天來進攻他們。

But Napoleon had different ideas - he remembered a great general who had once invaded Italy from the north by coming over the Alps: Hannibal. Napoleon was going to do what Hannibal had done; he had no elephants, but he did cross the Alps with his army in the depth of winter. The army had heavy cannons which had to be pulled up steep slopes, but the soldiers made great sledges of pinewood and on these sledges they heaved and pulled the guns up through the deep snow. At some places there was not even a path, only a ledge so narrow that a false step, a slip in the snow would send a man crashing down to his death. Yet, along the narrow ledges and clinging to cliffs the soldiers toiled and pulled, and when they felt exhausted and at the end of their strength, they only had to see their general to feel new courage and strength.

但 Napoleon 有不同的想法——他記得一位偉大的將軍曾經從北方翻越 Alps 入侵 Italy：Hannibal。Napoleon 要做 Hannibal 做過的事；他沒有大象，但他確實在隆冬時節帶著軍隊翻越了 Alps。軍隊有沉重的大砲需要拖上陡坡，但士兵們用松木製作了大型雪橇，在這些雪橇上他們奮力地把大砲拖過厚厚的積雪。有些地方甚至連小路都沒有，只有一道狹窄的岩架——腳一滑、在雪中踩空一步就會讓人墜落身亡。然而，沿著狹窄的岩架、攀附著懸崖，士兵們艱辛地拖拉前行，當他們感到精疲力竭、氣力耗盡時，只需看一眼他們的將軍，就能感到新的勇氣和力量。

At long last they reached the famous St Bernard Monastery at the highest point of the St Bernard Pass. The monks could hardly believe their eyes when they saw a whole army coming up at a time when, normally, not a single traveller came that way.

終於，他們到達了位於 St Bernard Pass 最高點的著名 St Bernard 修道院。當修士們看到一整支軍隊爬上來的時候——在這個通常連一個旅人都不會經過的季節——他們簡直不敢相信自己的眼睛。

The way down the pass was just as dangerous, now the trouble was to stop the sledges with the guns from running away and from crashing into the men in front.

從山口下行同樣危險，現在的麻煩是要防止載著大砲的雪橇失控飛衝出去，撞上前面的人。

Somehow they made it, they crossed the Alps and poured into Northern Italy. The Austrians, taken by surprise, lost battle after battle and after a crushing defeat at Marengo in 1800, came begging for peace. Not only Austria but Britain too made peace with France. Imagine the joy and jubilation in Paris, and in the whole of France. Napoleon Bonaparte, the First Consul, had indeed worked a miracle and no praise was too high for him, the victorious hero of France.

不知怎的，他們成功了。他們翻越了 Alps，如潮水般湧入 Italy 北部。Austria 人措手不及，接連敗北，在 1800 年的 Marengo 遭到毀滅性的打擊後，前來乞求和平。不僅 Austria，連 Britain 也與法國講和了。想像一下 Paris 乃至全法國的歡欣鼓舞吧。Napoleon Bonaparte，第一執政，確實創造了奇蹟，對他——法國凱旋的英雄——再高的讚美都不為過。

The time had come for Napoleon to aim even higher. Why should he remain First Consul when he could have a crown? But he was not to be a mere King - he was going to be Emperor of France, as Charlemagne had been. He always had great examples from history to inspire him: Alexander the Great, Hannibal, now it was Charlemagne.

Napoleon 更上層樓的時機到了。既然他可以擁有王冠，為什麼還要繼續當第一執政呢？但他可不是要當一個普通的國王——他要成為法國的皇帝，就像 Charlemagne 曾經那樣。他總是從歷史上偉大的人物身上汲取靈感：Alexander the Great、Hannibal，現在則是 Charlemagne。

Amidst pomp and splendour the day came when Napoleon Bonaparte, the son of a Corsican lawyer, and his wife, Josephine, were crowned Emperor and Empress of France. And no one less than the Pope had to come from Rome to hand the imperial crown to Napoleon at the coronation. But it was Napoleon who put the crown on his own head as well as crowning his wife, Josephine. This was to show that, unlike Charlemagne, he owed the crown to himself and not to the Pope. Napoleon Bonaparte had become the Emperor Napoleon, but he knew that it was the French Revolution which had opened the way to the throne for him - it was his own ability and the French Revolution which had carried him so high, and not the blessing of the Pope.

在盛大而輝煌的典禮中，那一天來臨了——Napoleon Bonaparte，一個 Corsica 律師的兒子，和他的妻子 Josephine，被加冕為法國的皇帝和皇后。而且不是別人，正是教宗不得不從 Rome 前來，在加冕典禮上將皇冠交給 Napoleon。但是把皇冠戴在自己頭上的是 Napoleon 本人，為他的妻子 Josephine 加冕的也是他自己。這是為了表明，與 Charlemagne 不同，他的皇冠歸功於他自己，而不是教宗。Napoleon Bonaparte 成為了 Napoleon 皇帝，但他知道，是法國大革命為他開闢了通往王座的道路——是他自己的才能和法國大革命把他推到了如此之高的地位，而不是教宗的祝福。

For Napoleon to be Emperor of France was only the beginning. He said: "There will be no peace in Europe until it is united under one government." There was no doubt which government he had in mind: his own.

對 Napoleon 來說，成為法國皇帝只是一個開始。他說：「歐洲在統一於一個政府之下以前，不會有和平。」毫無疑問，他心中想的是哪個政府：他自己的。

It is not surprising that the other nations of Europe were worried, so the three main powers in Europe at that time, Britain, Austria and Russia, formed an alliance. If one of these countries was attacked by Napoleon, the other two would come to its aid.

歐洲其他國家感到擔憂並不令人意外，因此當時歐洲的三大強國——Britain、Austria 和 Russia——結成了同盟。如果其中一國遭到 Napoleon 的攻擊，另外兩國就會來援助。

Napoleon did not like that at all - and he disliked Britain most. He called the British contemptuously "a nation of shop-keepers" and he, a born soldier, could only despise businessmen. But these "shop-keepers" had spoiled his plans in Egypt, they had formed an alliance against him, it was high time that he taught them a lesson.

Napoleon 完全不喜歡這種局面——他最不喜歡的是 Britain。他輕蔑地稱英國人為「一個店小二的國家」，而他，一個天生的軍人，只能鄙視商人。但正是這些「店小二」破壞了他在 Egypt 的計畫，他們結成同盟對抗他，是時候給他們一個教訓了。

He would invade England - and, indeed, French troops were massed along the Channel and people in England expected an invasion at any moment. But Napoleon was not such a fool as to attempt an invasion as long as there was a British navy that could send his invading ships to the bottom of the sea. First the British Navy had to be destroyed.

他要入侵 England——事實上，法國軍隊已沿海峽集結，England 的人民隨時預期會遭到入侵。但只要英國海軍還能把他的入侵船艦送入海底，Napoleon 就不會愚蠢到嘗試入侵。首先必須摧毀英國海軍。

Napoleon therefore ordered his Admiral Villeneuve to draw the British fleet away from the Channel and to destroy it on the high seas. The French admiral fulfilled the first part of this order - and so it came that the French fleet and the British fleet came to grips with each other not in the Channel but in Spanish waters, off Cape Trafalgar.

因此 Napoleon 命令他的海軍上將 Villeneuve 將英國艦隊從海峽引開，在遠洋上加以摧毀。法國上將完成了這道命令的第一部分——於是法國艦隊和英國艦隊交鋒的地點不在海峽，而在西班牙海域，在 Cape Trafalgar 外海。

The commander of the British fleet was once again Admiral Nelson. It is strange to think that this great sailor was seasick every time he put to sea. And he had lost his right eye and his right arm in sea battles. This one-eyed, seasick disabled individual was the man who saved Britain from invasion.

英國艦隊的指揮官再次是 Nelson 上將。令人不可思議的是，這位偉大的水手每次出海都會暈船。而且他在海戰中失去了右眼和右臂。就是這位獨眼、暈船的殘疾人，拯救了 Britain 免遭入侵。
