On October 21, 1805, Nelson, standing on the deck of his flagship Victory, watched the approaching French fleet. On his orders signal-flags were run up on the mast of the Victory, it was a signal that has become famous in history: "England expects every man to do his duty." And from all the ships a mighty cheer went up as the sailors read the signal.

1805 年 10 月 21 日，Nelson 站在他的旗艦 Victory 號的甲板上，注視著逼近的法國艦隊。在他的命令下，旗號被升到 Victory 號的桅杆上，那是一個在歷史上聞名的信號：「England 期望每個人都履行自己的職責。」當水手們讀到這個信號時，所有船上都發出了雄壯的歡呼聲。

As the two fleets came closer the guns began to roar - and then the Victory went into action. The French poured shot after shot into Nelson's ship, but the Victory closed in on a French ship. Then there came a shot from high up in the rigging of the French ship, and Nelson was hit in the shoulder. He fell down and whispered to Hardy, the captain of the Victory, "They have done for me this time, Hardy." But, lying on the deck, Nelson put a handkerchief over his wound, he did not want the sailors to see that he had received a fatal wound.

當兩支艦隊靠近時，大砲開始怒吼——然後 Victory 號投入了戰鬥。法國人一炮接一炮地轟擊 Nelson 的船，但 Victory 號逼近了一艘法國艦船。這時，從法國艦船高處的索具上射來一發子彈，Nelson 的肩膀被擊中了。他倒了下去，低聲對 Victory 號的船長 Hardy 說：「這次他們把我打倒了，Hardy。」但躺在甲板上的 Nelson 用一條手帕蓋住了他的傷口——他不想讓水手們看到他受了致命傷。

One hour later Nelson was still alive and he heard his sailors cheer. And then Captain Hardy bent down to him: "Ten French ships have been sunk, fifteen have surrendered, they are finished." "Thank God," said Nelson. "I have done my duty." And with these words he died.

一個小時後 Nelson 仍然活著，他聽到了水手們的歡呼聲。然後 Hardy 船長俯身對他說：「十艘法國船被擊沉，十五艘投降了，他們完了。」「感謝上帝，」Nelson 說，「我已經盡了我的職責。」說完這些話，他去世了。

The Battle of Trafalgar is - after the Armada - the most important sea battle in British history. It saved Britain from the invasion by Napoleon's troops. With his own fleet destroyed and the British fleet in command of the Channel, Napoleon had to give up his plans of invasion. Twice - at Aboukir and at Trafalgar - it was Nelson who had frustrated Napoleon's plans.

Trafalgar 海戰——繼無敵艦隊之役後——是英國歷史上最重要的海戰。它使 Britain 免遭 Napoleon 軍隊的入侵。由於自己的艦隊被摧毀、英國艦隊掌控了海峽，Napoleon 不得不放棄他的入侵計畫。兩次——在 Aboukir 和在 Trafalgar——都是 Nelson 挫敗了 Napoleon 的計畫。

---

Chapter 33
Austerlitz. Wellington. Russia 1812

第三十三章
Austerlitz 戰役、Wellington、1812 年俄國遠征

Napoleon wanted a "united Europe" - though he was far ahead of his time in his wish - but he wanted to unite the nations of Europe by force and under his own rulership; and so the idea of a united Europe - good as it may have been - brought war and suffering and bloodshed.

Napoleon 想要一個「統一的歐洲」——儘管在這個願望上他遠遠超越了他的時代——但他想要以武力、在自己的統治下統一歐洲各國；因此，統一歐洲的理念——儘管可能是好的——帶來的卻是戰爭、苦難和流血。

Napoleon had failed to conquer Britain, he had failed through the valour of Nelson and his sailors, but on land he did defeat the armies of Britain, Austria and Russia.

Napoleon 未能征服 Britain，他因 Nelson 及其水手們的英勇而失敗了，但在陸地上，他確實擊敗了 Britain、Austria 和 Russia 的軍隊。

At Austerlitz the combined Austrian and Russian armies far outnumbered the French, but Napoleon was so certain of victory that he said to his generals on the morning of the battle: "Look at that red sunrise, this is the sun that will see my great victory." And so it was. The Russian and Austrian armies were not only defeated but destroyed in this Battle of Austerlitz in 1805.

在 Austerlitz，Austria 和 Russia 聯軍的兵力遠超法軍，但 Napoleon 對勝利如此確信，以至於在戰鬥當天清晨他對將軍們說：「看那紅色的日出，這輪太陽將見證我偉大的勝利。」果然如此。1805 年的 Austerlitz 之戰中，Russia 和 Austria 的軍隊不僅被擊敗，更被徹底摧毀。

After this crushing defeat Austria gave up the struggle - and there was no longer any country on the Continent to oppose Napoleon except perhaps Russia, but even Russia could no longer interfere with his plans. With that in mind, Napoleon set about remaking Europe according to his own ideas.

在這場毀滅性的慘敗之後，Austria 放棄了抵抗——歐洲大陸上除了或許 Russia 之外，再也沒有任何國家能夠對抗 Napoleon，但即使是 Russia 也無法再干涉他的計畫。有鑑於此，Napoleon 開始按照自己的構想重塑歐洲。

He took Northern Italy (which had been part of the Austrian Empire) for himself and assumed the title "King of Italy." But in Southern Italy he formed a new kingdom, the Kingdom of Naples which he gave to one of his generals, Murat, who became King of Naples.

他把 Italy 北部（原屬 Austria 帝國的一部分）據為己有，並取得「Italy 國王」的頭銜。但在 Italy 南部，他建立了一個新王國——Naples 王國，交給了他的一位將軍 Murat，Murat 成為了 Naples 國王。

Another general, Bernadotte, was given Sweden and became King of Sweden. As it happened, in all the upheavals that came later, Bernadotte (who was originally a cook) remained King of Sweden and the present King of Sweden is a descendant of Napoleon's general, Bernadotte.

另一位將軍 Bernadotte 被賜予 Sweden，成為了 Sweden 國王。碰巧的是，在後來的所有動盪中，Bernadotte（他原本是一名廚師）始終是 Sweden 國王，而現任 Sweden 國王就是 Napoleon 的將軍 Bernadotte 的後裔。

In addition to his generals, Napoleon also had brothers to reward. One brother was given Holland, becoming King of Holland. Another brother was given a slice of Germany called Westphalia, and a third was made King of Spain.

除了他的將軍們，Napoleon 還有兄弟要賞賜。一個兄弟被給予 Holland，成為 Holland 國王。另一個兄弟得到了 Germany 的一塊地方，叫做 Westphalia。第三個兄弟被立為 Spain 國王。

So, Napoleon - now at the pinnacle of his power - looked after his generals and after his brothers well. His old mother, Lactitia Bonaparte, was given a luxurious home in Paris, but the old Corsican woman kept on grumbling and mumbling, "I wonder how long all this is going to last."

就這樣，Napoleon——如今處於權力的巔峰——好好地照顧了他的將軍們和兄弟們。他年邁的母親 Lactitia Bonaparte 在 Paris 得到了一個豪華的住所，但這位老 Corsica 婦人一直嘟嘟囔囔地抱怨著：「我倒想知道這一切能持續多久。」

Napoleon had no such worries: he was going to make it last. His main concern was to have a son who could inherit this great empire. Unfortunately, his wife, the Empress Josephine, had not given him any children - it seems she could not have any - and so Napoleon divorced her. He had to have a son. Who was to be his second wife? His choice fell on a princess of the noblest blood in Europe: the daughter of the Emperor of Austria. Neither the Emperor, nor the princess could refuse the most powerful man in Europe. And so Napoleon - who had once approved when another Austrian princess, Marie Antoinette, went to the guillotine - married Marie Louise, the daughter of the Austrian Emperor. A year later in 1811 a son was born who received the title King of Rome while still in his cradle. Napoleon was certain that his son would inherit an empire as great as the dominions of ancient Rome.

Napoleon 沒有這樣的擔憂：他要讓這一切持續下去。他最主要的關切是要有一個能繼承這個偉大帝國的兒子。不幸的是，他的妻子 Josephine 皇后沒有為他生下任何孩子——看來她無法生育——於是 Napoleon 與她離了婚。他必須要有一個兒子。誰將成為他的第二任妻子呢？他的選擇落在了歐洲最高貴血統的一位公主身上：Austria 皇帝的女兒。無論是皇帝還是公主，都無法拒絕歐洲最有權勢的人。就這樣，Napoleon——曾經贊同另一位 Austria 公主 Marie Antoinette 走上斷頭台的人——娶了 Austria 皇帝的女兒 Marie Louise。一年後的 1811 年，一個兒子出生了，尚在搖籃中就被授予了 Rome 國王的頭銜。Napoleon 確信他的兒子將繼承一個如同古 Rome 版圖一樣偉大的帝國。

By that time, however, there were already cracks in his empire. One of these cracks was in Spain. Napoleon had made one of his brothers King of Spain and there was a French army in Spain to make sure he remained King. But the Spaniards hated the foreign ruler, they formed little bands, called "guerrillas" (from guerra, war) and these guerrilla-bands ambushed and killed a few French soldiers here, a few there. Some guerrillas were caught and shot by the French, but there were always others to carry on the fight.

然而到了這個時候，他的帝國已經出現了裂痕。其中一道裂痕在 Spain。Napoleon 讓他的一個兄弟當了 Spain 國王，並在 Spain 駐紮了一支法國軍隊以確保他繼續為王。但 Spain 人仇恨這個外國統治者，他們組成了小型武裝隊伍，稱為「游擊隊」（源自 guerra，意為戰爭），這些游擊隊在這裡伏擊殺死幾個法國士兵，在那裡又殺幾個。一些游擊隊員被法軍抓住並槍決，但總有其他人接替繼續戰鬥。

What made it worse was that the British, these "shopkeepers," had sent an army into Spain through Portugal. The commander of these British troops was a general who was to become famous: the Duke of Wellington, called by his soldiers the "Iron Duke." Wellington did not have an army large enough to drive the French out of Spain, but he could keep them busy; they had to fight continually so Spain was never a safe possession for Napoleon.

更糟糕的是，英國人——這些「店小二」——從 Portugal 派了一支軍隊進入 Spain。這支英軍的指揮官是一位日後將成名的將軍：Wellington 公爵，他的士兵們稱他為「鐵公爵」。Wellington 的軍隊不足以將法軍趕出 Spain，但他能讓法軍疲於奔命；他們不得不持續戰鬥，因此 Spain 對 Napoleon 來說從來就不是一個安穩的領地。

Napoleon could have finished Wellington and the guerrillas in Spain if there had been time, but there was no time because a greater army was preparing to strike against him: Russia.

如果有時間的話，Napoleon 本可以在 Spain 解決 Wellington 和游擊隊的問題，但沒有時間了，因為一支更強大的軍隊正準備向他發動進攻：Russia。

Napoleon knew that Russia was getting ready to declare war against him, and he decided to strike first and invade Russia before the Russian armies were ready.

Napoleon 知道 Russia 正準備向他宣戰，他決定先發制人，趁 Russia 軍隊尚未準備好之前入侵 Russia。

Russia is a vast country - and for the conquest of Russia Napoleon needed the largest army he had ever commanded. Not only the French,

Russia 是一個廣袤的國家——為了征服 Russia，Napoleon 需要他指揮過的最龐大的軍隊。不僅是法國人，

make excellent quarters for his army and give shelter during the terrible cold of the Russian winter.

為他的軍隊提供良好的營區，在 Russia 可怕的寒冬中給予庇護。

But the troops had hardly moved in when fires started all over the city, fires laid by the Russians. A few hundred of these Russians were caught and shot, but this did not stop the raging fires and Moscow went up in flames.

但部隊剛剛進駐，整座城市到處就燃起了大火——那是 Russia 人放的火。幾百名放火的 Russia 人被抓獲並槍決，但這未能阻止肆虐的大火，Moscow 在烈焰中化為灰燼。

Napoleon stared gloomily at the billowing flames and smoke. It was October, the terrible Russian winter was coming, there was no shelter for his half million men. There was only one thing to do: retreat, to get out of this accursed country.

Napoleon 陰沉地凝視著翻滾的火焰和濃煙。已是十月，可怕的 Russia 冬天即將來臨，他的五十萬大軍無處容身。只有一件事可做：撤退，離開這個被詛咒的國家。

This retreat from Moscow was a disaster: the weather grew colder and colder; the food became scarcer and scarcer; the soldiers grew weaker and weaker.

從 Moscow 的撤退是一場災難：天氣越來越冷；食物越來越少；士兵們越來越虛弱。

Snow fell in great, blinding flakes, blizzards howled, the cold seemed to cut to the bone, and thin uniforms were no protection at all. As they stumbled and trudged knee-deep in snow, men fell down from hunger and exhaustion, but no one who could still walk bothered - men threw away their weapons and abandoned their guns.

大片大片令人目眩的雪花飄落，暴風雪呼嘯，寒冷似乎刺透了骨頭，單薄的軍服毫無防禦作用。當他們跌跌撞撞地在齊膝深的雪地中艱難前行時，士兵們因飢餓和疲憊而倒下，但還能走路的人已無暇顧及——人們丟掉武器，拋棄了大砲。

---

Chapter 34
Elba. Waterloo

第三十四章
Elba 島與 Waterloo 戰役

After the disaster of the Russian campaign, the countries which had bowed so unwillingly to Napoleon's will now rose against him. Prussia and Austria joined with the victorious Russians and turned against Napoleon. They offered him an honourable peace: he could remain Emperor of France but should give up his other conquests. But this was not Napoleon's way - it was "all or nothing" for him, he could never be satisfied with that.

在 Russia 遠征的災難之後，那些曾不情不願地屈從於 Napoleon 意志的國家現在起而反抗他。Prussia 和 Austria 加入了勝利的 Russia 一方，聯手對抗 Napoleon。他們向他提出了一份體面的和約：他可以繼續當法國皇帝，但必須放棄其他征服的領土。但這不是 Napoleon 的作風——對他來說，要就全部，不然就什麼都不要，他永遠不會滿足於此。

This ultimately led to the "Battle of the Nations" near the German city of Leipzig in 1813. In this battle the French fought against the combined forces of Prussia, Austria and Russia. The battle raged for three days - but Napoleon's star was no longer rising, and he was defeated. He was driven back to France - and, in the end, had to surrender.

這最終導致了 1813 年在 Germany 城市 Leipzig 附近的「民族大會戰」。在這場戰役中，法軍對抗 Prussia、Austria 和 Russia 的聯軍。戰鬥持續了三天——但 Napoleon 的星運已不再上升，他被擊敗了。他被趕回法國——最終不得不投降。

The victorious allies forced Napoleon to abdicate, to renounce the throne of France. They did not want another Republican government in France, so a brother of the last King, Louis XVI, who had escaped to England was recalled and became King of France under the name Louis XVIII (Louis XVII was the poor boy who had died under the harsh treatment of the shoemaker).

勝利的同盟國迫使 Napoleon 退位，放棄法國的王位。他們不希望法國再出現一個共和政府，於是那位逃往 England 的末代國王 Louis XVI 的兄弟被召回，以 Louis XVIII 的名號成為法國國王（Louis XVII 是那個在鞋匠的粗暴對待下死去的可憐男孩）。

Napoleon was eventually banished to the little Mediterranean island of Elba between Italy and Corsica.

Napoleon 最終被放逐到地中海上一座小島 Elba，位於 Italy 和 Corsica 之間。

As a result of the Napoleonic Wars all the old frontiers had been changed so often that it was impossible to go back to things as they had been before. A congress was held in Vienna in which all the nations of Europe were to take part, and in which all claims should be settled fairly and peacefully.

由於 Napoleonic Wars，所有舊的疆界都被改來改去，以至於不可能再回到從前的樣子。一場大會在 Vienna 召開，歐洲所有的國家都將參加，所有的領土要求都應公平和平地得到解決。

For a whole year the statesmen of Europe debated and argued at this Congress of Vienna, but their discussions were rudely shattered by the news that Napoleon had escaped from Elba and had landed in France.

整整一年，歐洲的政治家們在 Vienna 大會上辯論和爭吵，但他們的討論被一個消息猛然打斷——Napoleon 從 Elba 逃了出來，已登陸法國。

The new King of France had sent troops against him. They had orders to shoot him. But Napoleon calmly walked towards the soldiers and cried: "Is there one of you who wants to shoot the Emperor? Here I am!" His old magic worked again: the soldiers shouted, "Vive l'Empereur!" and offered to fight for him.

法國新國王派出了軍隊對付他。他們接到了射殺他的命令。但 Napoleon 從容地走向士兵們，喊道：「你們中有誰想射殺皇帝嗎？我就在這裡！」他往日的魔力再次奏效了：士兵們高呼「Vive l'Empereur！」並願意為他而戰。

And they came, regiment after regiment, the men who had marched with him in the burning sands of Egypt, who had crossed the snows of the St Bernard Pass with him, who had shared victories in Italy and Austria and Germany with him - they all came to serve him again, to fight for him and to die for him. It seems incredible, but to his soldiers Napoleon was a kind of god.

他們來了，一個團接一個團——那些曾在 Egypt 灼熱的沙漠中與他一同行軍的人、曾與他一同翻越 St Bernard Pass 積雪的人、曾與他在 Italy、Austria 和 Germany 共享勝利的人——他們都來了，再次為他效勞，為他戰鬥，為他赴死。這似乎不可思議，但對他的士兵們來說，Napoleon 就是某種神。

This new venture of Napoleon's lasted exactly a hundred days. The nations who had bickered and argued at the Congress of Vienna, quickly came to full agreement against the common enemy.

Napoleon 這次新的冒險恰好持續了一百天。那些在 Vienna 大會上爭吵不休的國家，迅速就對付這個共同敵人達成了完全的共識。

The Duke of Wellington, the Iron Duke, who had fought the French so well in Spain was in command of a British force which was to attack Napoleon from Belgium, and a Prussian army under General Blucher was to join the British from Germany.

Wellington 公爵——鐵公爵——那位在 Spain 出色抗擊法軍的將軍，指揮著一支英國軍隊，將從 Belgium 進攻 Napoleon，而由 Blucher 將軍率領的一支 Prussia 軍隊將從 Germany 與英軍會合。

Napoleon decided to fight Wellington before the Prussians arrived and attacked the British at Waterloo (in what is now Belgium).

Napoleon 決定在 Prussia 人到達之前先與 Wellington 交戰，在 Waterloo（今 Belgium 境內）進攻英軍。

Hour after hour the French stormed against the "square formations" of the British, but Wellington's men held their ground. The fury of the French attack increased, and Wellington began to fear his men could not hold out much longer, but just in the nick of time the Prussians arrived.

一個小時又一個小時，法軍一波又一波地衝擊英軍的「方陣」，但 Wellington 的部隊堅守陣地。法軍的攻勢越來越猛烈，Wellington 開始擔心他的部隊無法再堅持多久，但就在千鈞一髮之際，Prussia 人到了。

With the Prussians on their side, the British went into attack - the French fighting spirit was broken.

有了 Prussia 人的支援，英軍轉入進攻——法軍的戰鬥意志崩潰了。

Only the soldiers of Napoleon's "Old Guard" stood their ground. They were surrounded on all sides and asked to surrender. They answered proudly: "The Guard can die but it cannot surrender." And they died, fighting to the last man.

只有 Napoleon 的「老近衛軍」堅守陣地。他們被四面包圍，被要求投降。他們驕傲地回答：「近衛軍可以赴死，但不能投降。」他們戰鬥到最後一人，壯烈犧牲。

This was the famous Battle of Waterloo, June 18, 1815, the last in the Napoleonic Wars.

這就是著名的 Waterloo 戰役，1815 年 6 月 18 日，Napoleonic Wars 中的最後一戰。

After his defeat, Napoleon made his way to a port where he gave himself up to the captain of a British ship, the Bellerophone. He became the prisoner of the British Government. It was decided to send him to a place from which he could not escape as he had done from Elba: the little island of St Helena in the South Atlantic - half-way between Africa and South America.

戰敗之後，Napoleon 前往一個港口，向一艘英國軍艦 Bellerophone 號的艦長投降。他成了英國政府的囚犯。人們決定把他送到一個他無法像從 Elba 那樣逃脫的地方：南大西洋上的小島 St Helena——位於非洲和南美洲之間的半途。

On St Helena Napoleon lived for another six years. He used to go for walks at his own furious pace (he could never walk slowly), or he stood staring over the sea and remembering another island, the island where he was born, Corsica. During that time he wrote his autobiography, the story of his life.

在 St Helena，Napoleon 又生活了六年。他常常以他一貫的急促步伐散步（他永遠無法慢慢走），或者站在那裡凝望大海，回憶另一座島嶼——他出生的島嶼，Corsica。在那段時間裡，他撰寫了自己的自傳——他一生的故事。

Napoleon had tried to unite Europe in one empire, and he had failed. But - whether he knew it or not - he had carried the ideas of the French Revolution into every country in Europe. The nations of Europe, Prussia, Austria, Russia, they were still ruled by kings and emperors who had absolute power, they still had aristocrats who enjoyed special privileges, but with the French armies the ideas of the French Revolution had arrived. The laws Napoleon had passed, too, had been fairer than the ancient laws of the conquered countries.

Napoleon 曾試圖將歐洲統一為一個帝國，但他失敗了。然而——無論他是否知道——他已經把法國大革命的思想帶入了歐洲的每一個國家。歐洲各國—— Prussia、Austria、Russia——仍然由擁有絕對權力的國王和皇帝統治著，仍然有享有特權的貴族，但隨著法國軍隊，法國大革命的思想也到來了。Napoleon 頒布的法律也比被征服國家的古老法律更加公正。

And the common people all over Europe were no longer satisfied to live obediently under their rulers and noblemen as they had done before Napoleon, they too demanded a new order of freedom, equality and brotherhood.

歐洲各地的平民百姓不再滿足於像 Napoleon 之前那樣順從地生活在統治者和貴族的治下，他們也要求一個自由、平等、博愛的新秩序。

So Napoleon, who finished the French Revolution when he made himself Emperor, really carried the spirit of the French Revolution to all nations of Europe.

所以，Napoleon——當他自立為皇帝時終結了法國大革命的人——實際上把法國大革命的精神帶給了歐洲所有的國家。

Yet, think of all the bloodshed which had happened to spread these ideas - the Reign of Terror, the wars of Napoleon. And think of that strange man, the Count of St Germain. If Louis XV had followed his advice the changes which had to come would not have been so violent, they would have been gradual and the world would have been spared much suffering.

然而，想想為了傳播這些思想而發生的所有流血——恐怖統治、Napoleon 的戰爭。再想想那位奇異的人物，St Germain 伯爵。如果 Louis XV 聽從了他的忠告，那些必然到來的變革就不會如此暴烈，它們會是漸進的，世界也將免去許多苦難。
Chapter 35
The Threefold State

第三十五章
三元社會

The word "body" not only refers to the human body, but can also be used in a different sense. In the legal profession, the word is also used with a quite different meaning. A group of people who act together, and together are responsible, is called "a body" - the social body.

「身體」（body）一詞不僅指人的肉體，也可以用在完全不同的意義上。在法律專業中，這個詞有另一種含義。一群人共同行動、共同負責，就被稱為「一個體」——社會體。

We all, men, women and children, rich and poor, are part of the social body of our country - and, perhaps, even of a larger "social body."

我們所有人，不論男女老少、貧富貴賤，都是我們國家社會體的一部分——或許，甚至是一個更大的「社會體」的一部分。

Now such a social body as Britain, or Germany, or France produces all kinds of things: the farmers produce food, the factories produce machines, the writers produce books, the actors produce plays, the government produces laws, and so on.

像 Britain、Germany 或 France 這樣的社會體生產各式各樣的東西：農夫生產食物，工廠製造機器，作家創作書籍，演員演出戲劇，政府制定法律，諸如此類。

But there is such a vast difference between the work of an actor or painter and the work of a farmer that one has really to make a division between one kind of work and another.

但演員或畫家的工作與農夫的工作之間有著如此巨大的差異，人們確實必須對不同類型的工作加以區分。

On one side there is all the work which in one way or another satisfies our physical needs: food, clothes, furniture, cars, and so on. And there is the other work which in one way or another satisfies the mind: books, theatres, films, paintings, music, but also schools and universities, as well as churches or temples, mosques or synagogues. So one part of all the work that is going on is devoted to our physical needs - the factories and farms produce, the shops sell, the railways and lorries transport the goods from place to place - and all this work which gives us the things our bodies need, is called economy (from Greek oikonomos, the steward, or house-manager).

一方面，有各種以某種方式滿足我們物質需求的工作：食物、衣服、家具、汽車等等。另一方面，還有以某種方式滿足心靈需求的工作：書籍、劇院、電影、繪畫、音樂，也包括學校和大學，以及教堂、寺廟、清真寺或猶太會堂。所以，正在進行的所有工作中，有一部分致力於滿足我們的物質需求——工廠和農場生產，商店販售，鐵路和貨車將貨物從一處運往另一處——所有這些提供我們身體所需之物的工作，被稱為經濟（economy，源自希臘文 oikonomos，意為管家或家務管理者）。

The other work - in schools and colleges, in the artist's studio, in concert halls and theatres, in the churches, and in newspapers and books, all that work which is for the mind, the spirit, is called culture.

另一種工作——在學校和學院裡、在藝術家的工作室裡、在音樂廳和劇院裡、在教堂裡、在報紙和書籍中——所有這些為心靈、為精神而做的工作，被稱為文化。

In addition there is another kind of work: the Government produces laws, but there is also the police force which has to see that the laws are kept, there are judges and lawyers, and there is the army, navy and airforce; all this is the third part of the "social body." All this third part is under the order of the Government, and as Government is elected by political action, it is called politics (from Greek politeia, citizenship).

此外還有另一種工作：政府制定法律，但也有警察部隊確保法律被遵守，有法官和律師，還有陸軍、海軍和空軍；所有這些是「社會體」的第三個部分。這第三個部分全都在政府的指揮之下，而政府是通過政治行動選舉產生的，因此被稱為政治（politics，源自希臘文 politeia，意為公民身分）。

Whatever people do to earn a living belongs to one of these three groups, culture, politics, economy.

人們為謀生所做的一切工作，都屬於這三個領域之一：文化、政治、經濟。

Just as the human physical body is threefold, so the "social" body is threefold, consisting of culture, politics, economy. One could compare culture with the head (which also does not produce anything physical), economy with the limbs, and politics with the rhythmic system.

正如人的肉體是三元的，「社會」體也是三元的，由文化、政治、經濟組成。可以把文化比作頭部（它也不生產任何物質的東西），經濟比作四肢，政治比作韻律系統。

Now in Europe five hundred, six hundred years ago, all that which I have called "culture" was firmly ruled by the Church. The popes and bishops decided what should be taught in schools and universities, what plays might be performed, what books should be published, and any disobedience was heresy, and could end in torture or death at the stake. Culture was entirely in the hands of the Church.

在五、六百年前的 Europe，我所說的「文化」全部被教會牢牢掌控。教宗和主教決定學校和大學該教什麼、什麼戲劇可以演出、什麼書可以出版，任何不服從都是異端，可能以酷刑或火刑告終。文化完全掌握在教會手中。

The other two parts, politics as well as the economy, were just as firmly under the authority of the king. The king gave laws and his soldiers enforced them. The king gave land to whom he liked, and so controlled the food production.

另外兩個部分——政治和經濟——同樣牢牢掌握在國王的權威之下。國王頒布法律，他的士兵負責執行。國王把土地賜給他喜歡的人，從而控制了糧食生產。

But as the modern time approached - from the Renaissance onwards - there came that great change. People were no longer willing to blindly obey the Church or the kings. Of course, neither Church nor kings gave up their powers without a struggle, and so came the wars of religion, the Civil War in England, the Glorious Revolution, and the American Revolution.

但隨著近代的到來——從文藝復興開始——產生了那場偉大的變革。人們不再願意盲目服從教會或國王。當然，教會和國王都不會輕易放棄他們的權力，於是便有了宗教戰爭、England 的內戰、光榮革命和美國革命。

In France, the kings and the Church held on to their power longer than in Britain, and the result was the terrible events of the French Revolution.

在 France，國王和教會比在 Britain 更長久地把持著權力，結果就是法國大革命那些可怕的事件。

During the French Revolution the words "liberty, equality, fraternity" sounded for the first time - it was as if people had been waiting to hear these words, they rejoiced in shouting them, they sang them, they put them on flags and coins, on the coat of arms and on statues. Not only in France, but all over the world people thought that with these three words, with these three ideas, a new age of happiness for all would come. But, beautiful as the ideas were, the people who shouted them did not give much thought as to how they should be put into practice. The result was chaos and the guillotine, and in the end the dictator, Napoleon, came to power.

在法國大革命期間，「自由、平等、博愛」這幾個字第一次響起——彷彿人們一直在等待聽到這些話語，他們歡欣地呼喊著、歌唱著，把它們印在旗幟和錢幣上、刻在國徽和雕像上。不僅在 France，全世界的人都以為，靠著這三個詞、這三個理念，一個人人幸福的新時代就要來臨。但理想雖然美好，高喊這些口號的人們並沒有深思該如何將它們付諸實踐。結果就是混亂和斷頭台，最終獨裁者 Napoleon 奪取了政權。

The three words liberty, equality, fraternity can only be meaningful when they are used separately, with reference to each of the three divisions of the social body. Liberty belongs to culture, equality to politics and law, brotherhood to economics. During the French Revolution there was no comprehension of this: Robespierre sent the great scientist Lavoisier to the guillotine simply because he was a better scientist than others and thus sinned against equality. Marat told people to form a brotherhood for the purpose of killing aristocrats; it was chaos. Even in the time after the French Revolution, after Napoleon, the three ideas were still rather like dynamite - if people handled them wrongly the result was upheaval and bloodshed.

自由、平等、博愛這三個詞，只有在分別使用、各自對應社會體三個領域時，才能真正有意義。自由屬於文化，平等屬於政治和法律，博愛屬於經濟。在法國大革命期間，人們完全沒有理解這一點：Robespierre 把偉大的科學家 Lavoisier 送上了斷頭台，僅僅因為他比別人更優秀的科學家，因此「冒犯了」平等。Marat 告訴人們結成兄弟會去殺死貴族；一切都是混亂。即使在法國大革命之後、Napoleon 之後，這三個理念仍然像炸藥一樣——如果人們處理不當，結果就是動盪和流血。

At the time of the French Revolution, while all this noise and fighting was going on, there was also another great change. This change came so silently that no one realized at the time that it was a far more important change than the French Revolution and the Napoleonic Wars. This silent revolution changed life completely; it brought great blessings and also terrible misery.

在法國大革命期間，當所有這些喧囂和戰鬥進行的同時，還有另一場偉大的變革正在發生。這場變革來得如此悄然無聲，以至於當時沒有人意識到它是一場遠比法國大革命和拿破崙戰爭更重要的變革。這場無聲的革命徹底改變了生活；它帶來了巨大的福祉，也帶來了可怕的苦難。

But this silent revolution made the three ideals, liberty, equality, fraternity even more urgent, more necessary than they were before, yet hardly anyone at the time realized it.

但這場無聲的革命使得自由、平等、博愛這三個理想比以往更加迫切、更加必要，然而當時幾乎沒有人意識到這一點。

Chapter 36
The Beginning of the Industrial Revolution

第三十六章
工業革命的開端

The silent revolution, the Industrial Revolution, began in England, in Lancashire in the year 1764. By that time the making of woollen and cotton cloth had become a great industry in Lancashire. However, there were no factories, no smoking chimneys, only small towns and villages. The two processes involved in making cloth, the spinning and the weaving, were done in people's homes.

這場無聲的革命——工業革命——於一七六四年在 England 的 Lancashire 開始。到那時，毛織品和棉布的製作已經成為 Lancashire 的一項重要產業。然而，當時沒有工廠，沒有冒煙的煙囪，只有小鎮和村莊。製布涉及的兩道工序——紡紗和織布——都在人們的家裡完成。

Usually it was the father of the family who sat at the weaving loom and sent the "shuttle" backwards and forwards. The wife and children did the spinning of the yarn using a spinning wheel. A pedal turned a large wheel which drove a little spindle much faster. As it rotated, it twisted a thin sliver of wool into a thread.

通常是一家之父坐在織布機前，來回穿梭「梭子」。妻子和孩子們則用紡車紡紗。一個踏板轉動一個大輪子，帶動一個小紡錘轉得更快。紡錘旋轉時，將一條細細的羊毛條捻成一根線。

Now in that year 1764, one Lancashire weaver in the village of Blackburn, James Hargreaves by name, accidentally knocked his wife's spinning wheel over so that it was flat on the ground and the wheel was still turning. His wife, Jenny Hargreaves called him a clumsy lout, but the man paid no attention, he kept on staring at the turning wheel.

就在一七六四年那一年，Lancashire 的 Blackburn 村裡有個織工，名叫 James Hargreaves，他不小心碰倒了妻子的紡車，紡車平躺在地上，輪子仍在轉動。他的妻子 Jenny Hargreaves 罵他笨手笨腳，但這個人毫不在意，一直盯著轉動的輪子看。

"What's the matter with you?" asked Jenny.

「你怎麼了？」Jenny 問道。

"You know," said James Hargreaves, "looking at that thing, it just occurred to me that if one arranged the whole contraption as it is now - horizontally - one could make this one great wheel turn not only one but many spindles, even eight of them. All it needs is to make the wheel drive several transmission bands which turn several spindles."

「你知道嗎，」James Hargreaves 說，「看著這東西，我突然想到，如果把整個裝置照現在這樣——水平地擺放——就可以讓這一個大輪子不只帶動一個，而是許多個紡錘，甚至八個。所需要的只是讓輪子驅動幾條傳動帶，帶動幾個紡錘。」

That was the idea that came to Jimmy Hargreaves as he looked at his wife's spinning wheel on the floor: that by using several transmission bands on the same wheel, several spindles could be turned, which means that turning one wheel, one could make not only one, but several threads at the same time.

這就是 Jimmy Hargreaves 看著地上妻子的紡車時產生的想法：利用同一個輪子上的幾條傳動帶，可以帶動幾個紡錘，這意味著轉動一個輪子，就能同時紡出不只一根，而是好幾根線。

Now the Hargreaves were so poor that they did not even have a weaving loom of their own. James Hargreaves and several other equally poor weavers worked for a Mr Peel who owned a number of looms put up in a shed. So when Jenny made her yarn she could not give it to her husband - she had to sell it to Mr Peel who, then, gave it to the weavers.

Hargreaves 一家窮到連自己的織布機都沒有。James Hargreaves 和其他幾個同樣窮困的織工替一位名叫 Peel 先生的人工作，Peel 先生在一間棚屋裡擺放了好幾台織布機。所以 Jenny 紡好紗之後不能交給丈夫——她得把紗賣給 Peel 先生，然後 Peel 先生再把紗交給織工們。

As you can imagine these weavers who worked only for a wage were much worse off than a weaver who owned his own loom and could sell the cloth he made. Hargreaves was one of the poor weavers who did not possess their own looms - and all he thought was: if Jenny can twist eight threads with one turn of the wheel she will make eight times more yarn per day than before - and that will bring us eight times more money.

可以想見，這些只領工資的織工日子遠不如擁有自己織布機、能自己賣布的織工。Hargreaves 就是那些沒有自己織布機的窮織工之一——他心裡想的只有一件事：如果 Jenny 轉一次輪子就能紡出八根線，她一天就能紡出以前八倍的紗——那就能為我們帶來八倍的收入。

And so with a few carpenters' tools Hargreaves set about changing Jenny's spinning wheel so that it could drive eight spindles. But as he worked and experimented, it occurred to him that this new kind of spinning wheel should be kept secret. If other women all produced eight times more yarn, there would be so much yarn that the price of yarn would go down, and in the end they would produce more yarn but still get as little as before. So Hargreaves wanted his invention to remain a secret.

於是 Hargreaves 用幾件木匠工具開始改造 Jenny 的紡車，使它能驅動八個紡錘。但在工作和實驗的過程中，他想到這種新型紡車應該保密。如果其他婦女都能生產八倍的紗，紗就會多到價格下跌，到頭來她們雖然生產了更多的紗，收入卻和從前一樣少。所以 Hargreaves 希望他的發明保持秘密。

Hargreaves changed Jenny's spinning wheel and eventually it worked producing eight times more yarn - and every week Jenny took a quantity of yarn to Mr Peel which astonished everybody. How was it possible that this woman could make so much yarn with one wheel? The other women in the village would not leave Jenny in peace, and in a small village where everybody knows everybody else, and where people walk into each other's houses any time of day, in such a village, one can't keep any secrets. Perhaps, Jenny was also proud of her husband's cleverness and blurted out what he had done with her spinning wheel; in any case, the principle, one wheel with several transmission bands to drive more spindles, that principle became known in the village, and all the women demanded that their husbands make them a "spinning jenny" as they called it.

Hargreaves 改造了 Jenny 的紡車，最終成功了，產出八倍的紗——每個星期 Jenny 帶去給 Peel 先生的紗量都讓所有人驚嘆不已。這個女人怎麼可能用一架紡車紡出這麼多紗？村裡其他婦女不肯放過 Jenny，而在一個人人相識、隨時可以走進彼此家門的小村莊裡，什麼秘密都守不住。也許 Jenny 也為丈夫的聰明才智感到驕傲，脫口說出了他對紡車做了什麼；無論如何，一個輪子搭配幾條傳動帶驅動更多紡錘的原理，在村裡傳開了，所有的婦女都要求丈夫替她們做一台「珍妮紡紗機」（spinning jenny），人們這樣稱呼它。

Soon the news spread from Blackburn to other parts of Lancashire: James Hargreaves made a machine that makes eight yarns but needs only one spinner.

消息很快從 Blackburn 傳到了 Lancashire 的其他地方：James Hargreaves 造了一台機器，只需一個紡紗工就能紡出八根紗。

"Yes," said some people, "but if this goes on, this devilish invention will rob honest handworkers of their living."

「是的，」有些人說，「但如果這樣下去，這個魔鬼般的發明會搶走誠實手工工人的生計。」

If one spinner could do the work which had previously taken eight, then the other seven would soon be out of work - their livelihood would be taken away from them. That is what the weavers and spinners of Lancashire began to fear; and soon somebody else might make a loom on which one man could weave as much as twenty weavers used to do, and then thousands of weavers would be out of work.

如果一個紡紗工能做以前八個人做的事，那另外七個人很快就會失業——他們的生計會被剝奪。Lancashire 的織工和紡紗工們開始擔心的正是這件事；而且很快可能有人會造出一台織布機，讓一個人能織出相當於以前二十個織工的布量，那時數以千計的織工就會失業。

This kind of thing could not be allowed to go on; the making of these infernal machines had to be stopped. And so the Lancashire weavers organized a kind of protest march to the village of Blackburn where the Hargreaves lived. A few hundred of them marched and their leaders made fiery speeches: "The machines take the bread from us and from our families, we will be left to starve." The mob roared with anger.

這種事絕不能繼續下去；製造這些該死的機器必須被阻止。於是 Lancashire 的織工們組織了一場抗議遊行，朝 Hargreaves 一家居住的 Blackburn 村進發。幾百人浩浩蕩蕩地前進，他們的領袖發表慷慨激昂的演說：「機器從我們和我們家人口中搶走了麵包，我們將被遺棄至餓死。」人群怒吼著。

Hargreaves and his wife had wisely left their little cottage and were hiding at a friend's house - otherwise they would have fared ill at the hands of the mob. The furious body of men marched to Hargreaves' cottage, burst open the door and smashed his spinning jenny as well as all the furniture. And while they were at it, they also smashed the looms in Mr Peel's shed. Only when they had broken everything that could be destroyed, did the angry weavers leave Blackburn.

Hargreaves 和妻子明智地離開了他們的小屋，躲到朋友家——否則他們在暴民手中必定不會好過。憤怒的人群湧向 Hargreaves 的小屋，破門而入，砸碎了他的珍妮紡紗機和所有家具。順便連 Peel 先生棚屋裡的織布機也一起砸了。直到把所有能破壞的東西都毀掉，憤怒的織工們才離開 Blackburn。

This was the first machine-smashing riot in history, but by no means the last. Later it happened again and again that men put out of work by machines, tried to fight the machines by smashing them - but, of course, it was always in vain. The machines stayed, and the skilled handworkers lost their livelihood.

這是歷史上第一次砸機器暴動，但絕非最後一次。後來一再發生因機器而失業的工人試圖用砸毀機器來抗爭——但當然，這永遠是徒勞的。機器留了下來，技藝精湛的手工工人失去了生計。

Hargreaves realized that after this riot, Lancashire was no longer safe for him. He and his wife fled to another part of England, to Nottingham. Now he tried something he should have done before; he tried to take out a patent for his invention - so that anybody who copied the spinning jenny would have to pay him a fee. But you can only get a patent for a machine if no such machine is already in use when you apply for the patent. As spinning jennies were already made and used all over the country, Hargreaves could not get a patent, and so he got nothing for his invention.

Hargreaves 意識到暴動之後，Lancashire 對他來說不再安全。他和妻子逃到了 England 的另一個地方——Nottingham。這時他才嘗試做一件他早該做的事：為他的發明申請專利——這樣任何仿製珍妮紡紗機的人都必須向他付費。但你只有在申請專利時該機器尚未被使用的情況下，才能獲得專利。由於珍妮紡紗機已經在全國各地被製造和使用，Hargreaves 無法獲得專利，所以他的發明一分錢也沒有得到。

And so the Hargreaves remained poor to the end of their lives while others made fortunes. A new class of men was rising in Britain, the manufacturers - men who had the money to have big machines made for them - and they built spinning jennies with twenty spindles.

因此 Hargreaves 一家一直窮到最後，而其他人卻發了財。一個新階級在 Britain 崛起——製造商——這些人有錢訂製大型機器——他們建造了有二十個紡錘的珍妮紡紗機。

Another Lancashire inventor, Richard Arkwright, improved the spinning jenny. He had the bright idea to have the spinning wheel not driven by hand or foot, but by water power. For centuries flour mills had used water power to grind corn, now Arkwright used water power to drive the spinning wheel, so even the spinner who used to turn the wheel was no longer necessary. These factories driven by water power were called "mills" - cotton mills or woollen mills - because they worked like flour mills. Power-driven machines had arrived.

另一位 Lancashire 的發明家 Richard Arkwright 改良了珍妮紡紗機。他想到了一個妙主意：讓紡車不靠人手或腳力驅動，而是靠水力。幾個世紀以來，磨坊一直用水力來磨穀物，現在 Arkwright 用水力來驅動紡車，連以前轉動輪子的紡紗工都不再需要了。這些由水力驅動的工廠被稱為「工場」（mills）——棉紡工場或毛紡工場——因為它們的運作方式和磨坊一樣。動力驅動的機器來臨了。

When Arkwright built such a cotton mill in Lancashire the weavers again protested - they stormed the mill and burnt it down. But Arkwright simply went and built more mills in other parts of England. The new machines had come to stay - and the Industrial Revolution was on its way. Arkwright made a fortune.

當 Arkwright 在 Lancashire 建了這樣一座棉紡工場時，織工們再度抗議——他們衝進工場並將它燒毀。但 Arkwright 只是到 England 的其他地方去建造更多工場。新機器已不可逆轉——工業革命正在路上。Arkwright 因此發了大財。

It is strange to think that it all began in 1764 in Blackburn where James Hargreaves knocked over his wife's spinning wheel!

想到這一切都始於一七六四年的 Blackburn，James Hargreaves 碰倒了妻子的紡車，不禁令人感慨萬千！

Chapter 37
The Arrival of Steam Power

第三十七章
蒸汽動力的到來

The stories of Hargreaves and Arkwright show two kinds of inventions which brought about the Industrial Revolution. Hargreaves' invention was a machine which could do the same work as the human hand, but much quicker. His invention increased the speed of production.

Hargreaves 和 Arkwright 的故事展現了帶來工業革命的兩種發明。Hargreaves 的發明是一台能做與人手相同工作的機器，但速度快得多。他的發明提高了生產速度。

Arkwright's use of water power went further: it replaced not only human skill, but human strength and energy with the powers of nature.

Arkwright 對水力的運用則更進一步：它不僅取代了人的技藝，還用自然的力量取代了人的體力和精力。

It is interesting to follow the stages by which people learned to make the powers of nature work for them. At first they only had their own strength to work with - which is very little compared to the strength of some animals, therefore human beings learned to use certain animals - horses, oxen, donkeys - to work for them. Then came the wind and water - wind to drive sailing ships and water to drive mills. This stage lasted for a long time without much alteration.

追溯人類學會讓自然力量為己所用的各個階段，是很有意思的。起初，人們只能依靠自己的力量工作——這與某些動物的力量相比實在微不足道，因此人類學會了使用某些動物——馬、牛、驢——為自己工作。然後是風力和水力——風驅動帆船，水驅動磨坊。這個階段持續了很長時間，沒有太大的改變。

Leonardo da Vinci had, however, thought of another way of using water - in the form of steam. He realized that if you heat water, the expanding steam had great power which could be used to move the wheels of machines. He wrote in his notebooks that it would be possible to move a ship over the ocean by steam power. Unfortunately this great idea remained buried in his notebooks.

然而 Leonardo da Vinci 想到了另一種使用水的方式——以蒸汽的形式。他意識到，如果加熱水，膨脹的蒸汽具有巨大的力量，可以用來驅動機器的輪子。他在筆記本中寫道，有可能用蒸汽動力驅動船隻橫渡大洋。不幸的是，這個偉大的想法一直埋沒在他的筆記本中。

Two hundred years later, about 1650, a Frenchman, De Cant, was overcome with pity for the poor men who had to row the big ships when there was no wind. He came to the French minister Richelieu with a plan to use steam instead of slaves - and the minister was so upset by the idea of using machines instead of human beings that the poor inventor was thrown into prison for the rest of his life.

大約兩百年後，約一六五零年，一個法國人 De Cant 對那些無風時不得不划大船的可憐人們深感同情。他向法國大臣 Richelieu 提出了一個用蒸汽取代奴隸的計畫——但這位大臣對用機器取代人力的想法感到極度不安，可憐的發明家被投入監獄，度過了餘生。

Newcomen invented a steam-driven machine which was being used fifty years later, by about 1700, in England. His machine, driven by steam from a water boiler heated by coal, pumped water out of mines. Using a great amount of coal for very little work this wasteful water pump of the English mines was to be the cause of another great step in the Industrial Revolution.

Newcomen 發明了一台蒸汽驅動的機器，大約五十年後的一七零零年左右在 England 被使用。他的機器由燃煤鍋爐產生的蒸汽驅動，用來把礦井裡的水抽出來。這台英國礦井的水泵浪費大量的煤卻只做很少的功，但正是它將引發工業革命中另一個重大進步。

The man who changed the design of this pump and so gave the world a new source of power, was a Scotsman, James Watt. James Watt, who was born in Greenock and lived in Glasgow, had not received a higher education, but being skilled with his hands he had become a maker of scientific instruments for Glasgow University.

改變了這台水泵設計、從而給世界帶來新動力來源的人，是一位蘇格蘭人 James Watt。James Watt 出生於 Greenock，住在 Glasgow，沒有接受過高等教育，但因手藝精巧，成為了 Glasgow 大學的科學儀器製造師。

At the University there was a model of the steam-driven pump used in the coalmines - and this model had just as many snags and faults as the real pumps used in the mines. One day the Professor of Physics at Glasgow University got so annoyed with the model that he sent for James Watt and said: "Look here, you are the instrument maker. Can you do something with this contraption - change the design, so that it will work smoothly and without hitch?"

大學裡有一台煤礦用蒸汽水泵的模型——這台模型和真正礦井裡使用的水泵一樣毛病百出。有一天，Glasgow 大學的物理教授被這台模型氣得受不了，於是叫來 James Watt 說：「你看，你是儀器製造師。你能對這個玩意兒做點什麼嗎——改改設計，讓它運轉順暢、不出問題？」

The year 1764 when Watts started to fiddle about with that model of the water pump was the same year in which Hargreaves began to fiddle about with his wife's spinning wheel.

一七六四年，Watt 開始擺弄那台水泵模型的那一年，正是 Hargreaves 開始擺弄妻子紡車的同一年。

But Watt's task was more difficult than Hargreaves'. It took Watt several years (up to 1769) until he hit upon a design which made the machine run more smoothly and efficiently, that is, using far less coal. This design was the first really useful steam engine.

但 Watt 的任務比 Hargreaves 的更加困難。Watt 花了好幾年時間（直到一七六九年），才找到一種讓機器運轉更順暢、更高效的設計，也就是使用少得多的煤。這個設計就是第一台真正實用的蒸汽機。

It is not true, as is often said, that Watt "invented" the steam engine - it existed already. What Watt did was to change and improve its design. But Watt realized that his new design was not merely an improved pump, he realized that his design could be used to make steam drive any kind of machine.

人們常說 Watt「發明」了蒸汽機，這其實不正確——蒸汽機早已存在。Watt 所做的是改變和改良它的設計。但 Watt 意識到，他的新設計不僅僅是一台改良的水泵，他意識到他的設計可以用來讓蒸汽驅動任何種類的機器。

And so he went straight to London to take out a patent for his invention. In London he met an engineer, Matthew Boulton, and the two men went into partnership and founded an engineering firm, Boulton and Watt, which became world famous for making steam engines.

於是他直奔 London 為自己的發明申請專利。在 London 他結識了一位工程師 Matthew Boulton，兩人合夥創辦了一家工程公司——Boulton and Watt，這家公司因製造蒸汽機而舉世聞名。

The people who first became interested in buying that new steam engine were the mill owners, the cotton manufacturers.

最先對購買這種新型蒸汽機感興趣的人，是工場主們，也就是棉花製造商們。

Arkwright's idea of having the spinning wheels driven by water power, by streams and rivers, had certain disadvantages. First, the cotton mill had to be built beside the river or stream; secondly, as the water level of a river changed, it was a very irregular source of power, and in many dry summers the mills had to stop completely.

Arkwright 用水力——溪流和河川——來驅動紡車的想法有一些缺點。首先，棉紡工場必須建在河邊或溪旁；其次，由於河水水位會變化，它是一種非常不穩定的動力來源，在許多乾旱的夏天，工場不得不完全停工。

But with a steam engine driven by coal, a factory could be built anywhere near the coal supply and would run in all weathers.

但有了燃煤驅動的蒸汽機，工廠可以建在任何靠近煤炭供應的地方，而且在任何天候下都能運轉。

And so, the cotton industry which was growing rapidly, changed from water power to steam power. The cotton factories were still called "mills."

於是，快速成長的棉紡產業從水力轉向了蒸汽動力。棉紡工廠仍然被稱為「工場」（mills）。

Chapter 38
The Locomotive

第三十八章
火車頭

When James Watt went into partnership with the engineer, Boulton, their firm, Boulton and Watt, became world-famous as makers of steam engines. Steam engines revolutionized the cotton industry as cotton mills changed from water power to steam power. As more and more cotton mills were built, more steam engines were required, and the firm of Boulton and Watt flourished.

當 James Watt 與工程師 Boulton 合夥之後，他們的公司 Boulton and Watt 因製造蒸汽機而舉世聞名。隨著棉紡工場從水力轉為蒸汽動力，蒸汽機革新了棉紡產業。越來越多的棉紡工場建成，就需要越來越多的蒸汽機，Boulton and Watt 公司因而蓬勃發展。

Boulton and Watt also improved water pumps for mines, and these water pumps were also sold in great numbers. When an engineering firm sells a big machine like a steam engine, it is not just sent to the customer. They also send one or two engineers who see to it that the machine is properly installed and runs smoothly. That job is usually given to the young engineers employed by the makers.

Boulton and Watt 也改良了礦井用的水泵，這些水泵同樣大量售出。當一家工程公司出售像蒸汽機這樣的大型機器時，不只是把機器送到客戶那裡就好。他們還會派一兩名工程師前往，確保機器正確安裝並順利運轉。這項工作通常交給製造商僱用的年輕工程師。

One such engineer at Boulton and Watt was a Scotsman, William Murdoch. Young Murdoch was full of original ideas. When he came to the firm of Boulton and Watt and applied for a job he was interviewed by Boulton himself. During the conversation Murdoch - being a little nervous - twiddled his hat in his hands, and the hat fell from his fingers. When the hat hit the ground it made a strange solid thump, not at all like an ordinary hat. It turned out that, being short of money, and a thrifty Scotsman, Murdoch had made himself a hat of wood, turning it on a lathe. Old Boulton was so impressed by this that he engaged Murdoch right away.

Boulton and Watt 公司裡有一位這樣的年輕工程師，是蘇格蘭人 William Murdoch。年輕的 Murdoch 滿腦子新奇的想法。當他來到 Boulton and Watt 公司應徵工作時，由 Boulton 本人親自面試。談話中，Murdoch 因為有點緊張，雙手擺弄著帽子，帽子從指間滑落。帽子落地時發出一聲奇怪的沉悶聲響，完全不像普通帽子。原來，因為手頭拮据，加上蘇格蘭人的節儉本性，Murdoch 用車床車了一頂木頭帽子戴著。老 Boulton 對此印象深刻，當場就僱用了 Murdoch。

On one occasion young Murdoch was sent to Cornwall to install several pumps in a tin mine. The job took several weeks and during that time Murdoch lived in a Cornish village. And while he was in that village he experimented with another of his original ideas in his spare time: if the steam engine is not placed on the ground, as it is always done, but mounted on wheels, can it turn the wheels so that the machine moves itself? Murdoch found a way of doing this by connecting the "piston" of the steam engine (the part that goes up and down) by iron rods to the front wheels. He worked it all out on paper first - and then he made a little model of the whole contraption - just large enough to see if it would really work with coal and water.

有一次，年輕的 Murdoch 被派到 Cornwall 去安裝幾台錫礦的水泵。這項工作花了好幾個星期，期間 Murdoch 住在一個 Cornwall 的村莊裡。在那個村莊的閒暇時間，他實驗了另一個新奇想法：如果蒸汽機不像往常那樣放在地面上，而是安裝在輪子上，它能不能轉動輪子讓機器自己移動？Murdoch 找到了一個辦法，用鐵桿把蒸汽機的「活塞」（上下運動的部分）連接到前輪。他先在紙上把一切都設計好——然後做了整個裝置的小模型——大小剛好能看出用煤和水是否真的能運作。

But he did not want to try out his little model in the village, as the people who lived there were still very superstitious and Murdoch did not want to scare them. Instead he experimented at night and in a quiet lane that people seldom frequented. But one night the little machine ran away from him and clattered down the lane, spouting smoke and sparks. Just at that moment the vicar of the village came up the lane. When he saw a dark object belching smoke and sparks running towards him, he gave one yelp: "the Devil!" and ran. The village talked for weeks of nothing else.

但他不想在村裡試驗他的小模型，因為那裡的人仍然非常迷信，Murdoch 不想嚇到他們。所以他在夜間，在一條人跡罕至的僻靜小路上進行實驗。但有一天晚上，小機器脫離了他的控制，噴著煙火沿小路嘎嘎作響地跑了起來。正在那時，村裡的牧師走上了這條小路。當他看到一個噴著煙火的黑色物體朝自己衝來時，他驚叫了一聲：「魔鬼！」拔腿就跑。整個村莊為此議論了好幾個星期。

Still, the little model worked, and when Murdoch returned to his firm, Boulton and Watt, he showed it to old Watt and asked for permission to make further experiments with a steam engine that would drive itself. You should have heard Watt! He said it was a disgrace that an engineer employed by the respectable firm of Boulton and Watt wasted his time on such nonsense. And that was that. Young Murdoch had built the first locomotive in Britain - but nothing came of it because old Watt could see no use for it. (In Paris a Frenchman had made himself a steam-driven carriage twenty years earlier - but it toppled over in the street - and that was the end of that experiment.)

儘管如此，小模型確實能運作。當 Murdoch 回到 Boulton and Watt 公司時，他把模型展示給老 Watt 看，並請求允許他繼續實驗能自行驅動的蒸汽機。你真該聽聽 Watt 怎麼說的！他說，一個受僱於聲譽卓著的 Boulton and Watt 公司的工程師，竟然把時間浪費在這種胡鬧上，簡直是恥辱。就這樣結束了。年輕的 Murdoch 建造了 Britain 第一台火車頭——但什麼也沒能成，因為老 Watt 看不出它有什麼用處。（二十年前在 Paris，一個法國人造了一輛蒸汽馬車——但它在街上翻倒了——那次實驗就此告終。）

Murdoch, discouraged by Watt, gave up his idea of a steam-driven carriage, but another man carried on with it. He was a Cornishman, Richard Trevithick.

Murdoch 被 Watt 潑了冷水，放棄了蒸汽馬車的想法，但另一個人繼續了下去。他是 Cornwall 人 Richard Trevithick。

Trevithick built the first large locomotive. It ran on rails and pulled trucks in an iron mine. Before the locomotive, horse-drawn carts had been used in this mine; and the miners were furious that the horse drivers had been put out of work. So, in order to avoid violence, this first railway had to be stopped.

Trevithick 建造了第一台大型火車頭。它在鐵軌上運行，在一座鐵礦裡拉貨車。在火車頭出現之前，這座礦井使用的是馬拉車；礦工們對趕馬車的工人因此失業感到憤怒。所以，為了避免暴力衝突，這條第一條鐵路不得不停止運營。

Trevithick made another attempt to use a steam carriage. He went to London where he built a kind of "merry-go-round" - a circular track on which a locomotive went round and round - and people could ride on it for a shilling. But as the speed of that ride was only five miles per hour (8 kph), it was not a great thrill. Trevithick lost money on this venture and eventually gave up. He left England and went to South America.

Trevithick 又做了一次使用蒸汽馬車的嘗試。他去了 London，在那裡建造了一種「旋轉木馬」——一條環形軌道，火車頭在上面繞圈——人們花一先令就能搭乘。但由於時速只有五英里（八公里），算不上什麼刺激的體驗。Trevithick 在這次冒險中賠了錢，最終放棄了。他離開了 England，去了南美洲。

The man who took up the idea and made a success of it was George Stephenson. He was not - as people often say - the inventor of the locomotive, no more than Watt was the inventor of the steam engine. But, like Watt, Stephenson improved the design so that the locomotive became more than a toy.

接過這個想法並取得成功的人是 George Stephenson。他並不是——正如人們常說的那樣——火車頭的發明者，就像 Watt 也不是蒸汽機的發明者一樣。但和 Watt 一樣，Stephenson 改進了設計，使火車頭不再只是一個玩具。

The first railway line was built by Stephenson in 1825 between Stockton and Darlington, a stretch of about twenty miles (30 km). You can get some idea of the speed of this locomotive from the fact that a man on horseback rode in front of it to make sure that the line was clear.

第一條鐵路線由 Stephenson 於一八二五年建成，在 Stockton 和 Darlington 之間，全長約二十英里（三十公里）。從一個人騎馬在前面開路以確保軌道暢通這個事實，你就可以想像這台火車頭的速度了。

It was once again the cotton manufacturers who became interested in this new machine. The only way to move the bales of raw cotton from the port of Liverpool to Manchester, for instance, where most of the cotton mills were, was by barge on the canals, which was terribly slow. It took nearly as long as bringing the cotton from America to Liverpool.

再一次，對這台新機器感興趣的是棉花製造商們。例如，將大包生棉從 Liverpool 港口運到 Manchester——大多數棉紡工場所在地——的唯一途徑是用駁船走運河，這慢得可怕。幾乎和從美洲把棉花運到 Liverpool 一樣費時。

Initially it was for the transport of raw cotton that Stephenson built a railway line between Liverpool and Manchester. The line was opened in 1830, and his famous locomotive (there was only one) was called the Rocket. At that time it was the fastest thing on wheels: it could do thirty miles per hour (50 kph).

最初，Stephenson 在 Liverpool 和 Manchester 之間建造鐵路線，就是為了運輸生棉。這條線路於一八三零年開通，他那台著名的火車頭（當時只有一台）叫做「火箭號」（Rocket）。在當時，它是輪子上最快的東西：時速可達三十英里（五十公里）。

At first this railway was only used for goods, for cotton, but soon coaches for passengers were added. The first class coaches had cushioned seats and roofs, the second class had wooden seats and no roof, and there was also a third class, no seats and no roof. Imagine what it was like in the roofless coaches on a cold rainy day - and with thick smoke enveloping the passengers!

起初這條鐵路只用來運貨、運棉花，但很快就增加了載客車廂。頭等車廂有軟墊座椅和頂篷，二等車廂有木椅但沒有頂篷，還有三等車廂，既沒有座椅也沒有頂篷。想像一下在寒冷的雨天坐在沒有頂篷的車廂裡——還有濃煙籠罩著乘客！

The success of this Liverpool-to-Manchester line proved that the steam-driven locomotive could move goods as well as passengers both cheaper and faster than anything known before.

這條 Liverpool 到 Manchester 線路的成功證明了蒸汽驅動的火車頭運送貨物和旅客都比以往任何已知的方式更便宜、更快速。

Railways now began to spread all over the country, and changed the centuries-old way of life. When people still travelled by horse-drawn coaches from Edinburgh to London the journey took about two weeks and was pretty expensive too. But with the arrival of the railway, the four hundred mile (650 km) journey only took a day. People could move cheaply and quickly from place to place. And people who had never left their town or village before, ventured far afield for little money.

鐵路現在開始遍布全國，改變了數百年來的生活方式。當人們還是乘坐馬車從 Edinburgh 到 London 時，旅途大約需要兩個星期，而且相當昂貴。但隨著鐵路的到來，這段四百英里（六百五十公里）的旅程只需一天。人們可以便宜而快速地從一個地方移動到另一個地方。那些從未離開過自己小鎮或村莊的人，花很少的錢就能遠行探險。

Soon Leonardo da Vinci's dream was to come true too - and steam-driven ships would take the place of sailing ships.

很快，Leonardo da Vinci 的夢想也將成真——蒸汽驅動的輪船將取代帆船。

At first, George Stephenson's invention found some opposition. For instance, when Bavaria was to build its first railway line, the Government asked the opinion of the Council of Doctors. And the learned medical council declared that travelling at a speed of thirty miles per hour would cause diseases of the brain.

起初，George Stephenson 的發明遇到了一些反對。例如，當 Bavaria 準備建造第一條鐵路線時，政府向醫學委員會徵求意見。而這些博學的醫學專家宣稱，以每小時三十英里的速度旅行會導致腦部疾病。

Chapter 39
The Proletarians

第三十九章
無產階級

At the time of the Industrial Revolution, there was also a great change in British agriculture, in farming. Most of the land belonged to noblemen, to lords, to the "Squire" as the peasants called him. The squire did not work the land himself - the land was "let" to "tenant farmers" who worked the land, sold what they could and paid a rent to the squire.

在工業革命時期，British 的農業也發生了巨大的變化。大部分土地屬於貴族、領主——農民稱之為「鄉紳」。鄉紳自己並不耕種土地——土地「出租」給「佃農」，佃農耕種土地、出售所能賣的，並向鄉紳繳納租金。

Such an "estate" was usually divided into three large fields. Two fields grew crops and the third was grass and weeds. The reason for this was that if you grew wheat year after year, the soil became dead and useless. So the farmers grew their wheat in every field for two years and the third year the field was left fallow, was given a rest. So the three fields were first year crop, second year crop and fallow field.

這樣一塊「莊園」通常被分為三大塊田地。兩塊種莊稼，第三塊長草和雜草。原因是如果年復一年地種小麥，土壤就會枯竭變得無用。所以農民在每塊田裡種兩年小麥，第三年就讓田地休耕、休息一下。因此三塊田地分別是：第一年作物田、第二年作物田和休耕田。

In the two planted fields each tenant farmer had his own little strip, and the third field was common grazing for their livestock, cows, goats, sheep.

在兩塊種植田裡，每個佃農有自己的小塊田地，第三塊田則是他們的牲畜——牛、羊、山羊——的公共牧場。

But this changed when the landowners wanted the fallow field to be used for new crops which enriched the soil: turnips and clover. Turnips and clover were new in Britain - they were brought from the Continent - and they replenished the soil with the nitrates that wheat takes from it.

但當地主們希望在休耕田上種植能滋養土壤的新作物——蕪菁和三葉草——時，一切就變了。蕪菁和三葉草在 Britain 是新引進的——它們從歐洲大陸傳來——能補充小麥從土壤中攫取的硝酸鹽。

The poorer tenants could not do this; to plough and look after a third field required more work than they could manage. They had no money to pay farmhands and as there was no fallow field, they could not keep animals. Thus it was that thousands of poor tenants had to leave the land, because there was no longer a livelihood for them. So the old way of farming came to an end - only a few rich tenants remained, their fields becoming bigger by taking on the abandoned ones.

較窮的佃農做不到這一點；耕種和照料第三塊田需要超出他們能力的勞動。他們沒有錢僱用農工，而且由於不再有休耕田，他們也養不了牲畜。就這樣，成千上萬的窮佃農不得不離開土地，因為那裡不再有他們的生計。舊的農耕方式走到了盡頭——只剩下少數富裕的佃農留了下來，他們接收了被遺棄的田地，使自己的農場越來越大。

Thousands of poor families came to the towns desperate to make a living, and found work there.

成千上萬的窮苦家庭湧入城鎮，拚命尋找生計，並在那裡找到了工作。

The number of cotton mills had grown and grown - the whole world was buying the new, cheap, factory-made cotton from Britain. Money came pouring into Britain, and the manufacturers built new factories from the money they made.

棉紡工場的數量不斷增長——全世界都在購買 Britain 出產的這種新型、廉價、工廠製造的棉布。金錢源源不斷地流入 Britain，製造商們用賺來的錢建造新工廠。

The more cotton mills that went up, the more workers and machines that were needed. So the machine makers, the engineering firms, prospered and grew and employed more and more people. The iron foundries where iron ore was turned into iron and steel also had to produce more, and employed more and more workers.

建起的棉紡工場越多，需要的工人和機器就越多。於是機器製造商、工程公司蓬勃發展，僱用越來越多的人。把鐵礦石煉成鐵和鋼的鑄造廠也必須增產，僱用了越來越多的工人。

Before the Industrial Revolution, let us say in the year 1750, three quarters of Britain's population lived in the country and only one quarter lived in towns, so Britain was an agricultural country at that time. A hundred years later, by 1850, the industrial cities had drawn in the larger part of the population, and Britain had become an industrial nation.

在工業革命之前，假設是一七五零年，Britain 四分之三的人口住在鄉下，只有四分之一住在城鎮，所以 Britain 當時是一個農業國家。一百年後，到了一八五零年，工業城市已經吸納了大部分人口，Britain 變成了一個工業國家。

The coming of the machines brought money pouring into Britain and it brought work to thousands, then hundreds of thousands, and then to millions, but now we must consider the conditions in which the factory workers lived, so we can see the other face, the hideous face of the Industrial Revolution.

機器的到來為 Britain 帶來了滾滾財富，也為數千人、數十萬人、然後數百萬人帶來了工作，但現在我們必須看看工廠工人的生活條件，才能看到工業革命的另一面——醜陋的一面。

Before Hargreaves made his spinning jenny, the weavers and spinners lived in their cottages in the country and although they were poor, they lived a simple, healthy life in the clear country air. Each weaver was his own master who could begin or end his work when he liked.

在 Hargreaves 製造珍妮紡紗機之前，織工和紡紗工住在鄉間的小屋裡，雖然貧窮，但在清新的鄉村空氣中過著簡單健康的生活。每個織工都是自己的主人，可以隨心所欲地開始或結束工作。

However, after the great change it was different. To get steam for the steam engines that drove the wheels, coal was burnt, and where coal was burnt there was smoke. As the cotton mills grew and spread, the number of tall chimney stacks which poured black smoke into the air until it darkened the sky also grew and spread, and to work in a cotton mill now meant to work in a town of perpetual gloom where the air was thickened by coal and cotton dust.

然而，大變革之後，一切都不同了。要讓驅動輪子的蒸汽機產生蒸汽，就要燒煤，而燒煤的地方就有煙霧。隨著棉紡工場的增長和擴展，將黑煙噴入空中直到遮天蔽日的高聳煙囪也越來越多、越來越廣，在棉紡工場工作現在意味著在一個永遠陰沉的城鎮裡工作，空氣中瀰漫著煤塵和棉絮。

When a new cotton mill went up, it would need hundreds of workers and these workers would want to live near the mill. So the builders or sometimes the mill owners bought up land as close to the mill site as possible. And on this land they built rows of houses which were planned to crowd as many people as possible, into the smallest space possible.

當一座新的棉紡工場建起來，就需要數百名工人，而這些工人會想住在工場附近。於是建築商或有時是工場主，盡可能地在離工場最近的地方買下土地。在這些土地上，他們建造了一排排房屋，設計的目的就是在最小的空間裡塞進最多的人。

The builders had a free hand; there were no rules or laws that governed how they should build, so ugly towns were built, and in them the overcrowded tenements soon became slums.

建築商完全自由發揮；沒有任何規則或法律規定他們該怎麼建造，於是醜陋的城鎮被建了起來，其中擁擠不堪的廉租屋很快變成了貧民窟。

And so, over the green hills of England, there spread a cloud of smoke which never lifted. And below the cloud there stood row upon row of the ugliest buildings ever to disgrace the world.

就這樣，在 England 翠綠的山丘之上，漫延開一片永遠不散的煙雲。煙雲之下，一排又一排世上最醜陋的建築矗立著，令人蒙羞。

The rooms in these houses had no ventilation, no water, and no lavatory. For a whole street there was one water pump at one end which was the only water supply for all needs of all the people in the street. And at the other end of the street there was a shed with a hole in the ground - that was the lavatory for the whole street. Each patch of ground between the rows of houses was used as a refuse dump and covered with heaps of rubbish and filth.

這些房屋裡的房間沒有通風、沒有自來水、沒有廁所。整條街只在一端有一座水泵，那是全街所有人所有需求的唯一水源。在街的另一端有一間棚子，地上挖了一個洞——那就是全街的廁所。房屋排列之間的每一塊空地都被用作垃圾場，堆滿了成堆的垃圾和穢物。

Inside the houses, every small room, including the cellars, contained an average of ten people. The people who lived in these conditions, hordes of ragged women, dirty children, were completely cut off from any education or culture.

在房屋內部，每間小房間，包括地下室，平均住著十個人。生活在這種條件下的人——成群衣衫襤褸的婦女、骯髒的孩子——完全與任何教育或文化隔絕。

At that time a new name was given to this class of dirty, working people, they were called "proletarians." The better class of people who did not have to live in the slums were firmly convinced that it was good for the proletarians to work endless hours in the factories - because, if they had more leisure they would only become worse.

當時，這群骯髒的勞動人民被賦予了一個新名字，他們被稱為「無產階級」（proletarians）。那些不必住在貧民窟的上等人堅定地相信，無產階級在工廠裡無休止地工作是好事——因為如果他們有更多閒暇，只會變得更糟。

In the midst of these slums there stood the giant, smoke-blackened factories, and when the workers walked to the factory, the smoke was often so thick that they had to grope their way through the darkness.

在這些貧民窟中央矗立著巨大的、被煙燻黑的工廠，工人們走去工廠時，煙霧常常濃到他們必須在黑暗中摸索前行。

Inside the factory the hot air produced by the coal furnace was thick with floating bits of cotton fibre which got into people's throats and brought on fits of coughing. In this atmosphere men, women and children from the age of five, worked six days a week from 5 am till 8 pm - fifteen hours per day, with only a half hour's break at midday.

工廠裡面，燃煤爐產生的熱空氣中瀰漫著飄浮的棉纖維碎屑，鑽進人們的喉嚨引起陣陣咳嗽。在這樣的環境中，男人、女人和五歲以上的兒童，每週工作六天，從清晨五點到晚上八點——每天十五個小時，中午只有半小時的休息。

All day long the noise of coughing accompanied the clanging and rattling of the machines. If a child could not get rid of the fibres in their throat by coughing they were given a glass containing a mixture of mustard and water. This horrible mixture made the child sick and expelled the fibres.

整天，咳嗽聲伴隨著機器的叮噹聲和嘎嘎聲。如果一個孩子無法靠咳嗽清除喉嚨裡的纖維，就會被灌一杯芥末和水的混合物。這種可怕的混合物讓孩子嘔吐，從而排出纖維。

There were no seats in the factory - there was no rest - and the foremen went round, armed with a big cane which came down mercilessly on any man, woman or child who faltered in their work.

工廠裡沒有座椅——沒有休息——工頭們拿著大棍子巡視，對任何在工作中懈怠的男人、女人或孩子都毫不留情地打下去。

And what was the reward these "proletarians" received for their work? The average pay was very little.

而這些「無產階級」工作得到的報酬是什麼呢？平均工資少得可憐。

To keep these factories going, more and more coal had to be brought up from the mines - and the working conditions in the coal mines were even worse than in the factories.

為了維持這些工廠的運轉，需要從礦井中挖出越來越多的煤——而煤礦中的工作條件比工廠還要惡劣。

In the coal mines, the digging was done by men, but for other work young children were used. In the underground tunnels children were chained to coal trucks and had to pull them. In many tunnels the ceiling was so low that the children had to crawl for miles on their hands and knees, drawing the heavy coal trucks after them.

在煤礦中，挖煤的是成年男子，但其他工作則由年幼的孩子來做。在地下坑道裡，孩子們被鏈子拴在煤車上，必須拉著煤車前行。在許多坑道中，天花板低到孩子們必須手腳並用地爬行數英里，拖著沉重的煤車。

They started work before sunrise and came out after dark so that they saw the sun only on Sundays. As they were undernourished breathed air full of coal dust, and had to do work beyond their strength, these children did not live very long. Thousands died - and those who survived were often crippled.

他們在日出前開始工作，天黑後才出來，所以只有星期天才能看到太陽。由於營養不良、呼吸著充滿煤塵的空氣、被迫從事超越體力的勞動，這些孩子活不了多久。數以千計的孩子死去——倖存的往往也落下了殘疾。

That was what the Industrial Revolution had brought to Britain. The people who owned the cotton mills, and those who owned the coal mines, grew rich and prosperous. They built themselves beautiful mansions with large parks; they had butlers, footmen, cooks, ladies' maids - a host of servants. And they regarded the inhuman conditions of the proletarians as their lot in life, just as the Romans regarded the condition of enslaved people.

這就是工業革命帶給 Britain 的。擁有棉紡工場的人和擁有煤礦的人變得富裕繁榮。他們為自己建造了帶有大片園林的華麗宅邸；他們有管家、侍從、廚師、女僕——大批僕人。他們把無產階級的非人境遇視為天經地義，就像羅馬人看待奴隸的處境一樣。

The production of cotton cloth grew from 27,000 tonnes in 1800 to 70,000 tonnes in 1820, and money came pouring in - but only into the pockets of the factory owners.

棉布的產量從一八零零年的兩萬七千噸增長到一八二零年的七萬噸，金錢滾滾而來——但只流入了工廠主的口袋。

Chapter 40
Liberty and Economics

第四十章
自由與經濟

On the one hand were the cotton manufacturers who amassed fortunes while on the other their workers lived in conditions so inhuman that one can hardly fully imagine them; and the proprietors of coal mines enjoyed every luxury while in their mines, children crawled through tunnels; all the flourishing entrepreneurs enjoyed a prosperity never known before, while hundreds of thousands of fellow human beings - men, women and children - lived as no dog, no criminal, would be allowed to live in modern Britain. If you keep this picture in mind - the life of the property owners, and the life of the proletarians who owned nothing - then you must ask: "Did these prosperous people feel no pity, no compassion? Did they not feel sorry for the unhappy proletarians? Did the prosperous people have no heart for the misery in the slums?"

一邊是積累了大量財富的棉花製造商，另一邊是他們的工人，生活在幾乎無法想像的非人條件下；煤礦主享受著一切奢華，而在他們的礦井裡，孩子們在坑道中匍匐爬行；所有蓬勃發展的企業家都享受著前所未有的繁榮，而數十萬同胞——男人、女人和孩子——生活在一種連狗、連罪犯在現代 Britain 都不被允許的境遇中。如果你記住這幅畫面——有產者的生活，和一無所有的無產階級的生活——那你一定會問：「這些富裕的人難道沒有憐憫、沒有同情心嗎？他們難道不為不幸的無產階級感到難過嗎？這些富裕的人對貧民窟的苦難難道毫無心腸嗎？」

The answer is that most of them were not cruel monsters, they were not heartless, they did feel pity and sorrow, but they thought that the misery, the poverty and squalor of the proletarians were something that could not be avoided, it was simply their lot, something that could never be changed.

答案是，他們中的大多數人並不是殘忍的怪物，他們並非鐵石心腸，他們確實感到憐憫和悲傷，但他們認為無產階級的苦難、貧窮和骯髒是無法避免的，那只不過是他們的命運，永遠不可能改變。

The prosperous people, like the cotton mill owners of Manchester, believed, above all things, in "freedom." A businessman, so they thought - must be free to buy goods at the cheapest price and to sell them at the highest price he can get. The customer, too, is free to buy or not to buy. If the businessman asks too much, the customers will stay away and not buy from him. And so, between them, the businessman and the customer come to a fair price on which they both can agree. This was called: "the free play of the Market." Let the market have a "free play" and all the goods will settle at the right price. So the businessmen believed that in business, in buying and selling, there should be freedom, otherwise there would be no business.

那些富裕的人，比如 Manchester 的棉紡工場主們，最信奉的就是「自由」。他們認為，商人必須有自由以最低價格購買商品，以最高價格出售。顧客也有自由選擇買或不買。如果商人要價太高，顧客就會離開，不從他那裡購買。這樣，商人和顧客之間就達成了雙方都能接受的公平價格。這被稱為「市場的自由運作」。讓市場「自由運作」，所有商品就會穩定在合理的價格。所以商人們相信，在商業中、在買賣中，應該有自由，否則就沒有商業。

And now we come to the working class, to the proletarians. The Manchester cotton mill owners said: "The proletarians also have something to sell: their work which means so many hours of their lives - so much energy of their bodies. That's what the proletarian who owns nothing has to sell: a certain portion of his life, a certain portion of his energy. That's what work is. Just as we sell our cotton to customers, so the proletarians sell their work to us. And they are free to sell their work at the best price they can get."

現在我們來看看工人階級，無產階級。Manchester 的棉紡工場主們說：「無產階級也有東西可賣：他們的勞動，也就是他們生命中的若干小時——他們身體的若干精力。一無所有的無產階級能出賣的就是：一部分生命、一部分精力。這就是勞動的本質。正如我們把棉布賣給顧客，無產階級把他們的勞動賣給我們。他們有自由以最好的價格出售自己的勞動。」

If a cotton manufacturer can't get a high price for his cotton, he must take a low price. If the worker can't get a high wage he must take a low one. That's the free play of the market.

如果棉花製造商無法賣到高價，就必須接受低價。如果工人無法得到高工資，就必須接受低工資。這就是市場的自由運作。

All things which can be bought and sold - cars, houses, apples, clothes - are called "commodities." And the cotton manufacturers, the coal mine proprietors, the machine makers believed quite sincerely that human work (a part of one's lifetime, of one's health and strength) was a commodity. And as other commodities found the right price by the free play of the market, so "work" found its price by the free play of the market.

所有可以買賣的東西——汽車、房屋、蘋果、衣服——都被稱為「商品」。棉花製造商、煤礦主、機器製造商真誠地相信，人類的勞動（一個人生命的一部分、健康和體力的一部分）也是一種商品。就像其他商品通過市場的自由運作找到合理的價格一樣，「勞動」也通過市場的自由運作找到它的價格。

In business if you buy a commodity you are trying to buy as cheaply as possible, you don't pay a shopkeeper more if you can get the same thing in another shop for much less.

在商業中，如果你購買一種商品，你會盡量買到最便宜的，如果在另一家店可以用低得多的價格買到同樣的東西，你不會多付給這家店主。

And so it seemed to the business owners quite right that they should buy the commodity "work" as cheaply as possible. After all, if the workers did not like it, they were free to try and get a higher price somewhere else. (Of course, they could not get a better wage anywhere.)

所以在企業主們看來，盡可能便宜地購買「勞動」這種商品是完全正確的。畢竟，如果工人不喜歡，他們可以自由地去其他地方爭取更高的報酬。（當然，他們在任何地方都無法得到更好的工資。）

So what was behind the misery of the slums, the suffering of the proletarians, was the quite sincere belief in freedom, in liberty in business, in economics.

所以，貧民窟的苦難、無產階級的痛苦背後，是對自由的真誠信仰，是對商業自由、經濟自由的真誠信仰。

We saw that putting liberty, equality, fraternity in the wrong places during the French Revolution created chaos and the massacres of the guillotine.

我們已經看到，在法國大革命期間，把自由、平等、博愛放錯了位置，造成了混亂和斷頭台的屠殺。

And now we see that by putting "liberty" into business, into economics, it produced untold misery during the Industrial Revolution. The Industrial Revolution, just like the French Revolution, created misery and suffering because people - at any rate, the business people - put "liberty" in the wrong place.

現在我們看到，把「自由」放進商業、放進經濟中，在工業革命期間造成了無以言表的苦難。工業革命就像法國大革命一樣，製造了苦難和痛苦，因為人們——至少商人們——把「自由」放錯了位置。

The business people, the cotton manufacturers, were not cruel monsters, they honestly believed in freedom - unfortunately in the wrong place. And they believed, therefore, that the terrible life of the proletarians could not be changed; if you changed it, you would interfere with "freedom."

商人們、棉花製造商們並不是殘忍的怪物，他們真誠地信仰自由——不幸的是放錯了地方。因此他們相信，無產階級可怕的生活是無法改變的；如果你改變它，就是干涉了「自由」。

And strangely enough they were confirmed in their belief by a minister of the Church of England, the Rev Thomas Malthus. Malthus wrote a book in which he said that there is never, at any time, enough food for all people in the world, and so there are always some who have to starve. He said, there is never enough cloth, never enough houses - and so some must go in rags, some must live ten or twenty to a room. There is never enough money - and so some must be poor.

而奇怪的是，一位英國國教的牧師 Thomas Malthus 牧師更加鞏固了他們的信念。Malthus 寫了一本書，書中說世界上永遠不會有足夠的食物養活所有人，所以總有一些人必須挨餓。他說，永遠沒有足夠的布料、永遠沒有足夠的房屋——所以有些人必須穿著破衣，有些人必須十個二十個人擠一間房。永遠沒有足夠的錢——所以有些人必須貧窮。

This servant of God, went on to say that it had always been so, there was always what he called "a surplus population," extra people for whom there is not enough food or clothes or houses or money. This surplus population was meant to live and die in misery, that was the law of nature, and therefore a law of God. It would be wrong to interfere with this law, it would be wrong to help this "starving surplus population" by charity, by gifts, they were condemned to hunger and misery by a law of nature. It was the duty of those who had a fair share - so said the Rev Malthus - to let the others starve.

這位上帝的僕人接著說，事情歷來如此，總是存在他所稱的「過剩人口」——多餘的人，食物、衣服、房屋或金錢都不夠分給他們。這些過剩人口注定在苦難中生死，這是自然法則，因此也是上帝的法則。干預這條法則是錯的，通過慈善、通過施捨來幫助這些「飢餓的過剩人口」是錯的，他們被自然法則判定了飢餓和苦難。Malthus 牧師說，那些擁有合理份額的人的責任——就是讓其他人餓著。

Now the wealthy classes of Britain had a clergyman's word for it that it was right, a law of nature, that the working class people should exist in misery.

現在 Britain 的富裕階層有了一位牧師為他們背書，說工人階級活在苦難中是正確的，是自然法則。

But not all the rich people fell into this very convenient trap, not all business men made the mistake of placing liberty alongside economics, not all made the mistake of believing that human work was a "commodity" to be bought and sold.

但不是所有的富人都掉進了這個非常方便的陷阱，不是所有的商人都犯了把自由與經濟並列的錯誤，不是所有人都犯了認為人類勞動是一種可以買賣的「商品」的錯誤。

It is a mistake, of course, because a day, an hour of a short human life is so precious that no money can pay for it. Not all rich people made these mistakes though. There was one man, a Welshman, who fought against these mistakes and showed by practical demonstration how wrong they were.

這當然是一個錯誤，因為短暫人生中的一天、一小時是如此珍貴，沒有金錢能夠償付。不過，並非所有的富人都犯了這些錯誤。有一個人，一個 Wales 人，他與這些錯誤作鬥爭，並以實際行動證明了它們是多麼的大錯特錯。

Chapter 41
Robert Owen

第四十一章
Robert Owen

At the time of the Industrial Revolution two new classes of people was created. On the one side there were the factory workers, the working class or the "proletarians" as they were called, and, on the other side, the owners of cotton mills, of other factories, or coal mines and iron mines, the owners of great estates, or the owners of houses which were let. All these people who owned property of one kind or another, and who made money out of this property, were called "capitalists." Capital is any money which is not used for spending, but "invested," buying something that will in time bring more money.

在工業革命時期，兩個新階級被創造出來。一邊是工廠工人，工人階級，或被稱為「無產階級」；另一邊是棉紡工場的主人、其他工廠的主人，或煤礦和鐵礦的主人、大莊園的主人，或出租房屋的房東。所有這些擁有這樣或那樣財產、並從財產中賺錢的人，被稱為「資本家」。資本就是不用於消費、而是「投資」的錢——購買某種東西，使其日後帶來更多的錢。

At the time of the Industrial Revolution Britain became divided into capitalists, middle class and working class. But it was possible for a person to make their way from the working class to the capitalists. Such a person was Robert Owen.

在工業革命時期，Britain 分裂為資本家、中產階級和工人階級。但一個人是有可能從工人階級躋身資本家行列的。Robert Owen 就是這樣一個人。

Born in 1771 in Wales, Robert Owen's family was so poor that the boy had to earn his own living as a shop assistant from the age of ten. As a shop assistant the little boy had to work from 8 am to 10 pm and the wage he got was only 10 shillings per week, which was very little. But Robert Owen had his mind on getting on in life. He saved a little money, left Wales and travelled to Manchester which was the centre of the cotton industry, and a place where you could see both the misery of the working class and the splendid life of the capitalists. Robert Owen - he was fifteen years old then - saw how money was made. He saw that one pound of raw cotton (it looks like dirty cotton wool) was worth 25 pence, but once this pound of cotton was woven and spun and had become cotton cloth it was worth £5, a difference of £4.75. And the largest part of this enormous profit went into the pockets of the man who owned the machines that did the spinning and weaving.

Robert Owen 於一七七一年出生在 Wales，家境貧寒，這個男孩從十歲起就不得不靠當店員謀生。作為店員，小男孩必須從早上八點工作到晚上十點，週薪只有十先令，少得可憐。但 Robert Owen 一心想出人頭地。他攢了一點錢，離開 Wales，前往棉紡產業的中心 Manchester——在那裡，你可以同時看到工人階級的苦難和資本家的奢華生活。當時十五歲的 Robert Owen 看到了錢是怎麼賺的。他看到一磅生棉（看起來像髒棉花）值二十五便士，但一旦這磅棉花經過紡織變成棉布，就值五英鎊，差價高達四英鎊七十五便士。而這筆巨大利潤的絕大部分，都進了擁有紡織機器的人的口袋。

And so Robert Owen, still working as a shop assistant, saved every penny he could from his wages. He denied himself any pleasure that cost money, and in five years - at the age of twenty - he bought three spinning machines, and engaged a few workers to run them. He had become a "capitalist," a manufacturer in his own right.

於是 Robert Owen 仍然做著店員的工作，從工資中節省每一分錢。他拒絕任何花錢的享樂，五年之後——二十歲時——他買了三台紡紗機，僱了幾個工人來操作。他已經成為了一個「資本家」，一個真正的製造商。

Now among the big cotton mills of Manchester, Robert Owen's little factory was very small, and although he made a fair living, he could hardly make a fortune. However, he gained a good reputation for efficiency and for honesty, and it was due to this reputation that the owner of a very large cotton mill offered him the very highly paid job of manager of his mill. Robert Owen sold his little factory and became the highly respected manager of one of the largest mills in Manchester at the age of twenty-two.

在 Manchester 眾多大型棉紡工場中，Robert Owen 的小工廠微不足道，雖然過得去，卻很難發大財。然而，他因效率高和為人誠實而贏得了良好的聲譽，正是由於這個名聲，一位大型棉紡工場的老闆給了他一份薪水優渥的工場經理職位。Robert Owen 賣掉了自己的小工廠，在二十二歲時成為 Manchester 最大工場之一備受尊敬的經理。

For a young man without education or training, Robert Owen had gone far, but there was more good fortune in store for him. At that time cotton mills also spread to Scotland and the largest Scottish cotton mills were in New Lanark on the Clyde.

對一個沒有受過教育或訓練的年輕人來說，Robert Owen 已經走得很遠了，但更大的好運還在等著他。當時棉紡工場也擴展到了 Scotland，最大的蘇格蘭棉紡工場在 Clyde 河畔的 New Lanark。

The owner of these Scottish mills in New Lanark was David Dale who had an only daughter. In the course of some business Robert Owen came from Manchester to New Lanark and met Miss Dale. They fell in love and he married her. He became first a partner (joint owner), and when Mr Dale died, owner of Scotland's largest cotton mills.

New Lanark 這些蘇格蘭工場的主人是 David Dale，他有一個獨生女。在一次商務往來中，Robert Owen 從 Manchester 來到 New Lanark，遇見了 Dale 小姐。他們相愛並結了婚。他先是成為合夥人（共同所有者），在 Dale 先生去世後，成為了 Scotland 最大棉紡工場的主人。

So far the story of Robert Owen is just a success story - the story of a young, ambitious man who had good qualities and who was extremely lucky. But there was another side to Robert Owen.

到目前為止，Robert Owen 的故事只是一個成功故事——一個年輕、有抱負、品質優良又極其幸運的人的故事。但 Robert Owen 還有另一面。

Unlike other cotton manufacturers he felt a deep concern about the miserable, inhuman conditions in which the workers lived. What could be done to help them? Pay them higher wages? That would not really make much difference. No, higher wages alone was not enough, the whole way of life should be changed. And slowly - it was not a sudden idea - slowly Robert Owen formed his plan to set up a new community that should be a model for the working class people everywhere.

與其他棉花製造商不同，他對工人們所生活的悲慘、非人的條件深感關切。能做什麼來幫助他們呢？給他們更高的工資？那其實不會有太大的改變。不，光是更高的工資還不夠，整個生活方式都應該改變。慢慢地——這不是一個突然的想法——Robert Owen 逐漸形成了他的計畫，要建立一個新的社區，為各地的工人階級做出典範。

Robert Owen started by re-building his workers' houses; in these new houses every family had two rooms - something unheard of among workers in those days. But these people were not used to "cleanliness," what could one do to make them keep the rooms clean? Owen did not want to force his workers to do this or that - he wanted their co-operation. And so the workers elected amongst themselves "inspectors" who visited all the houses regularly. They wrote into a little book which family had a clean home, and which had a dirty one. That was quite enough - for no woman could bear to be put down as a dirty housewife while her neighbour got good marks for cleanliness.

Robert Owen 首先重建了工人的住房；在這些新房子裡，每個家庭有兩間房間——在當時的工人中聞所未聞。但這些人不習慣「清潔」，怎樣才能讓他們保持房間乾淨呢？Owen 不想強迫工人做這做那——他想要他們的合作。於是工人們自己選出了「檢查員」，定期走訪所有住戶。他們在一本小冊子上記錄哪個家庭房屋乾淨，哪個髒亂。這就足夠了——因為沒有哪個女人能忍受被記為邋遢的主婦，而鄰居卻因為清潔得到好評。

In the factory, too, Robert Owen had his own way of encouraging good work. There were boards of different colours in every factory, black, blue, red, yellow, white. People who worked very badly had their names written on the black board, and the best workers on the white one. Of course, the lazy workers were soon ashamed of being on black or blue boards week after week, and changed. Thus the standard of work in Owen's factories became higher than anywhere else in the cotton industry.

在工廠裡，Robert Owen 也有自己鼓勵優良工作的辦法。每間工廠裡都有不同顏色的告示牌——黑色、藍色、紅色、黃色、白色。工作最差的人名字寫在黑色板上，最好的工人名字寫在白色板上。當然，懶惰的工人很快就為自己一週又一週地待在黑色或藍色板上感到羞愧，於是改進了。因此 Owen 工廠的工作標準比棉紡業中任何其他地方都要高。

In other places the shops where the workers bought food or clothes were run by unscrupulous shopkeepers who overcharged and cheated, but not in New Lanark. Robert Owen put up shops which bought all goods cheaply at wholesale prices and sold them without profit to the workers. These stores of Robert Owen were the beginning of the Co-operative (Co-op) Stores which, later, spread all over Britain. The Co-op movement started with Robert Owen's shops in New Lanark.

在其他地方，工人們買食物和衣服的商店由不擇手段的店主經營，他們漫天要價、欺騙顧客，但 New Lanark 不是這樣。Robert Owen 開設了商店，以批發價格低價購入所有商品，然後不加利潤地賣給工人。Robert Owen 的這些商店就是合作商店（Co-op）的開端，後來遍布整個 Britain。合作社運動始於 Robert Owen 在 New Lanark 的商店。

No one had given any thought to how a worker could live if he fell ill. But Robert Owen thought of it. Partly from the workers' money and partly from his own, he started a "sickness fund" as it was called - money that was put aside for sick workers and their families.

沒有人想過一個工人生了病該怎麼生活。但 Robert Owen 想到了。一部分從工人的錢中，一部分從他自己的錢中，他創立了一個所謂的「疾病基金」——為生病的工人及其家庭預留的錢。

But Robert Owen's special concern was the children. No child under the age of ten was allowed to work in his factories (remember that he himself had started at ten and so he did not think it wrong). But the children from ten to fifteen who did work in the factory only worked for five hours.

但 Robert Owen 最關心的是孩子們。他的工廠裡不允許十歲以下的兒童工作（記住他自己也是十歲開始的，所以他認為這並無不妥）。而十到十五歲在工廠工作的孩子，每天只工作五小時。

No one had given a thought to the education of working class children, but Robert Owen did. He built a school in New Lanark that was more than a hundred years ahead of its time.

沒有人想過工人階級孩子的教育問題，但 Robert Owen 想到了。他在 New Lanark 建了一所學校，這所學校超前了他的時代一百多年。

His idea was that a school should not only teach this or that subject, but that it should also form the children's character. To beat a child, to use a cane or strap, is not the way to build up a strong character - it produces cowards or bullies. And so in this school in New Lanark there was no corporal punishment, which was quite unusual in those days.

他的理念是，學校不應只教授這個或那個科目，還應該培養孩子們的品格。打孩子、用藤條或皮帶，不是培養堅強品格的方式——只會製造出懦夫或惡霸。因此在 New Lanark 的這所學校裡沒有體罰，這在當時是相當不尋常的。

Robert Owen also believed that music and even dancing was essential in a child's education, and so music and folk-dancing were part of the weekly lessons.

Robert Owen 還相信音樂甚至舞蹈對兒童教育是不可或缺的，所以音樂和民族舞蹈是每週課程的一部分。

New Lanark gradually became a model community of healthier and happier people due to the change in social conditions implemented by Robert Owen. Undoubtedly his workers were grateful for what he had done for them and their children.

由於 Robert Owen 實施的社會條件改革，New Lanark 逐漸成為一個更健康、更快樂的模範社區。毫無疑問，他的工人們對他為他們和他們的孩子所做的一切心存感激。

Robert Owen had given the right answer to the wrong theories, the answer that the world of industry, or economics, needs co-operation, one could say he was a hero of brotherhood, of fraternity. He, the capitalist, had worked in co-operation, in the spirit of brotherhood, with his workers.

Robert Owen 為錯誤的理論給出了正確的答案：工業界或經濟領域需要的是合作。可以說他是博愛的英雄、是兄弟情誼的英雄。他，一個資本家，以博愛的精神與他的工人們合作。

Robert Owen had hoped his model community in New Lanark would be copied by others in Britain, but he was mistaken. No other factory owner copied him. In his disappointment Robert Owen made a great mistake - he tried to set up a much larger community in America.
