This new experiment in the New World, called "New Harmony" was, unfortunately, a failure. He lost all his money, had to sell New Lanark and died in poverty in 1858.

Robert Owen 曾希望他在 New Lanark 的模範社區會被 Britain 的其他人效仿，但他錯了。沒有其他工廠主效仿他。在失望之下，Robert Owen 犯了一個大錯——他試圖在美洲建立一個規模大得多的社區。這個在新大陸上的新實驗叫做「New Harmony」，不幸的是失敗了。他失去了所有的錢，不得不賣掉 New Lanark，於一八五八年在貧困中去世。

And under the new owners, New Lanark went back to the bad old ways. Yet, Robert Owen had not lived and worked in vain. He had shown that the Industrial Revolution demanded co-operation, brotherhood, in industry, in economics.

在新業主的管理下，New Lanark 重回了過去的惡劣狀態。然而，Robert Owen 的一生和努力並非徒勞。他證明了工業革命要求在產業和經濟中實行合作與博愛。

Chapter 42
The Workers' Struggle

第四十二章
工人的抗爭

Robert Owen was in his own way, a genius. Long before that time another genius, Leonardo da Vinci, had many ideas which were far ahead of his time: in Leonardo's own time his ideas could not yet be put into practice, and it was the same with Robert Owen. In his own time people thought he was a crank and took little notice of what he did at New Lanark. However, many of Owen's ideas were eventually put into practice.

Robert Owen 以他自己的方式，是一位天才。在他很久以前，另一位天才 Leonardo da Vinci 有許多遠超時代的想法：在 Leonardo 自己的時代，他的想法還無法付諸實踐，Robert Owen 也是如此。在他自己的時代，人們認為他是個怪人，對他在 New Lanark 所做的事不太在意。然而，Owen 的許多想法最終都被付諸實行了。

His non-profit stores were the beginning of the Co-op Stores which spread all over Britain. And the "sick fund" for his workers was the beginning of the National Health Service.

他的非營利商店是合作商店的開端，後來遍布整個 Britain。他為工人設立的「疾病基金」是國民健康服務的雛形。

There was another idea of Robert Owen's which was not realized in his own time.

Robert Owen 還有另一個想法在他的時代未能實現。

To understand this idea, remember an incident from the early days of the locomotive. Richard Trevithick had built a railway for an iron mine. But the workers protested against it, because it put the driver of horse-drawn carts out of work. And, since all the workers stood together in this matter, the owner had to give in and the railway was removed.

要理解這個想法，請回想火車頭早期的一件事。Richard Trevithick 為一座鐵礦建了一條鐵路。但工人們抗議，因為它使趕馬車的人失業了。由於所有工人在這件事上團結一致，礦主不得不讓步，鐵路被拆除了。

On their own, workers were quite powerless, they were at the mercy of the capitalist, the factory owner. But whenever the workers of a factory or a mine acted together they had power, they could force the owner to take notice of their wishes.

工人們單打獨鬥是完全無力的，他們任憑資本家、工廠主擺布。但每當一家工廠或一座礦井的工人共同行動時，他們就有了力量，能迫使老闆注意到他們的願望。

The incident with the railway in the iron mine was one of many which took place in cotton mills, steel works, coal mines. From all these incidents the workers learnt the lesson: that only by standing together, by acting in union could they hope to improve the terrible conditions in which they lived.

鐵礦鐵路事件只是發生在棉紡工場、鋼鐵廠、煤礦中許多類似事件之一。從所有這些事件中，工人們學到了教訓：只有團結一致、共同行動，才能希望改善他們生活中可怕的條件。

And so the workers of one mine, of one cotton mill, or of one steel works, joined together and formed what they called "unions." But these little unions of a single cotton mill or a single coal mine had neither much power nor much money. Regarding small matters they could persuade or force a manufacturer to take notice of the workers' wishes, but when it came to important matters, like higher wages or better living-conditions, the little unions could do nothing. If his workers made a nuisance of themselves, the owner could always sack them, send them away and get new workers from the crowded slums. So the small unions of each single factory or mine could do nothing towards a real improvement in the conditions of the workers.

於是一座礦井、一家棉紡工場或一家鋼鐵廠的工人們聯合起來，組成了他們所說的「工會」（unions）。但這些單一棉紡工場或單一煤礦的小型工會既沒有多少權力，也沒有多少資金。在小事情上，他們能說服或迫使製造商注意工人們的願望，但涉及重要事務，如更高的工資或更好的生活條件，小型工會就無能為力了。如果工人們令老闆不耐煩，老闆隨時可以解僱他們、趕走他們，從擁擠的貧民窟中找來新工人。所以各個工廠或礦井的小型工會根本無法真正改善工人的境遇。

And now we come back to Robert Owen who was so concerned with the terrible conditions of the workers. It was his idea that all the small unions of the cotton mills should co-operate and form one large union, the Trade Union for all the cotton workers. And all the small unions of the coal mines should co-operate and work together in one great trade union of all coal miners - and so on.

現在我們回到 Robert Owen，他如此關心工人們可怕的處境。他的想法是，所有棉紡工場的小型工會應該合作，組成一個大型工會——所有棉紡工人的工會。所有煤礦的小型工會也應該合作，聯合成一個所有煤礦工人的大型工會——以此類推。

Such a trade union was much more powerful than the smaller ones that had gone before. If a mill owner sacked all his workers he could not get any other, for the trade union forbade its members to work for that owner.

這樣的工會比以前的小型工會強大得多。如果一個工場主解僱了所有工人，他也找不到其他工人，因為工會禁止其成員為那個老闆工作。

The trade unions, which became very powerful organizations, were the idea of Robert Owen who, even though he was a capitalist himself, realized that co-operation and brotherhood is the right principle in economics.

工會後來成為了非常強大的組織，而這正是 Robert Owen 的構想。儘管他自己就是一個資本家，他卻認識到合作與博愛才是經濟領域正確的原則。

The workers took to this idea, and every small union of a single factory became a branch of the great national trade union. But at this stage the Government stepped in and made a law forbidding trade unions.

工人們接受了這個想法，每個單一工廠的小型工會都成為全國性大型工會的一個分支。但到了這個階段，政府介入了，制定了一項禁止工會的法律。

In those days not every person in Britain could vote at election times, only the people who owned property: a house, a shop, a farm, a factory. If you didn't even own the house you lived in - like the workers - you had no voting right. And whatever government was elected, was on the side of the property owners, not on the side of the workers who could not even vote.

在那個年代，不是 Britain 的每個人都能在選舉時投票，只有擁有財產的人才可以：房屋、商店、農場、工廠。如果你連住的房子都不是自己的——像工人們一樣——你就沒有投票權。而無論選出哪個政府，都是站在有產者一邊的，而不是站在連投票權都沒有的工人一邊。

The trade unions would have given power to the working class, and the Government would not stand for this. And so all unions were forbidden by law and, for the time being, Robert Owen's idea came to nothing.

工會本來可以賦予工人階級權力，而政府不願容忍這種情況。於是所有工會都被法律禁止了，Robert Owen 的構想暫時化為泡影。

In 1815 when Napoleon was finally defeated at Waterloo, Britain could look forward to a period of peace. But to the cotton workers, peace brought only worse misery than before. During the war with Napoleon the British Army and Navy had needed hundreds of thousands of uniforms, and the cotton industry had flourished. The mills employed as many people as they could get and they had even paid them a little more than usual. But as soon as the war was over, there was no longer any need for uniforms. The demand reduced their production, and hundreds of thousands of cotton workers were sacked - they were no longer wanted. There was no pay for anybody out of work, and if the unemployed cotton workers starved to death then, as the Rev Malthus had said, it was simply a law of nature; sad, but it could not be helped.

一八一五年，Napoleon 在 Waterloo 最終被擊敗，Britain 迎來了和平時期。但對棉紡工人而言，和平帶來的只是比以前更深的苦難。在與 Napoleon 的戰爭期間，英國陸軍和海軍需要數十萬套軍服，棉紡業蓬勃發展。工場盡可能多地僱用工人，甚至比平時多付了一點工資。但戰爭一結束，就不再需要軍服了。需求減少使生產萎縮，數十萬棉紡工人被解僱——他們不再被需要了。失業者沒有任何救濟金，如果失業的棉紡工人餓死了，那麼正如 Malthus 牧師所說，那不過是自然法則；令人悲傷，但無能為力。

But even the workers still employed in the cotton mills suffered for now they were paid much less than before. If a man said that he could not live on the reduced wage, the answer was that there were thousands willing to work for even less. But while the wages dropped the food prices went up. And so the misery, the hunger, the suffering of the cotton workers was worse than it had ever been before.

即使仍在棉紡工場工作的工人也在受苦，因為現在他們的工資比以前少了很多。如果一個人說他靠減少後的工資活不下去，回答是：有成千上萬的人願意以更低的工資工作。然而工資在下降，食物價格卻在上漲。因此，棉紡工人的苦難、飢餓和痛苦比以往任何時候都更加嚴重。

It is no wonder that some stood up and preached to the crowds of ragged and starving men and women, that only an armed rising, a revolution like the French Revolution, could help them.

難怪有人站出來向衣衫襤褸、飢腸轆轆的男男女女宣講，只有武裝起義——一場像法國大革命那樣的革命——才能拯救他們。

And so on August 16, 1819, the cotton workers of Manchester held a great protest meeting at St Peter's Field, just outside Manchester. About eighty thousand people, men and women came: they had no weapons, but they marched to the meeting in columns of five, like soldiers, to the tune of drums and bugles, and they carried the red, white and blue banners of the French Revolution.

於是，一八一九年八月十六日，Manchester 的棉紡工人在 Manchester 郊外的 St Peter's Field 舉行了一場盛大的抗議集會。大約八萬人前來，有男有女：他們沒有武器，但他們五人一列、像士兵一樣在鼓聲和號角聲中走向集會地點，舉著法國大革命的紅白藍三色旗幟。

The vast numbers of the demonstrators, and their menacing looks terrified the well-to-do shopkeepers and all the wealthy citizens of Manchester who demanded protection. And so a cavalry regiment was sent to keep law and order.

示威者的龐大人數和威脅的面孔嚇壞了富裕的店主和 Manchester 所有有錢的市民，他們要求得到保護。於是一個騎兵團被派去維持秩序。

When the red-coated soldiers arrived at St Peter's Field, the crowd of cotton workers remained quite orderly, except for shouting some abuse. But then one cotton worker mounted a platform to make a speech.

當身穿紅色軍服的士兵抵達 St Peter's Field 時，棉紡工人的人群相當有序，只是喊了一些辱罵的話。但接著有一個棉紡工人登上了講台準備演說。

At that moment the officer in charge of the soldiers gave the order: Arrest this man! And the line of red coats drew their swords and rode into the crowd. A great roar of anger rose from the people, they tried to stop the horsemen by clutching at bridles and stirrups, and the soldiers hit out with their swords. They rode down people who barred the way. And then the crowd panicked. People tried to run away and in the rush hundreds were trampled down. When the field was cleared, it was littered with the bodies of dead and injured people.

就在那一刻，指揮士兵的軍官下令：逮捕此人！一排紅衣兵拔出軍刀衝進人群。人群中爆發出一陣憤怒的怒吼，他們試圖抓住韁繩和馬鐙來阻止騎兵，士兵們用劍亂砍。他們騎馬踩踏擋路的人。然後人群陷入恐慌。人們試圖逃跑，在混亂中數百人被踩倒。當場地清空時，遍地都是死傷者的屍體。

This was the Massacre of Peterloo, as it was called by the workers who compared it with bitter humour to Waterloo. But this terrible, shameful event did one thing: it roused the conscience of the British people. Even the wealthy landowners and business people realized now that the living conditions of the workers had to be changed. And gradually laws came which did away with the worst evils of the Industrial Revolution. In 1824 trade unions were made legal, and in 1833 child labour was reduced to ten hours a day.

這就是「Peterloo 屠殺」，工人們以苦澀的幽默將其與 Waterloo 相提並論。但這個可怕的、可恥的事件做到了一件事：它喚醒了英國人民的良知。即使是富有的地主和商人們現在也意識到，工人的生活條件必須改變。漸漸地，法律出台了，消除了工業革命最惡劣的弊端。一八二四年工會被合法化，一八三三年童工工時被縮減為每天十小時。

In 1845, around that time when the English Parliament was very slowly and hesitatingly improving things for the workers, Karl Marx, a German, arrived in England. Even then, living conditions in the workers' slums were still terrible. And it was with these conditions before him that Karl Marx wrote Das Kapital, a book that was to make history. Marx preached that only a ruthless struggle between the classes - between the proletarians and the capitalists - could in the end, after the victory of the workers, produce a new society, a society in which all the good things would be shared fairly by all. This new society in which all property, houses, factories, farms would be "common property" and not owned by capitalists, he called "Communist Society."

一八四五年前後，當英國議會非常緩慢而猶豫地為工人改善狀況時，一個德國人 Karl Marx 來到了 England。即使在那時，工人貧民窟的生活條件仍然十分可怕。正是面對這些狀況，Karl Marx 寫出了《資本論》（Das Kapital），一本將改變歷史的書。Marx 宣揚只有階級之間的殘酷鬥爭——無產階級與資本家之間的鬥爭——才能在工人勝利之後，最終產生一個新社會，一個所有好東西被所有人公平分享的社會。這個所有財產、房屋、工廠、農場都成為「公共財產」而不由資本家擁有的新社會，他稱之為「共產主義社會」。

With this book which taught the class struggle and the future Communist society, Karl Marx became the founder of Communism.

憑藉這本宣揚階級鬥爭和未來共產主義社會的書，Karl Marx 成為了共產主義的創始人。

If Britain had followed the example of Robert Owen, there would have been no Massacre of Peterloo, no class war, but co-operation. But the property-owning classes of Britain believed too long in liberty in the wrong place; they believed too long in the ideas of the Rev Malthus - that the surplus population was doomed to suffer - and so instead of Robert Owen's ideas, it was Karl Marx's that spread in the world. And this led to the Communist states like Russia, China and the terrible division of the world in the second half of the twentieth century.

如果 Britain 效仿了 Robert Owen 的榜樣，就不會有 Peterloo 屠殺、不會有階級戰爭，而會有合作。但 Britain 的有產階級太長時間信奉放錯了位置的自由；他們太長時間相信 Malthus 牧師的理論——過剩人口注定受苦——因此傳遍世界的不是 Robert Owen 的思想，而是 Karl Marx 的思想。這導致了像 Russia、China 這樣的共產主義國家，以及二十世紀下半葉世界的可怕分裂。

It all started with the Industrial Revolution.

這一切都始於工業革命。

Chapter 43
Garibaldi: the Early Years

第四十三章
Garibaldi：早年歲月

We have looked at the events which made Britain a world power in the nineteenth century. At the same time this great and wealthy nation had a working class that lived in misery because the ruling classes had no understanding of the idea of brotherhood, of co-operation in economics.

我們已經看了讓 Britain 成為十九世紀世界強國的那些事件。與此同時，這個偉大而富裕的國家有一個生活在苦難中的工人階級，因為統治階層不理解博愛的理念、不理解經濟中合作的精神。

Now we come to heroes of freedom, of liberty. For this we look at other countries at the time when Britain was going through the Industrial Revolution.

現在我們來談談自由的英雄。為此我們看看 Britain 經歷工業革命時其他國家的情況。

In other parts of Europe, such as Italy, there came another kind of revolution, a revolution more concerned with liberty than with fraternity. At that time Italy was not just one country, but was divided into separate states, each with its own ruler. In the South there was the Kingdom of Naples ruled by a Spanish Prince. There was the whole North of Italy which was not independent at all but was ruled by Austria. One part, called Piedmont had an Italian King, and another part was ruled by the Pope in Rome. Italy was broken up like a jigsaw puzzle.

在 Europe 的其他地方，例如 Italy，出現了另一種革命，一場更關乎自由而非博愛的革命。當時的 Italy 不是一個統一的國家，而是被分割成各自獨立的邦國，每個邦國都有自己的統治者。在南方是由一位西班牙王子統治的 Naples 王國。整個北部 Italy 根本不是獨立的，而是被 Austria 統治。有一部分叫做 Piedmont，有一位義大利國王，另一部分則由 Rome 的教宗統治。Italy 像一塊拼圖一樣被拆散了。

But, after the Napoleonic Wars, especially amongst the young, there grew a great desire, a great longing, to be one nation, under one government. You can imagine that this was not to the liking of the rulers of each state. The Emperor of Austria did not want to lose his part of Northern Italy, the King of Piedmont did not want to give up his throne, and so the young men who spoke openly of a united Italy were arrested and thrown into prison.

但在拿破崙戰爭之後，特別是在年輕人中間，萌生了一個巨大的渴望——成為一個國家、擁有一個政府。你可以想像這不合各邦國統治者的心意。Austria 的皇帝不想失去北 Italy，Piedmont 的國王不想放棄他的王位，所以那些公開談論統一 Italy 的年輕人被逮捕並投入監獄。

Some of the young hot-heads still continued to meet secretly. But as they wrote each other letters about their hopes for a united Italy, the oppression became worse. No one was allowed to give a party or hold a meeting without permission by the police. Every letter sent by post was opened by police officers and if it contained dangerous ideas the writer of the letter was arrested and sent to prison for years. No newspaper and no book could be published that contained any "dangerous" thoughts, or that complained about the oppression. Italy became a land without freedom.

一些年輕的熱血青年仍然繼續秘密聚會。但當他們互相通信談論統一 Italy 的希望時，壓迫變得更加嚴酷。沒有人被允許在未經警察許可的情況下舉辦聚會或集會。每封寄出的信都被警察拆開檢查，如果其中包含危險思想，寫信的人就會被逮捕並被判入獄多年。任何報紙和書籍如果包含任何「危險」思想，或抱怨壓迫，都不允許出版。Italy 成了一個沒有自由的國度。

Some young Italians fled to other countries, to France, to Britain, and there they plotted and planned for a free and united Italy. They wrote books which were then smuggled into Italy and passed from hand to hand. All this helped the cause of freedom, it kept the hope for better times alive in the hearts of the people, but it was not enough. What was needed was a man who could lead them into battle, a fighter for freedom. Such a man was Guiseppe Garibaldi (1807-82).

一些年輕的義大利人逃到其他國家，去了 France，去了 Britain，在那裡他們為一個自由統一的 Italy 密謀策劃。他們寫的書被走私進入 Italy，在人們手中傳閱。所有這些都有助於自由的事業，讓人們心中對美好未來的希望不滅，但這還不夠。需要的是一個能帶領他們上戰場的人，一個自由的鬥士。這樣的人就是 Guiseppe Garibaldi（一八零七至一八八二年）。

Garibaldi's father was a sailor, a simple man who had only one ambition: that his only son should have a good education and become something better than a sailor. But young Garibaldi was not interested in books - he wanted to go to sea. His father would not hear of it. So, at the age of fifteen, Garibaldi persuaded some other boys to run away with him. They stole a small sailing boat and sailed away. However, at the father's request, a coastguard vessel sailed after them and brought the youngsters back.

Garibaldi 的父親是一個水手，一個淳樸的人，只有一個願望：讓獨子受到良好的教育，成為比水手更好的人。但年輕的 Garibaldi 對書本不感興趣——他想去航海。父親不肯答應。於是在十五歲那年，Garibaldi 說服了其他幾個男孩跟他一起逃跑。他們偷了一艘小帆船揚帆而去。然而，應父親的請求，一艘海岸巡邏船追了上去，把這些少年帶了回來。

This little event shows two things about Garibaldi: he was head-strong and he was a leader. In any case, the father realized that such a boy would never make a good lawyer or doctor, and let him go to sea.

這件小事揭示了 Garibaldi 的兩個特點：他固執己見，而且他是一個領袖。無論如何，父親意識到這樣的男孩永遠不會成為一個好律師或好醫生，於是讓他出海去了。

It was on his sailing voyages that at Marseilles, in France, Garibaldi met Italians who had fled from their homeland to work for the revolution, and he became an enthusiastic member of this group of rebels.

正是在他的航海旅途中，在 France 的 Marseilles，Garibaldi 遇到了為革命而逃離祖國的義大利人，他成為了這群反叛者中一個熱情的成員。

As a sailor, Garibaldi had great opportunities to work for the revolution. When his ship came to an Italian port he talked to sailors and fishermen and tried to win them over to the idea of rising against their rulers to free and unite Italy. On one occasion the police discovered what was going on, and although Garibaldi escaped, he was proclaimed a traitor, condemned to death and a reward was offered for his capture.

作為一個水手，Garibaldi 有很好的機會為革命工作。每當他的船抵達一個義大利港口，他就跟水手和漁民交談，試圖說服他們響應起義、反抗統治者、解放和統一 Italy 的理念。有一次警察發現了他的活動，雖然 Garibaldi 逃脫了，但他被宣布為叛國者，被判處死刑，並懸賞捉拿。

As Italy was no longer safe for Garibaldi, he embarked on a ship sailing to Brazil, to Rio de Janeiro. At this time Brazil was in the throes of a revolution, the people of one province had risen against the Government. Garibaldi immediately joined the rebels - and for the next six years fought against the Government on land and sea.

由於 Italy 對 Garibaldi 來說不再安全，他搭上了一艘開往 Brazil 的 Rio de Janeiro 的船。當時 Brazil 正處於一場革命的劇痛之中，一個省的人民起而反抗政府。Garibaldi 立刻加入了叛軍——在接下來的六年裡，在陸地和海上與政府軍作戰。

On one occasion he was taken prisoner, but after a few weeks some people who were secretly on his side helped him to escape. However, he was unlucky; he was caught again before he had gone far. The officer in charge of the prisoners was furious: "Who are the men who helped you to escape?" he shouted. Garibaldi refused to betray his friends. He was beaten with sticks and canes, but still gave no answer. Then the officer tried a worse torture. At his order Garibaldi was hung up by his hands from a beam. The excruciating pain in his arms made Garibaldi faint, but he did not give away his friends. He was taken down and thrown into his cell. Two weeks later he escaped again - and this time he got away.

有一次他被俘虜了，但幾週後一些暗中支持他的人幫他逃走了。然而他運氣不好，還沒走遠就再次被抓。負責看管囚犯的軍官勃然大怒：「誰幫你逃跑的？」他吼道。Garibaldi 拒絕出賣朋友。他被棍棒抽打，但仍不吐一個字。然後軍官嘗試了更殘酷的刑罰。在他的命令下，Garibaldi 被雙手吊在一根橫樑上。手臂劇烈的疼痛使 Garibaldi 昏了過去，但他始終沒有供出朋友。他被放下來扔進牢房。兩週後他再次逃脫——這一次他成功了。

He continued fighting on the side of the rebels and was given command of a ship. One day he was on deck of this ship, watching the coast through a telescope. He saw a big house and on the balcony there stood a young woman. He could see her quite clearly through his telescope, and as soon as he saw her he said to himself: "This is the woman I am going to marry."

他繼續站在叛軍一方作戰，並被任命指揮一艘船。有一天他在甲板上用望遠鏡觀察海岸。他看到一座大房子，陽台上站著一個年輕女子。透過望遠鏡他看得很清楚，看到她的那一刻他對自己說：「這就是我要娶的女人。」

At his order the ship stopped. A boat was lowered and Garibaldi rowed ashore. He searched everywhere for the house he had seen through the telescope, but could not find it. He was just about to give up when he met with another rebel officer he knew who said: "I am just about to visit friends who have a house nearby, come with me, they will be pleased to meet you."

他下令停船。一艘小船放下水，Garibaldi 划船上了岸。他到處尋找透過望遠鏡看到的那座房子，但找不到。他正要放棄時，遇到了一個他認識的叛軍軍官，軍官說：「我正要去拜訪附近有房子的朋友，跟我來，他們會很高興見到你。」

Garibaldi accepted the invitation and accompanied the officer - and when they came to the house, the first person he saw was the young woman he had seen through the telescope. For a full minute Garibaldi and the woman looked at each other without saying a word. As they both said later, they felt as if they were not meeting for the first time but had known each other a long, long time ago. At last Garibaldi found his voice and his first words to this woman - on whom he had set eyes only that morning - were: "You must become my wife."

Garibaldi 接受了邀請，跟著軍官一起去——當他們來到那座房子時，他看到的第一個人就是他透過望遠鏡看到的那位年輕女子。整整一分鐘，Garibaldi 和那位女子互相凝視，一句話也沒有說。正如他們後來都說的，他們覺得彷彿不是第一次見面，而是在很久很久以前就認識了。最後 Garibaldi 終於找到了聲音，他對這個他不過是那天早上才看到的女子說出的第一句話是：「你必須成為我的妻子。」

The woman answered only with a nod and a smile. Thus began their great romance.

那個女子只以點頭和微笑回應。他們偉大的愛情就此開始。

The woman's name was Anita Ribera; she was only eighteen and her father had promised her to a man she did not love. The man she now saw before her, Garibaldi was already famous for his daring; he had a head like a lion, with flowing fair hair, a beard the colour of gold, and eyes of deep blue. He was tall and strong and looked every inch what he was: a reckless adventurer. Anita knew, from the moment of this first encounter, that she would marry this man and no other, but that her father would never consent to her marrying a foreign adventurer.

這位女子名叫 Anita Ribera；她只有十八歲，父親已經把她許配給了一個她不愛的男人。她眼前的這個人，Garibaldi 已經因為他的大膽而聞名；他有一顆獅子般的頭顱，飄逸的金色頭髮，金色的鬍鬚，深藍色的眼睛。他高大強壯，從頭到腳都像他本人：一個不顧一切的冒險家。Anita 從第一次相遇的那一刻就知道，她會嫁給這個人而不是別人，但她的父親永遠不會同意她嫁給一個外國冒險家。

Shortly after this strange first meeting, Anita eloped with Garibaldi and married him. From then onwards they shared all the dangers and hardships of a life that had more than its fair share of both.

在這次奇妙的初遇之後不久，Anita 與 Garibaldi 私奔並結了婚。從那時起，他們共同分擔了一生中所有的危險和磨難——而他們這一生中的危險和磨難實在太多了。

In one battle, the rebels for whom Garibaldi fought were defeated and in the chaos of fleeing troops, Anita was separated from her husband and taken prisoner. But she escaped, managed to lasso a horse and rode sixty miles (100 km) through wild country, alone and without food. Twice she had to swim wide rivers by holding on to the horse's mane, but after four days she reached safety and rejoined her jubilant husband.

在一場戰鬥中，Garibaldi 所效力的叛軍被擊敗了，在潰逃的混亂中，Anita 與丈夫失散並被俘。但她逃脫了，設法套住了一匹馬，獨自一人、沒有食物地騎了六十英里（一百公里），穿越荒野。她兩次不得不抓著馬鬃游過寬闊的河流，但四天後她到達了安全地帶，與欣喜若狂的丈夫重逢。

In another battle Garibaldi was badly wounded and left for dead on the battlefield. When the news of his death was brought to Anita she would not believe it. She said: "My heart would tell me if he were dead, but my heart knows he is still alive."

在另一場戰鬥中，Garibaldi 身負重傷，被遺棄在戰場上等死。當他陣亡的消息傳到 Anita 那裡時，她不肯相信。她說：「如果他死了，我的心會告訴我，但我的心知道他還活著。」

It was already night when they brought her the news, but she went out into the darkness with a little oil lamp. She went to the battlefield that was covered with hundreds of bodies. And there, alone in the night, she went from corpse to corpse, shining her lamp at the still faces; for hours she stumbled amongst the dead until she found her husband. He was covered with blood, unconscious, but his heart was still beating. She dressed his wounds, then she went to fetch help and for weeks she nursed him back to life.

消息傳來時已是夜晚，但她帶著一盞小油燈走進了黑暗。她來到佈滿了數百具屍體的戰場。在那裡，獨自一人在夜色中，她從一具屍體走到另一具，用燈照著那些靜止的面孔；她在死者中間跌跌撞撞地走了幾個小時，直到找到了丈夫。他渾身是血，昏迷不醒，但心臟仍在跳動。她為他包紮傷口，然後去求援，用了好幾個星期的時間將他護理回生命。

In the midst of these constant dangers their first child was born. The baby, a boy, was only twelve days old when the rebels suffered a great defeat and Garibaldi and his family had to flee into the Brazilian jungle. It was the rainy season, for weeks they lived in the heavy downpour, soaked to the skin, without proper food, plagued by insects, in constant danger from jungle beasts and snakes as well as enemy troops, and always in fear that the baby might die. But they and the baby survived and escaped.

在這持續不斷的危險中，他們的第一個孩子出生了。嬰兒是個男孩，才出生十二天，叛軍就遭受了一場大敗，Garibaldi 和他的家人不得不逃進 Brazil 的叢林。當時正值雨季，他們在大雨中生活了好幾個星期，全身濕透，沒有像樣的食物，飽受昆蟲侵擾，時刻面臨叢林野獸和毒蛇以及敵軍的危險，始終擔心嬰兒可能會死去。但他們和嬰兒都活了下來，成功逃脫。

Garibaldi's time in South America prepared him for the real task that was still ahead, the task of leading a revolution in Italy against the tyrants who kept the country divided and the people oppressed.

Garibaldi 在南美洲的歲月為他真正的使命做好了準備——領導 Italy 的一場革命，對抗那些讓國家四分五裂、人民受壓迫的暴君。

Chapter 44
Garibaldi and the Unification of Italy

第四十四章
Garibaldi 與義大利統一

Before continuing with Garibaldi's biography we must look at conditions in Europe in the first half of the nineteenth century. After the French Revolution all the rulers in Europe, kings, emperors, tsars, feared that these dangerous ideas of liberty, equality and fraternity, would spread to their own lands and that they, too, would lose their thrones and even their lives. And so they all took measures to keep their subjects quiet by instilling fear in them. The oppression in Italy was similar in France, in Germany, in Austria, in Russia. Speaking or writing about freedom was enough to send a person to prison. The police were not there to protect the people but to arrest and imprison and execute anybody who was suspected of harbouring dangerous ideas. Britain was the only country where people could speak their mind. Elsewhere in Europe there was neither free speech nor freedom to write or print anything that was not to the liking of the monarchs.

在繼續 Garibaldi 的傳記之前，我們必須看看十九世紀上半葉 Europe 的狀況。法國大革命之後，Europe 所有的統治者——國王、皇帝、沙皇——都害怕自由、平等、博愛這些危險的思想會傳播到他們自己的領土，他們也會失去王位甚至生命。於是他們都採取措施，通過灌輸恐懼來讓臣民安靜。Italy 的壓迫在 France、Germany、Austria、Russia 也同樣存在。談論或書寫自由就足以把一個人送進監獄。警察的存在不是為了保護人民，而是為了逮捕、監禁和處決任何被懷疑懷有危險思想的人。Britain 是唯一一個人們可以暢所欲言的國家。在 Europe 的其他地方，既沒有言論自由，也沒有書寫或印刷任何不合君主心意之物的自由。

But oppression, police and persecution cannot stop ideas. It has never worked in the long run; only for a while. In Europe it worked for quite a while, until 1848. The year 1848 is one of the years in history which should be written in red - it was a year of revolutions.

但壓迫、警察和迫害阻止不了思想。從長遠來看，這從未奏效過；只能維持一時。在 Europe，它維持了相當長一段時間，直到一八四八年。一八四八年是歷史上應該用紅字書寫的年份之一——這是革命之年。

It all started in France. In February 1848 the French revolted against King Louis Philippe (a relative of Louis XVI) and he fled to England. And the success of this uprising sparked revolutions all over Europe; in Vienna the students led a revolution against Ferdinand, Emperor of Austria, but they were unlucky, after heroic fighting they were overpowered by troops and many students were executed. In Germany, too, a revolution broke out, but was quelled by the armed forces.

一切始於 France。一八四八年二月，法國人起來反抗國王 Louis Philippe（Louis XVI 的親戚），他逃到了 England。這次起義的成功在整個 Europe 引發了革命；在 Vienna，學生們領導了一場反對 Austria 皇帝 Ferdinand 的革命，但他們運氣不好，經過英勇的戰鬥後被軍隊鎮壓，許多學生被處決。在 Germany 也爆發了革命，但被武裝力量平息了。

And now we come to Italy. The North of Italy was a part of the Austrian Empire, but against the wishes of the Italian people. And in this year of revolutions, 1848, the people of Northern Italy rose in rebellion against the Austrians.

現在我們來看 Italy。北 Italy 是 Austria 帝國的一部分，但這違背了義大利人民的意願。在這個革命之年——一八四八年，北 Italy 的人民起而反抗 Austria 人。

What about the rest of Italy? There was one kingdom, the Kingdom of Piedmont, where the King, Charles Albert, rather unexpectedly declared himself for the rebels and willing to fight on their side for a free and united Italy, and promised to give it a parliament as Britain had.

Italy 其他地方呢？有一個王國——Piedmont 王國——那裡的國王 Charles Albert 出人意料地宣布支持叛軍，願意站在他們一邊為自由統一的 Italy 而戰，並承諾像 Britain 一樣給予 Italy 一個議會。

Thus we can return to Garibaldi. With a revolution in Italy raging, and a king siding with the rebels, nothing could have kept him and faithful Anita in South America. Leaving the children with relatives in France, they arrived in Italy full of hope to see the country liberated and united in one nation.

因此我們可以回到 Garibaldi。Italy 革命如火如荼，一位國王站在了叛軍一邊，沒有任何東西能把他和忠誠的 Anita 留在南美洲。他們把孩子們留給在 France 的親戚，滿懷希望地抵達 Italy，盼望看到國家被解放並統一為一個民族。

But Garibaldi's hopes and the hopes of the Italian people were bitterly disappointed. The Emperor of Austria, having successfully quashed the students' revolution in Vienna, now raised a large army which came pouring down over the Alps into Northern Italy and crushed the ill-trained and ill-armed Italian rebels. And the King of Piedmont quickly gave in made peace.

但 Garibaldi 的希望和義大利人民的希望被殘酷地粉碎了。Austria 皇帝在成功鎮壓了 Vienna 的學生革命之後，現在調集了一支大軍翻越 Alps 山脈湧入北 Italy，粉碎了訓練不足、裝備低劣的義大利叛軍。Piedmont 國王很快就投降求和了。

And Garibaldi? He and Anita with a small group of faithful followers were left in the lurch. The countryside, the cities in Austrian hands, and the Austrian soldiers were out in force, hunting for that dangerous rebel Garibaldi. There was only one hope for the little group of rebels - to march as fast as they could to the coast and escape on a ship.

那 Garibaldi 呢？他和 Anita 以及一小群忠誠的追隨者被拋棄了。鄉野、城市都在 Austria 人手中，Austria 士兵傾巢而出，搜捕那個危險的叛亂者 Garibaldi。這小群叛軍唯一的希望就是盡快趕到海岸，搭船逃走。

And march they did - mile after mile, without rest, onwards before the Austrians could catch up with them. But the hardship of these marches broke Anita's health; she marched bravely on but became weaker and weaker.

他們開始了急行軍——一英里又一英里，不眠不休地前進，趕在 Austria 人追上之前。但這些急行軍的艱辛摧毀了 Anita 的健康；她勇敢地繼續行走，但越來越虛弱。

At long last they reached the coast and found fishermen willing to help them. At night the little band embarked in half a dozen boats and left the shore. But, to their misfortune, it was a bright moonlit night and as they passed a little promontory, Austrian guns stationed there opened fire. Only one boat carrying Garibaldi, Anita and six men, escaped. All other boats were sunk. The single boat returned to the shore and the survivors scattered in all directions, only one man remained with Garibaldi and Anita. By this time Anita could no longer walk and the two men carried her until they reached a farmhouse. Fortunately, the farmer was an Italian patriot and admirer of Garibaldi. He kept them hidden from the Austrians. They had caught the other survivors and shot them but they still hunted for Garibaldi. They never found him. Anita had gone through too much hardship and, in spite of every care, she died on this farm. It was the only time that Garibaldi broke down and wept.

他們終於到達了海岸，找到了願意幫助他們的漁民。在夜色中，這小隊人馬分乘六艘小船離開了海岸。但不幸的是，那是一個月光明亮的夜晚，當他們經過一個小海岬時，駐紮在那裡的 Austria 大砲開火了。只有一艘載著 Garibaldi、Anita 和六個人的船逃脫了。其他所有船都被擊沉。這唯一的船返回岸邊，倖存者四散逃逸，只有一個人留在 Garibaldi 和 Anita 身邊。此時 Anita 已經無法行走，兩個男人輪流抬著她，直到他們到達一座農舍。幸運的是，這個農夫是一位義大利愛國者，也是 Garibaldi 的崇拜者。他把他們藏了起來，躲避 Austria 人。Austria 人抓住了其他倖存者並槍斃了他們，但仍在搜捕 Garibaldi。他們始終沒有找到他。Anita 經歷了太多的磨難，儘管受到了一切照料，她還是在這座農場去世了。這是 Garibaldi 唯一一次崩潰痛哭的時刻。

But he could not spare much time for sorrow - he could not even stay to see Anita buried - for the Austrians were still seeking for him and the hide-out was no longer safe. He and his friend had more than one hair-breadth escape but in the end he did get away and left Italy again for many years. Once again he roamed the seas as a captain of trading vessels and came as far as China.

但他沒有太多時間悲傷——他甚至不能留下來看 Anita 下葬——因為 Austria 人仍在搜尋他，藏身之處不再安全。他和朋友經歷了不止一次千鈞一髮的逃脫，但最終他確實逃了出去，再次離開了 Italy 許多年。他再次以商船船長的身分漫遊大海，遠至 China。

But six years later, in 1854, there came another chance to return to his homeland. An important change had taken place in the Kingdom of Piedmont. A young and courageous king had come to the throne, Victor Emmanuel, who was truly willing to fight for a free and united Italy. But Piedmont could not hope to win against the might of Austria without a powerful ally - and there was such an ally: France.

但六年後，一八五四年，又一個返回祖國的機會來了。Piedmont 王國發生了一個重要的變化。一位年輕而勇敢的國王登上了王位——Victor Emmanuel，他真心願意為一個自由統一的 Italy 而戰。但 Piedmont 不能指望在沒有強大盟友的情況下戰勝 Austria 的力量——而這樣的盟友確實存在：France。

When Louis Philippe was driven away in the French Revolution of 1848, the French made Louis Napoleon, a nephew of Napoleon Bonaparte, president of the republic. This nephew was, however, just as ambitious as his uncle had been, and after a short time as president, declared himself Emperor of France under the title Napoleon III. (Napoleon's son who had died young was considered Napoleon II). And this new Napoleon was willing to come to the aid of Piedmont in its fight against Austria.

當 Louis Philippe 在一八四八年的法國革命中被驅逐後，法國人讓 Napoleon Bonaparte 的侄子 Louis Napoleon 擔任共和國總統。然而這個侄子和叔叔一樣野心勃勃，擔任總統不久後便自立為法國皇帝，稱 Napoleon III。（Napoleon 早逝的兒子被算作 Napoleon II。）而這位新 Napoleon 願意在 Piedmont 對抗 Austria 的戰爭中施以援手。

What was still needed was a man to lead the Italians, a man experienced in battle, a man whom they could follow with heart and soul, and that man was Garibaldi. He was called to Piedmont where he started to train a volunteer force of one thousand men especially chosen for fitness and courage. They were given red shirts as a sign of their willingness to give their blood for freedom.

還需要的是一個能領導義大利人的人，一個有戰場經驗的人，一個他們能全心全意追隨的人，而那個人就是 Garibaldi。他被召喚到 Piedmont，在那裡他開始訓練一支由一千名精選的體格強健、勇敢無畏之人組成的志願軍。他們穿上紅衫，作為他們願意為自由流血的標誌。

The time of Garibaldi's Redshirts came when a revolution broke out on the island of Sicily. This island was under Spanish rule who were cruel masters. They were certainly inhumanly cruel in their treatment of the people of Sicily. In the end the poor, down-trodden islanders could not stand it any longer and revolted. But the Sicilian peasants would not have had any hope of success if Garibaldi had not come with his Redshirts, and in three months the Spaniards were driven out.

Garibaldi 紅衫軍大顯身手的時刻到來了——Sicily 島爆發了革命。這個島嶼處於西班牙人的統治之下，他們是殘酷的主人。他們對 Sicily 人民的待遇確實慘無人道。最終，貧苦的、被踐踏的島民們忍無可忍，奮起反抗。但如果不是 Garibaldi 帶著紅衫軍到來，Sicily 農民不可能有任何成功的希望，三個月之內西班牙人就被驅逐了。

The Kingdom of Naples in the south was also under Spanish rule. Garibaldi and his Redshirts crossed over from Sicily to attack this Kingdom of Naples - but they did not have to do any attacking. The army sent against him surrendered without firing a single shot. The people of Naples rose in rebellion against the Spanish ruler who fled in haste and Garibaldi was welcomed as their liberator.

南方的 Naples 王國也在西班牙人的統治之下。Garibaldi 和他的紅衫軍從 Sicily 渡海進攻 Naples 王國——但他們根本不需要進攻。派來對抗他的軍隊不發一槍就投降了。Naples 人民起而反抗西班牙統治者，統治者倉皇逃竄，Garibaldi 被當作解放者歡迎。

At this point Garibaldi's fame and popularity was so great that, had he so wished, he could have made himself King of Italy. But this was not in his nature - and he remained faithful to Victor Emmanuel, the King of Piedmont.

此時 Garibaldi 的名望和聲望如此之高，如果他願意的話，他完全可以自立為義大利國王。但這不是他的本性——他始終忠於 Piedmont 國王 Victor Emmanuel。

In the meantime there was also war in Northern Italy, though Garibaldi took no part in it. In Northern Italy Napoleon III, as he had promised, had come to help the Italians against Austria. In a terrible battle the combined French and Italian troops defeated the Austrians. This Battle of Solferino in 1859 is important for quite another reason which we shall come to.

與此同時，北 Italy 也爆發了戰爭，雖然 Garibaldi 沒有參與。在北 Italy，Napoleon III 信守承諾，前來幫助義大利人對抗 Austria。在一場慘烈的戰役中，法國和義大利聯軍擊敗了 Austria 人。一八五九年的 Solferino 戰役因為另一個我們稍後會提到的原因而具有重要意義。

In any case, after the Battle of Solferino, the north of Italy was also set free, and at long last the great dream of so many Italians came true. In 1861 the whole of Italy was declared one nation - no longer divided into bits and pieces, and the first king of Italy, Victor Emmanuel, gave this new country a parliament, free elections and free speech (as Britain also had). Freedom had come to Italy, and few men had done so much and suffered so much for it as Garibaldi, the hero of freedom.

無論如何，在 Solferino 戰役之後，北 Italy 也獲得了自由，許多義大利人長久以來的偉大夢想終於成真。一八六一年，整個 Italy 被宣布為一個國家——不再四分五裂，第一位義大利國王 Victor Emmanuel 給了這個新國家一個議會、自由選舉和言論自由（正如 Britain 所擁有的那樣）。自由來到了 Italy，很少有人像 Garibaldi 這位自由英雄那樣為之付出如此之多、承受如此之多。

It is true that in later years Garibaldi quarrelled with King Victor Emmanuel and with the King's ministers, but then the old rebel was not an easy man to get on with and as stubborn in old age as he was in his youth. But that had also made him a hero of liberty, as Robert Owen was a hero of fraternity.

誠然，晚年的 Garibaldi 與國王 Victor Emmanuel 和國王的大臣們發生了爭吵，但這位老革命家本來就不是一個容易相處的人，他在老年時和年輕時一樣固執。但正是這種性格使他成為了自由的英雄，正如 Robert Owen 是博愛的英雄。
Chapter 45
Henri Dunant

第四十五章
Henri Dunant

We have looked at liberty, equality and fraternity, but these qualities would be incomplete without something else. Like a great river which at its delta divides into three, so liberty, equality, fraternity come from one source, and they cannot exist without that source. The source is charity, or compassion, a deep strong feeling for other people, the ability to share the joys and sorrows of others as if they were one's own. Owen had compassion for his workers, Garibaldi had compassion for his oppressed fellow countrymen in Italy, and it was this which made them heroes of brotherhood or of liberty. Now we shall come to a hero of compassion.

我們已經看過了自由、平等與博愛，但若少了另一樣東西，這些品質便不完整。就像一條大河在河口分成三條支流，自由、平等、博愛其實源自同一個泉源，沒有這個泉源它們便無法存在。這個泉源就是慈愛，或者說悲憫——一種對他人深沉而強烈的感受力，一種能將他人的喜悅與悲傷視為自己的喜悅與悲傷的能力。Owen 對他的工人懷有悲憫，Garibaldi 對他在 Italy 受壓迫的同胞懷有悲憫，正是這份悲憫使他們成為博愛或自由的英雄。現在，我們要認識一位悲憫的英雄。

This man was born in Switzerland, in Geneva - a beautiful city on Switzerland's largest lake, the Lake of Geneva. In that part of Switzerland, French is the national language and our hero has a French name Henri Dunant (1828-1910), but he was Swiss.

這個人出生在 Switzerland 的 Geneva——一座坐落在 Switzerland 最大湖泊 Geneva 湖畔的美麗城市。在 Switzerland 的那個地區，法語是當地的語言，我們的英雄有一個法文名字 Henri Dunant（1828-1910），但他是 Switzerland 人。

Dunant was the son of rich business people in Geneva, and as he grew up he showed the makings of a good businessman himself - a man who used money to make more money. But, already as a child, Dunant showed another side. One day, passing by the lake, he saw some boys angling for fish. When they caught one they did not kill it but threw it into a basket where some fish were feebly flapping. Young Dunant could not stand the sight; he went to the boys, gave them whatever pocket money he had on him for the fish and threw the fish back into the lake.

Dunant 是 Geneva 一戶富裕商人家庭的兒子，在成長過程中，他展現了成為一名優秀商人的潛質——一個善於用錢生錢的人。但早在孩提時期，Dunant 就顯露了他另一面的特質。有一天，他經過湖邊，看見幾個男孩在釣魚。他們釣到魚之後並不殺死牠，而是丟進一個籃子裡，裡頭已經有幾條魚在無力地拍打著。年幼的 Dunant 受不了這個景象；他走向那些男孩，把身上所有的零用錢給了他們，換來那些魚，然後把魚全部丟回湖裡。

But he had a good brain for business and as a grown up man he became a very wealthy and respected businessman in Geneva. A businessman is always looking for an opportunity to invest money, to multiply it, and so was Dunant. The question was: where would his money bring the largest profit?

但他確實有著敏銳的商業頭腦，長大後成為 Geneva 一位非常富有且受人尊敬的商人。商人總是在尋找投資的機會，讓錢滾錢，Dunant 也不例外。問題在於：把錢投到哪裡能獲得最大的利潤？

Now at that time, rich people, capitalists, like Dunant began to invest money not only in their own countries, not even in Europe, but overseas in colonies. Dunant's own country, Switzerland, had no colonies, but her great neighbour, France, had. It was only natural that Dunant whose mother language was French, should think of a French colony for investing his money. And the nearest French colony was Algeria, on the coast of North Africa.

在那個時代，像 Dunant 這樣的有錢人、資本家，開始不只在自己的國家投資，甚至不只在 Europe，而是把錢投到海外的殖民地。Dunant 自己的國家 Switzerland 沒有殖民地，但她強大的鄰居 France 有。母語是法語的 Dunant，自然而然會想到在一個法國殖民地投資。而最近的法國殖民地就是位於北非海岸的 Algeria。

And so our businessman, Dunant, travelled to Algeria to see for himself whether there were opportunities for investment that would in time bring a good profit. In the end he bought land, large estates with good soil on which wheat could be grown. But he also wanted to build mills where the wheat could be ground, and he wanted to dig canals to have water to drive the mills. To build a canal in Algeria the permission of the French Government in Paris was required. So Dunant wrote to Paris and asked for permission. But no answer came.

於是我們的商人 Dunant 親自前往 Algeria，想看看那裡是否有能帶來豐厚利潤的投資機會。最後他買下了一片土地，大片擁有良好土壤、可以種植小麥的莊園。但他還想建造磨坊來磨麥，也想挖掘水渠引水來驅動磨坊。要在 Algeria 興建水渠，需要取得在 Paris 的法國政府的許可。於是 Dunant 寫信到 Paris 申請許可，但始終沒有收到回音。

Dunant was angry: he had paid most of his fortune for the land and now he was held up by some bureaucrat in an office in Paris. And he decided he would go straight to the head of the French Government, which at that time was the new Emperor, Napoleon III. He would get permission for his canals from the Emperor. So he travelled to Paris, but the Emperor was not there. Napoleon III had marched with his army to Italy to help the Italians against Austria.

Dunant 非常惱怒：他已經把大部分的財產都花在買地上，如今卻被 Paris 某個辦公室裡的官僚給卡住了。他決定直接去找法國政府的最高領導人，也就是當時新任的皇帝 Napoleon 三世。他要從皇帝那裡取得水渠的許可。於是他前往 Paris，但皇帝不在那裡。Napoleon 三世已經率軍前往 Italy，去幫助 Italy 人對抗 Austria。

But this did not stop Dunant. If Napoleon III was in Italy, he would also go to Italy and get hold of His Majesty there. Dunant travelled to Italy, and in the end, he got as far as the headquarters of the French army just on the evening before the great Battle of Solferino. Of course, no one, least of all the Emperor, had time to listen to Dunant and his complaints; the French were busy getting ready for the coming battle. Dunant had to wait.

但這阻止不了 Dunant。既然 Napoleon 三世在 Italy，他就也去 Italy，在那裡找到陛下。Dunant 前往 Italy，最終在 Solferino 大戰前夕抵達了法軍的司令部。當然，沒有人有時間聽 Dunant 的抱怨，皇帝更不用說了；法軍正忙著為即將到來的戰役做準備。Dunant 只好等待。

And so it came that the next day, June 24, 1859, Dunant had the opportunity to watch the whole battle of Solferino from a hill.

就這樣，隔天——1859 年 6 月 24 日——Dunant 有機會從一座山丘上目睹了整場 Solferino 戰役。

It was June, a hot Italian June, and throughout the day the two armies - the French and Italians on one side, the Austrians on the other - fought a savage, murderous battle in the burning sun.

那是六月，一個炎熱的 Italy 六月，整整一天，兩支軍隊——一邊是法軍和 Italy 軍，另一邊是 Austria 軍——在烈日下展開了一場殘酷血腥的戰鬥。

Lines of men in marching order stormed against each other with the force of a raging torrent. This was a battle with hand-to-hand fighting, men stabbed their enemies with bayonets, they smashed their skulls with rifle-butts, they hacked them down with sabres. And when a man had no weapon left he would seize an enemy by the throat or tear at him with his teeth. It was a battle in which men fought like beasts, without mercy, and even the wounded fought on as long as they had strength. Cavalry horses trampled upon the bodies on the ground, cannon wheels rolled over them. The earth was soaked with blood, and the cries of anguish and pain were at times as loud as the thunder of gunfire.

一排排行軍隊列的士兵如洶湧的洪流般向彼此猛衝。這是一場肉搏戰，士兵們用刺刀刺穿敵人，用槍托砸碎他們的頭顱，用軍刀劈砍他們。當一個人手裡沒有武器了，他就會掐住敵人的喉嚨，或者用牙齒撕咬。這是一場人如野獸般廝殺的戰鬥，毫無憐憫，即使受了傷的人也拼盡最後一絲力氣繼續戰鬥。騎兵的馬踐踏著地上的屍體，砲車的輪子從屍體上碾過。大地浸透了鮮血，痛苦的哀號聲有時甚至蓋過了槍砲的轟鳴。

Towards evening the Austrians were defeated and in full retreat. The battle was over, but not the suffering. Forty thousand wounded, French, Italian, Austrian, were left lying on the battlefield without nurses, doctors, without food or water. Their thirst was far worse than the pain of their wounds, and the whole night the cries of the tormented rent the air. It was so bad that next morning some men were found who had crammed earth into their mouth and who had died in convulsions.

到了傍晚，Austria 軍戰敗，全面撤退。戰鬥結束了，但苦難沒有。四萬名傷兵——法國人、Italy 人、Austria 人——被遺棄在戰場上，沒有護士、沒有醫生、沒有食物也沒有水。他們的口渴遠比傷口的疼痛更難忍受，整晚，受折磨者的哀號聲劃破夜空。慘狀嚴重到第二天早上，人們發現有些人把泥土塞進了自己的嘴裡，在痙攣中死去。

The next day the suffering of the wounded continued, for there was still no help for them. They were covered with flies and their wounds festered. On that day the businessman Dunant forgot his business. If no one else did something for the thousands in agony, he would.

隔天，傷兵的痛苦仍在持續，因為依然沒有人來救助他們。蒼蠅覆蓋了他們的身體，傷口開始潰爛化膿。就在那一天，商人 Dunant 忘記了他的生意。如果沒有別人為這數以千計正在受苦的人做些什麼，那他來做。

He gathered the peasants of a nearby Italian village and organized a band of people to begin the nearly hopeless task. He got the village children to act as water carriers. He sent carts to the nearest town and with his own money bought bandages, pins, sponges, fruit. He got hold of two English tourists and made them join the little band of peasant men and women who attended the wounded. At first the Italian peasants would only look after Italian and French soldiers - they would not help the Austrian enemies. But Dunant cried out "Tutti fratelli" (We are all brothers), and the Italian peasants repeated: "It is true, all men are brothers." And they treated the wounded Austrians like their own soldiers. There were forty thousand wounded and only a pitiful little band of volunteers - perhaps a hundred - to help. For three days these true Christians, driven by the example of Dunant, worked day and night, with no more than an hour's rest now and then. And Dunant managed, at last, to get from the French army horse-carts to take the wounded to the nearest town where schools, churches, town halls, were cleared for them.

他召集附近一個 Italy 村莊的農民，組織了一群人，開始進行這近乎無望的工作。他讓村裡的孩子充當送水員。他派馬車去最近的城鎮，用自己的錢買來繃帶、別針、海綿和水果。他找到兩個英國遊客，讓他們加入這支由農民男女組成的小小隊伍來照顧傷兵。起初 Italy 農民只願意照顧 Italy 和法國士兵——他們不肯幫助 Austria 敵人。但 Dunant 大聲喊道「Tutti fratelli」（我們都是兄弟），Italy 農民也跟著說：「沒錯，所有人都是兄弟。」於是他們像照顧自己的士兵一樣照顧受傷的 Austria 人。有四萬名傷兵，而來幫忙的只是一小群可憐的志願者——大概一百人左右。三天裡，這些真正的基督徒在 Dunant 的榜樣驅動下，日夜不停地工作，中間只偶爾休息一個小時。最後 Dunant 終於從法軍那裡爭取到馬車，把傷兵運往最近的城鎮，學校、教堂、市政廳都被清空來收容他們。

But he never saw the Emperor Napoleon III. The Emperor had not liked the sight and had, immediately after the battle, set out for Paris. But Dunant was no longer interested in his business, in his canals and mills. He returned to Geneva, to Switzerland with only one thought in his mind: "What can I do to help the wounded in future wars, in future battles?" Back in Geneva, he wrote a book, The Battle of Solferino, in which he not only described all that had happened, but proposed that all nations

但他始終沒有見到皇帝 Napoleon 三世。皇帝不喜歡眼前所見的景象，戰役一結束就立刻動身返回 Paris。但 Dunant 已經不再關心他的生意、他的水渠和磨坊了。他回到 Geneva，回到 Switzerland，腦海中只有一個念頭：「我能做什麼，來幫助未來戰爭、未來戰役中的傷兵？」回到 Geneva 後，他寫了一本書——《Solferino 回憶錄》，書中他不僅描述了所發生的一切，還提議各個國家

[...原文此處因頁面斷裂而缺失...]

him, and for many years, no one knew whether he still lived or not.

他，而且許多年來，沒有人知道他是否還活著。

But in 1908 when Dunant was eighty years old, a journalist discovered him; he was in a village in the Alps. Now gifts, telegrams, from all over the world arrived and Dunant could at least die with the knowledge that he was not forgotten.*

但在 1908 年，當 Dunant 八十歲時，一位記者找到了他；他住在 Alps 山中的一個小村莊裡。這時，來自世界各地的禮物和電報紛至沓來，Dunant 至少可以帶著「自己沒有被遺忘」的認知離開人世。*

He will never be forgotten - he is one of the great heroes of compassion, of mercy, of love between human beings.

他永遠不會被遺忘——他是悲憫、仁慈、人與人之間的愛的偉大英雄之一。

\* Dunant was awarded the first Nobel Prize for peace in 1901.

\* Dunant 於 1901 年獲頒第一屆 Nobel 和平獎。

---

Chapter 46
Abraham Lincoln

第四十六章
Abraham Lincoln

Robert Owen was a hero of fraternity, and Garibaldi a hero of liberty. Now we come to our hero of equality. But we must be clear what "equality" means. It means "equality of rights," it means that every citizen of a state has the same rights. There must not be different laws for rich and poor, for the noble lord and the worker - that is what is meant by "equality" of rights. A hardworking person will, probably, get on better in life than a lazy one, but before the law, in a court case or in a legal argument, they are equal.

Robert Owen 是博愛的英雄，Garibaldi 是自由的英雄。現在我們要認識的是平等的英雄。但我們必須先弄清楚「平等」是什麼意思。它指的是「權利的平等」，意思是一個國家的每一位公民都享有相同的權利。不能有一套法律是給富人的，另一套是給窮人的；不能貴族領主和勞工適用不同的法律——這就是「權利」平等的意思。一個勤奮的人在生活中可能會過得比懶惰的人好，但在法律面前，在法庭審判或法律辯論中，他們是平等的。

But only a hundred and fifty years ago there existed people who, by the law of their country, had no rights at all. They did not even have the right to leave their job if they did not like it. These people without rights were enslaved Africans working in the United States of America, where slavery was still legal in 1855.

然而就在一百五十年前，還有一些人依照他們國家的法律完全沒有任何權利。他們甚至沒有權利在不喜歡工作時離開。這些沒有權利的人就是在 United States of America 工作的被奴役的非洲人，在 1855 年奴隸制在那裡仍然是合法的。

Of course, some Americans said then that the enslaved people were well treated by most owners - they were not so badly off. But even if that were true, slavery would still be wrong. And a good many slave owners were not kind but cruel and brutal - they could hurt and kill enslaved people as they pleased, for these people had no rights.

當然，當時有些美國人說，大部分的奴隸主對被奴役的人待遇不錯——他們過得並不太差。但即使這是真的，奴隸制仍然是錯誤的。而且許多奴隸主並不仁慈，而是殘忍暴虐的——他們可以隨心所欲地傷害和殺死被奴役的人，因為這些人沒有任何權利。

Yet it was only the Southern states of the United States - Alabama, Georgia, Louisiana, the Carolinas, Virginia - which still allowed slavery. The reason why these Southern states still enslaved Africans was a plant which produces a white fluffy tuft - cotton.

然而，只有 United States 的南方各州——Alabama、Georgia、Louisiana、the Carolinas、Virginia——仍然允許奴隸制。這些南方各州之所以仍然奴役非洲人，原因在於一種長出白色蓬鬆纖維團的植物——棉花。

Come to think of it, no plant has caused so much suffering as cotton: the conditions of the cotton mills of the Industrial Revolution in Britain, the transatlantic slave trade. But, of course, it was not the plant, it was human greed which caused the suffering.

仔細想想，沒有任何一種植物像棉花一樣造成了這麼多的苦難：Britain 工業革命時期棉紡廠的惡劣條件、跨大西洋的奴隸貿易。但當然，造成苦難的不是植物，而是人類的貪婪。

In the United States cotton could only be grown in the hot climate of the Southern states, and the work in the vast cotton plantations was done by people who had been taken from Africa and enslaved. In the North where cotton did not grow, there was no need for vast numbers of workers. And so the Northern states, one after another, abolished slavery.

在 United States，棉花只能在南方各州炎熱的氣候下種植，而廣大棉花種植園裡的勞動，是由從 Africa 被擄來並被奴役的人完成的。在棉花不生長的北方，不需要大量的勞動力。因此北方各州一個接一個地廢除了奴隸制。

So in the middle of the nineteenth century then, the United States was a nation divided by the question of slavery. The Northern states had abolished slavery; it was against the law to enslave people. But the people of the Southern states said: "It is easy for you, you have no cotton plantations. But we in the South depend on cotton, and it would be quite impossible to work the cotton plantations and make a profit from them, without having slaves to work them."

於是到了十九世紀中葉，United States 是一個因奴隸問題而分裂的國家。北方各州已經廢除了奴隸制；奴役他人是違法的。但南方各州的人說：「你們說得輕鬆，你們又沒有棉花種植園。但我們南方依賴棉花，要是沒有奴隸來耕作，要經營棉花種植園並從中獲利，那是完全不可能的。」

This state of things could go on - but only for a time. More and more people in the North felt it was wrong for a civilized nation, like the United States, to still enslave people like the ancient Romans, so they demanded that the Southern states should abolish slavery. The American Government in Washington should make a law for the whole of America that there should be no more slavery. As the Northern states had a majority in the Government, they could make such a law for the whole country.

這種狀態可以繼續下去——但只能維持一段時間。越來越多北方人認為，像 United States 這樣的文明國家，還像古 Rome 人那樣奴役他人是不對的，因此他們要求南方各州應該廢除奴隸制。在 Washington 的美國政府應該為全美國制定一項法律，不再允許奴隸制度存在。由於北方各州在政府中占多數，他們有能力為全國制定這樣的法律。

But the Southern states said: "If you make such a law, then we shall break up the United States, and we, the Southern states, will declare our part of America a separate country. We shall have a republic of our own and our own government, and keep the slaves." To which the Northern states replied: "We will not allow you to divide America. We shall keep you by force under the Government in Washington which is your and our Government."

但南方各州說：「如果你們制定這樣的法律，那我們就要拆散 United States，我們南方各州將宣佈把我們這部分的 America 變成一個獨立的國家。我們要有自己的共和國、自己的政府，並保留奴隸。」對此，北方各州回答：「我們不會允許你們分裂 America。我們會用武力把你們留在 Washington 的政府之下——那是你們的政府，也是我們的政府。」

That was the position in the year 1860. In that year Abraham Lincoln (1809-65) became President of the United States - that is the lawful President of the North and the South.

這就是 1860 年的局勢。那一年 Abraham Lincoln（1809-65）成為 United States 的總統——也就是南方和北方的合法總統。

Abraham Lincoln's career was a typically American success story. He came from a very poor home in Kentucky, which at that time was still half wild. His mother died when he was only eight years old. His father was a carpenter, a restless man who cared little for his son. From the age of nine young Lincoln had to earn his own living - working on farms, working in shops or helping on a ferry boat. In between these jobs he would occasionally go to school. It wasn't his fault that he could not get a proper education, but he tried to make up for it by educating himself. When he was a shop assistant customers found him with a book on the counter which he studied at every possible moment.

Abraham Lincoln 的生涯是一個典型的美國成功故事。他來自 Kentucky 一個非常貧窮的家庭，那裡在當時仍然半是荒野。他的母親在他年僅八歲時就去世了。他的父親是一名木匠，一個不安分的人，對兒子很少關心。從九歲起，年幼的 Lincoln 就得自己謀生——在農場工作、在商店幫忙、或在渡船上打雜。在這些工作之間，他偶爾會去上學。他無法接受正規教育並不是他的錯，但他努力靠自學來彌補。當他在商店當店員時，顧客們會看到他在櫃台上放著一本書，一有空就埋頭研讀。

Later on Lincoln started a small business, a shop, together with a partner. But the partner was dishonest and a drunkard. He drank himself to death and left Lincoln with enormous debts. It took Lincoln many years to pay off these debts - but pay he did. He was determined to be honest in all his dealings.

後來 Lincoln 和一個合夥人一起開了一家小店。但那個合夥人不誠實又酗酒。他把自己喝死了，留下龐大的債務給 Lincoln。Lincoln 花了許多年才還清這些債務——但他確實還清了。他決心在所有的交往中都要誠實。

And in these years when he worked in shops and had to pay these debts he began to study law in his spare time. And eventually, he passed his exams and became a lawyer in Springfield, the capital of Illinois.

就在這些在商店工作、必須還債的歲月裡，他開始利用閒暇時間研讀法律。最終，他通過了考試，成為 Springfield——Illinois 州首府——的一名律師。

As a lawyer, Abraham Lincoln remained scrupulously honest. One day a man came to him with the request to take his case to court. Lincoln listened to the man's story and then he said: "Yes, I could take your case to court, I could win it and so get from you five hundred dollar as my fee - but I won't do it, because you are in the wrong. Goodbye."

作為律師，Abraham Lincoln 始終一絲不苟地保持誠實。有一天，一個人來找他，請他代為出庭打官司。Lincoln 聽完了那人的故事，然後說：「是的，我可以替你上法庭，我可以打贏這場官司，這樣我就能收你五百塊錢的律師費——但我不會這麼做，因為你理虧。再見。」

With such a strong sense of fairness and justice Abraham Lincoln had been against slavery from his youth. He thought it was an evil that should disappear from America. He entered politics to fight this evil and was elected by the people of Springfield to be their Congressman in Washington. From there one thing led to another, and in 1860, in that time of great tension, Abraham Lincoln, the son of a poor carpenter, became President of the United States.

帶著這樣強烈的公平正義感，Abraham Lincoln 從年輕時就反對奴隸制。他認為這是一種邪惡，應該從 America 消失。他投身政治來對抗這種邪惡，被 Springfield 的人民選為他們在 Washington 的國會議員。從那時起一件事接著一件事發展，到了 1860 年，在那個緊張萬分的時刻，Abraham Lincoln——一個窮木匠的兒子——成為了 United States 的總統。

Lincoln did not want to see his country split by a civil war, and he promised not to force the Southern states to give up their slaves. But they did not believe him and in January 1861 the states South Carolina, Mississippi, Florida, Alabama, Georgia, Louisiana and Texas declared themselves an independent republic and set up their own government (by May they were joined by Virginia, Arkansas, Tennessee and North Carolina). They also declared that slavery was the "natural condition" of the Black people.

Lincoln 不想看到他的國家被內戰撕裂，他承諾不會強迫南方各州放棄他們的奴隸。但他們不相信他，1861 年一月，South Carolina、Mississippi、Florida、Alabama、Georgia、Louisiana 和 Texas 各州宣佈自己為獨立的共和國，並組建了自己的政府（到五月時 Virginia、Arkansas、Tennessee 和 North Carolina 也加入了他們）。他們還宣稱奴隸制是黑人的「自然狀態」。

This was open revolt, it was rebellion against the lawful government in Washington, and Abraham Lincoln as President had a duty to fight the rebels.

這是公然的叛亂，是對 Washington 合法政府的反叛，而身為總統的 Abraham Lincoln 有責任對叛軍作戰。

And so, in 1861, the terrible Civil War between the Southern states (the Confederates) and Northern states (the Unionists) began, a war in which people of the same nation fought each other, a war that lasted four years and in which six hundred thousand men lost their lives.

就這樣，1861 年，南方各州（邦聯軍）與北方各州（聯邦軍）之間可怕的內戰開始了，一場同一個國家的人民互相廝殺的戰爭，一場持續了四年、六十萬人喪生的戰爭。

To begin with it was not a war to set the enslaved people free, it was a war to keep the Southern states in the Union, but during the war Abraham Lincoln declared that, if the North was going to win, then slavery in the South would be abolished.

一開始這並不是一場解放被奴役者的戰爭，而是一場要把南方各州留在聯邦之中的戰爭，但在戰爭期間 Abraham Lincoln 宣佈，如果北方贏得勝利，那麼南方的奴隸制將被廢除。

In 1865 the war ended with the victory of the Northern states - and slavery came to an end in America. It would have been a blessing if fair-minded Abraham Lincoln had remained leader in peace as he had been in war. His aim was to treat the defeated Southern states not as conquered enemies, but as friends and so heal the wounds of war. But it was not to be so. Just before the surrender of the South, Lincoln went to a theatre one evening. A fanatical Southerner made his way to the President's box during the performance, and shot him.

1865 年，戰爭以北方各州的勝利告終——奴隸制在 America 走到了盡頭。如果公正的 Abraham Lincoln 能像他在戰時那樣在和平時期繼續擔任領導人，那將是一件幸事。他的目標是對待戰敗的南方各州不是把他們當作被征服的敵人，而是當作朋友，以此來癒合戰爭的創傷。但事實並非如此。就在南方投降前不久，Lincoln 有一天晚上去了劇院。一個狂熱的南方人在演出期間潛入總統包廂，開槍射殺了他。

The President who came after Lincoln, Andrew Johnston, was unable to go against Congress which made the Southern states feel they were conquered enemies and so created a bitterness which lingered on in the South for many years.

繼 Lincoln 之後的總統 Andrew Johnston 無力對抗國會，國會使南方各州感覺自己是被征服的敵人，因而產生了一種在南方持續多年的怨恨。

The Black people were no longer enslaved, but this was only the beginning of the road to equality. It took more than another hundred years for Black people to enjoy equality of rights in America, especially in the South.

黑人不再被奴役了，但這只是通往平等之路的起點。又過了一百多年，黑人才在 America 享有平等的權利，尤其是在南方。

So around the same time as the Industrial Revolution in Britain brought demands for fraternity, and in Italy there was a struggle for liberty, in America the Civil War was a war for equality. And the hero of this war for equality was Abraham Lincoln.

因此，大約在同一時期，Britain 的工業革命帶來了對博愛的訴求，Italy 正在為自由而奮鬥，而在 America，內戰是一場為平等而戰的戰爭。這場平等之戰的英雄就是 Abraham Lincoln。

---

Chapter 47
Tsar Alexander II

第四十七章
沙皇 Alexander 二世

At the same time as there was a struggle for human rights and equality in America, a similar kind of struggle took place in Russia, a country which became America's opponent in the second half of the twentieth century. At the time of the struggle between North and South in America, Russia, too, was coming to grips with the problem of equality.

就在 America 為人權和平等而奮鬥的同時，類似的鬥爭也在 Russia 發生——一個在二十世紀下半葉成為 America 對手的國家。當 America 南北之間的鬥爭正在進行時，Russia 也在面對平等的問題。

Russia had at that time its own kind of "slaves" - but they were called "serfs." The serfs in Russia were of Russian origin like their masters, but they were also enslaved, and their lives were miserable.

Russia 在那個時期有自己的一種「奴隸」——但他們被稱為「農奴」。Russia 的農奴和他們的主人一樣是 Russia 人，但他們同樣被奴役著，生活悲慘。

At that time there were only a few cities in Russia, there were practically no industries, no factories, and most of this vast country was farmland. But there were no farmers as you find in Britain today. There were only vast estates - each stretching over thousands of acres - and these great estates were owned by the Russian aristocrats.

那時候 Russia 只有少數幾座城市，幾乎沒有工業、沒有工廠，這個廣袤國家的大部分土地都是農地。但那裡沒有像你在今天的 Britain 看到的那種農夫。有的只是大片大片的莊園——每一座都綿延數千英畝——而這些大莊園都歸 Russia 的貴族所有。

The workers, the peasants, who worked in the fields for their noble masters, were not "tenants" as they had been in Britain, they were "serfs" which meant they were the property of the owner, just like the cattle or the houses on the estate. But they were not just slaves. There was one difference. Enslaved people in America could be sold on their own. Serfs in Russia could only be sold if the land on which they lived was also being sold. The serfs were a part of the land, like the trees that grew on it.

在田裡為貴族主人勞作的工人、農民，不像在 Britain 那樣是「佃農」，他們是「農奴」，意思是他們是主人的財產，就像莊園裡的牲畜或房屋一樣。但他們又不完全等同於奴隸。有一個區別：America 的被奴役者可以單獨被買賣。Russia 的農奴只有在他們居住的土地也一起出售時才能被賣。農奴是土地的一部分，就像生長在土地上的樹木一樣。

The estate-owner gave his serfs neither money nor food. Each serf-family had a little plot of land to grow their own food - and they were supposed to work two days a week at their own plot - and four days a week in the fields of their master. But, in practice, the nobleman hardly ever gave them enough time for their own plots - and the serfs hardly ever had enough to eat.

莊園主人既不給農奴金錢，也不提供食物。每個農奴家庭有一小塊地來種自己的食物——他們原本應該每週用兩天在自己的地上耕作——另外四天在主人的田裡勞動。但實際上，貴族幾乎從不給他們足夠的時間去照料自己的地——農奴們也幾乎從來吃不飽。

The master could inflict any punishment he liked on his serfs - for good reasons or for no reason at all. A thousand strokes with a birch rod was quite common. But there was one punishment the serfs feared more than any other. If serfs showed disobedience several times they were sent to Siberia. There, where the ground was frozen nine months of the year, where millions of mosquitoes made life a misery in the warm months, there were the dreaded punishment or prison camps where the poor wretches, dressed in their rags even in the iciest cold and fed on a little bread and water worked until death came as a relief.

主人可以對農奴施加任何他喜歡的懲罰——不論有沒有理由。用白樺木條抽打一千下是很平常的事。但有一種懲罰是農奴們最害怕的。如果農奴多次表現出不服從，就會被送到 Siberia。在那裡，大地一年有九個月是冰凍的，溫暖的月份裡又有數百萬隻蚊子讓生活苦不堪言，那裡有令人恐懼的懲罰營或監獄，可憐的人們即使在最嚴寒的天氣也只穿著破衣爛衫，靠著一點麵包和水過活，不停地勞動直到死亡降臨才得到解脫。

One quarter of the whole population of Russia were serfs - and this quarter worked and produced food for all the others.

Russia 全部人口的四分之一是農奴——而正是這四分之一的人勞動並生產食物來養活所有其他人。

Schools and universities existed only for the sons of the great landowners and rich merchants. But what was taught in these schools and universities was laid down by the Government, by the Tsar of Russia and his ministers.

學校和大學只為大地主和富商的兒子而設。但這些學校和大學裡教什麼，完全由政府決定，由 Russia 的沙皇和他的大臣們規定。

In Russia, too, the Tsar and the noblemen were afraid that the ideas of the French Revolution, the ideas of liberty, fraternity and equality, would spread and the people rise in revolt. And so that Government did everything possible to prevent the spreading of "dangerous" ideas.

在 Russia，沙皇和貴族們同樣害怕法國大革命的思想——自由、博愛和平等的思想——會蔓延開來，使人民起而反抗。因此政府竭盡所能地阻止「危險」思想的傳播。

In addition to the police who would arrest anybody who said or wrote anything dangerous or anti-government, there was also a secret police. The secret police were people who were paid by the Government to spy on everybody and to report anyone who showed by a careless word that they had "dangerous" ideas. Not even a high-ranking nobleman was safe from the secret police, and everybody in Russia, from prince down to serf, lived in fear of these spies. Once a spy of the secret police had reported you, you were doomed. There was no trial, no hearing in court, you were arrested and either executed or sent to the prison camps of Siberia to die a lingering death.

除了會逮捕任何說出或寫下危險言論或反政府言論的人的普通警察之外，還有秘密警察。秘密警察是由政府出錢雇用來監視所有人的人，他們會舉報任何因為一句不小心的話而暴露出擁有「危險」思想的人。即使是高階貴族也逃不過秘密警察的監視，在 Russia，從王公到農奴，所有人都活在對這些密探的恐懼中。一旦秘密警察的密探舉報了你，你就完了。沒有審判，沒有法庭聽證，你會被逮捕，然後不是被處決，就是被送到 Siberia 的監獄營去慢慢死去。

In 1855 a new Tsar came to the throne of Russia, Alexander II (1818-81). He was a man who wanted some progress in Russia. There was a new wind blowing in Russia - and the first sign of this new wind was that Alexander II, the new Tsar, gave permission for the building of railways in Russia. His father, the Tsar before him, had forbidden railways on the grounds that they would encourage unnecessary travelling and so make people restless.

1855 年，一位新沙皇登上了 Russia 的王座——Alexander 二世（1818-81）。他是一個希望 Russia 有些進步的人。Russia 刮起了一股新風——而這股新風的第一個跡象就是新沙皇 Alexander 二世批准了在 Russia 修建鐵路。他的父親，也就是上一任沙皇，曾經禁止修建鐵路，理由是鐵路會鼓勵不必要的旅行，從而使人民變得躁動不安。

The new Tsar, Alexander II, not only wanted railways, he wanted a very great change: he wanted to abolish serfdom, he wanted the serfs to become free and to have equal rights with the other people of Russia.

新沙皇 Alexander 二世不僅想要鐵路，他還想要一個非常重大的改變：他想廢除農奴制，他想讓農奴獲得自由，並與 Russia 其他人民享有平等的權利。

You might think that the serfs were pleased to hear the news that they were to be free. But they were not; as long as they were serfs they had at least a little plot of land given to them by their master. But if they were no longer serfs they would no longer have land, and such a life was no use. They would sooner remain serfs than be without land.

你可能以為農奴聽到他們將要獲得自由的消息會很高興。但他們並不高興；只要他們還是農奴，至少還有主人分給他們的一小塊土地。但如果他們不再是農奴，就不再擁有土地，而那樣的生活毫無意義。他們寧可繼續當農奴也不願沒有土地。

Alexander II realized that he would have to take land from the noblemen and give it to the peasants, but the noblemen had to be paid for this land. Who should pay for it? The peasants, of course. They should work the new plots given to them and sell a part of their crops, then year after year, pay a sum to the noblemen until they had paid for their land. This was a solution that seemed fair to both noblemen and serfs, and so serfdom was abolished in Russia.

Alexander 二世意識到他必須從貴族手中拿走土地分給農民，但貴族們必須因此得到補償。誰來付這筆錢？當然是農民。他們應該耕種分配給他們的新土地，賣掉一部分收成，然後年復一年地付一筆錢給貴族，直到他們把土地的費用付清為止。這個方案對貴族和農奴雙方來說似乎都算公平，於是農奴制在 Russia 被廢除了。

The year 1861 is a great one for human rights in history. It was the year when the American Civil War began which led to slavery being abolished, and it was the year Tsar Alexander II abolished serfdom in Russia. It was a great step towards equality when in 1861, slavery in America, and serfdom in Russia were abolished.

1861 年在人權歷史上是偉大的一年。這一年美國內戰爆發，最終導致奴隸制被廢除；也是這一年沙皇 Alexander 二世廢除了 Russia 的農奴制。1861 年，America 的奴隸制和 Russia 的農奴制被廢除，這是邁向平等的一大步。

Alexander II had done something for equality, for human rights, but he had no intention to allow the Russian people to have a say in government. He had absolute power and would not share it with a parliament. By then there were many people in Russia who wanted more freedom, especially the students at the universities. The students held public meetings in which they demanded elections and a parliament for Russia. The result was that hundreds of students were arrested and sent to Siberia.

Alexander 二世為平等、為人權做了一些事，但他無意讓 Russia 人民在政府中擁有發言權。他擁有絕對的權力，不願與議會分享。到那時 Russia 已經有許多人渴望更多的自由，尤其是大學裡的學生。學生們舉行公開集會，要求 Russia 實行選舉和設立議會。結果是數百名學生被逮捕並被送往 Siberia。

Moreover, Tsar Alexander II decided that it was science in particular that made people think and get dangerous ideas in their heads, and so the teaching of science - physics, chemistry, physiology, astronomy - was simply forbidden. The only subjects which remained were Latin and Greek, history and geography.

此外，沙皇 Alexander 二世認定，正是科學讓人們思考並在腦中萌生危險的想法，因此科學的教學——物理、化學、生理學、天文學——全部被禁止。唯一保留的科目只有拉丁文和希臘文、歷史和地理。

The students hit back by making several attempts to kill Tsar Alexander II. He escaped and gave the secret police more power than they ever had before. The secret police could arrest, hang, shoot, or send anybody to Siberia, as they pleased.

學生們進行了幾次暗殺沙皇 Alexander 二世的企圖來反擊。他僥倖逃過，並賦予秘密警察前所未有的權力。秘密警察可以隨心所欲地逮捕、絞死、槍殺任何人，或把任何人送到 Siberia。

By now the students were determined that this tyrant of a Tsar should die. In 1881 Alexander II was being driven in a coach through the streets of Moscow when a student suddenly threw a bomb into the coach; it exploded and killed the Tsar.

此時學生們已下定決心，這個暴君沙皇必須死。1881 年，當 Alexander 二世乘馬車行經 Moscow 街頭時，一名學生突然向馬車投擲了一枚炸彈；炸彈爆炸，沙皇當場身亡。

Alexander II died because he had not realized that equality alone was not enough but that liberty, too, is necessary in the modern age. It is a strange coincidence that both the man who ended serfdom and the man

Alexander 二世之所以死去，是因為他沒有意識到僅有平等是不夠的，在現代，自由同樣不可或缺。一個奇特的巧合是，終結農奴制的那個人和那個

[...原文此處因頁面斷裂而缺失...]

---

Chapter 48
Bismarck

第四十八章
Bismarck

We have seen some of the great changes which took place in the nineteenth century, in Britain, and Italy, in France (where Napoleon III came to power), in America and in Russia. Now we come to Germany.

我們已經看過了十九世紀發生的一些重大變革，在 Britain、Italy、France（Napoleon 三世在那裡掌權）、America 和 Russia。現在我們來到 Germany。

In the middle of the nineteenth century, Germany was - like Italy - not one country, but divided into many states each with its own ruler, though the people all spoke the same language. There was the Kingdom of Prussia, the Kingdom of Bavaria, the Kingdom of Saxony and many other smaller and larger states.

十九世紀中葉，Germany 和 Italy 一樣，不是一個統一的國家，而是分裂成許多各有其統治者的邦國，儘管人民都說同一種語言。有 Prussia 王國、Bavaria 王國、Saxony 王國，以及許多其他大大小小的邦國。

Just as in Italy, the people in Germany had a desire to become one united nation, but the different kings had no wish to give up their power. And when, in that "red" year of 1848, revolutions erupted in several parts of Germany, these uprisings were suppressed, and Germany remained divided.

就像在 Italy 一樣，Germany 的人民渴望成為一個統一的國家，但各邦的國王們不願放棄他們的權力。當 1848 年那個「紅色」之年革命在 Germany 各地爆發時，這些起義被鎮壓了，Germany 依然是分裂的。

Germany was not so fortunate as Italy, while there were freedom-loving people in Germany, there was no great leader like Garibaldi. And when Germany was united in the end, it was not the work of a man who loved freedom. Otto von Bismarck (1815-98), the man who formed Germany into one nation, was not interested in freedom, but in power.

Germany 不像 Italy 那麼幸運，雖然 Germany 也有熱愛自由的人民，卻沒有像 Garibaldi 那樣偉大的領袖。而當 Germany 最終統一時，這並非出自一個熱愛自由之人的手筆。Otto von Bismarck（1815-98），這個將 Germany 鑄造成一個國家的人，對自由不感興趣，他感興趣的是權力。

Bismarck, born in 1815, was not the son of a poor family as Garibaldi was. His family were Prussian aristocrats, noblemen who had been great lords in Prussia since the Middle Ages. Bismarck was never a common sailor like Garibaldi, a shop assistant like Lincoln or Robert Owen; he grew up as the son of great land owners - and although the peasants on the estates were not serfs or slaves, they were still obedient and respectful to their masters. So young Bismarck grew up with the conviction that the world was made for masters who command, and servants who obeyed. Words like liberty, equality and fraternity meant nothing to him.

Bismarck 生於 1815 年，不像 Garibaldi 那樣出身貧寒。他的家族是 Prussia 的貴族，自中世紀以來就是 Prussia 的大領主。Bismarck 從來不是像 Garibaldi 那樣的普通水手，也不是像 Lincoln 或 Robert Owen 那樣的店員；他是以大地主之子的身分長大的——雖然莊園裡的農民不是農奴或奴隸，但他們對主人仍然是順從恭敬的。因此年輕的 Bismarck 從小就深信，這個世界是為發號施令的主人和服從命令的僕人而造的。自由、平等、博愛這些詞對他毫無意義。

But young Bismarck was a clever boy, so clever that he did well at school without working hard. It was the same at university: he spent most of his time fighting duels (sabre-fighting was a favourite sport amongst German students) and enjoying himself, yet he did very well at his exams.

但年輕的 Bismarck 是個聰明的孩子，聰明到不用太努力在學校就能表現很好。大學也是一樣：他大部分時間都在決鬥（劍術決鬥是 Germany 大學生最喜愛的運動）和享樂，然而考試成績卻非常出色。

The family was rich, so there was no need for Bismarck to work for a living, and he could settle down to the pleasant life of a great land-owner. But Bismarck was also a man of great energy - and doing nothing did not suit him at all, so he took an interest in the politics of his country, Prussia.

家族很富有，所以 Bismarck 不需要為生計工作，他可以安心過大地主的愜意生活。但 Bismarck 也是一個精力充沛的人——無所事事完全不適合他，於是他開始對自己國家 Prussia 的政治產生了興趣。

At this time the King of Prussia had already made some concessions to the people: he had allowed them to have a parliament. This parliament did not have much power, it could never go against the King, but it was at least some kind of democratic institution.

這時候 Prussia 國王已經對人民做出了一些讓步：他允許他們擁有一個議會。這個議會沒有多大權力，永遠不能違抗國王，但至少算是某種民主制度。

Bismarck became a member of this parliament. But he already had certain ideas about the future of Prussia and the future of Germany - and the parliament was, for him, only a means to achieve what he had in mind.

Bismarck 成為了這個議會的成員。但他對 Prussia 的未來和 Germany 的未來已經有了明確的想法——而議會對他來說，只不過是實現他心中目標的一個手段。

Bismarck agreed with the people who wanted the separate states of Germany to become united in one great nation, and he realized that such a united Germany could be a very powerful nation, a nation of many millions, a nation with the largest army in Europe. This united Germany could become one of the great world powers.

Bismarck 認同那些希望 Germany 各邦統一成一個偉大國家的人，他也意識到這樣一個統一的 Germany 會是一個非常強大的國家，一個擁有數百萬人口的國家，一個擁有 Europe 最大軍隊的國家。這個統一的 Germany 可以成為世界上的大國之一。

But how could Germany become united? Not by revolutions - a man like Bismarck, a nobleman, only had contempt for rebels and revolutions. No, there was another way. His own country, Prussia should force the other states of Germany to accept Prussia as master, and his own King, the King of Prussia, should become Emperor of Germany, of the whole nation. Not a revolution from below, but force from above should make Germany one nation.

但 Germany 要如何統一？不是靠革命——像 Bismarck 這樣的貴族，對叛亂和革命只有蔑視。不，還有另一條路。他自己的國家 Prussia 應該強迫 Germany 的其他邦國接受 Prussia 為主人，而他自己的國王——Prussia 國王——應該成為整個 Germany 的皇帝。不是從下而上的革命，而是從上而下的強力，來使 Germany 成為一個國家。

We saw that 1861 was a fateful year in history. It was the year in which the Civil War that abolished slavery in America began, and when the serfs in Russia were set free; it was the year in which Italy became one nation under King Victor Emmanuel. It was also the year in which Bismarck became Prime Minister of Prussia and so could begin to put his ideas into practice.

我們看到 1861 年是歷史上命運攸關的一年。這一年，導致 America 廢除奴隸制的內戰爆發了，Russia 的農奴獲得了自由；Italy 在 Victor Emmanuel 國王的統治下成為一個統一的國家。這也是 Bismarck 成為 Prussia 首相，從而能夠開始付諸實現他的構想的一年。

To make Prussia strong enough to impose her will on the rest of Germany, she needed a large army, and such an army cost money. Bismarck asked the Prussian Parliament to increase taxes to pay for the army. In his speech he spoke words which were, unfortunately, prophetic. He said: "The great issues of the world will not be decided by words and arguments, but by blood and iron."

要使 Prussia 強大到能把自己的意志強加於 Germany 其他各邦，她需要一支龐大的軍隊，而這樣的軍隊需要花錢。Bismarck 要求 Prussia 議會增加稅收來支付軍費。在他的演說中，他說了一番不幸一語成讖的話。他說：「世界上的重大問題不是靠言語和辯論來解決的，而是靠鐵和血。」

But the Prussian members of parliament thought the taxes were already high enough and voted against the increase - they knew that the people did not want to pay more taxes. But Bismarck was not interested in what the people wanted - he knew what he himself wanted: a large, strong Prussian army. He went to the King of Prussia and the King simply ordered that the taxes be put up. And the Prussians obeyed and paid.

但 Prussia 的議員們認為稅收已經夠高了，投票反對加稅——他們知道人民不想繳更多的稅。但 Bismarck 對人民想要什麼不感興趣——他知道他自己要什麼：一支龐大而強悍的 Prussia 軍隊。他去找 Prussia 國王，國王便直接下令加稅。Prussia 人服從了，也付了。

So the Prussian army grew, it became the strongest, best-trained army within the German states, and the other states, Bavaria, Saxony did not like it at all - they had some idea what all this was about. But they all pinned their hopes on the country south of Germany: Austria. They hoped Austria was great enough and strong enough to stop Prussia from becoming master of Germany. They soon lost this hope.

於是 Prussia 的軍隊壯大了，它成為 Germany 各邦中最強大、訓練最精良的軍隊，而其他各邦——Bavaria、Saxony——完全不喜歡這個局面——他們多少猜到了這一切是為了什麼。但他們都把希望寄託在 Germany 南邊的國家：Austria。他們希望 Austria 足夠強大，能夠阻止 Prussia 成為 Germany 的主人。但他們很快就失去了這個希望。

In 1866 out of the blue and for very little reason, Bismarck started a war against Austria. After a shattering defeat, Austria begged for peace. The war was over in one month and Bismarck had shown the German states that none of them could hope to resist the Prussian army.

1866 年，Bismarck 毫無預警地、幾乎沒什麼理由地對 Austria 發動了戰爭。在一場慘敗之後，Austria 求和。戰爭一個月就結束了，Bismarck 已經向 Germany 各邦展示，他們中沒有任何一個能指望抵擋 Prussia 的軍隊。

There was still one great power to the west of Germany which could interfere with Bismarck's plans: France under the Emperor Napoleon III. Bismarck wanted a war with France, but he wanted France to declare the war to make it appear that Prussia was only defending herself.

在 Germany 西面還有一個可能干擾 Bismarck 計畫的大國：Napoleon 三世統治下的 France。Bismarck 想要與 France 開戰，但他要 France 來宣戰，好讓事情看起來像是 Prussia 只是在自衛。

And he managed it. First he falsified a message Napoleon III had sent to the Prussian King, so that it seemed as if this message was a French insult to Prussia. Of course, the Prussian newspapers printed fiery articles against the French, and the French newspapers answered by writing wildly against the Prussians. Newspapers had (and still have) the power to sway people's minds. In France and in Prussia people became convinced that the "national honour" was at stake, hatred between the two nations grew, and in the end, Napoleon III did exactly what Bismarck had wanted him to do, he declared war on Prussia.

他辦到了。首先，他竄改了 Napoleon 三世發給 Prussia 國王的一封信件，使它看起來像是 France 對 Prussia 的侮辱。當然，Prussia 的報紙印出了抨擊法國人的激烈文章，法國的報紙則以猛烈抨擊 Prussia 人的文章回敬。報紙過去有（現在仍然有）左右人心的力量。在 France 和 Prussia，人們都確信「國家榮譽」受到了威脅，兩國之間的仇恨日益增長，最終 Napoleon 三世做了 Bismarck 一直希望他做的事情——他向 Prussia 宣戰。

The war lasted two years, 1870-71 and ended, as Bismarck had foreseen, with the victory of the Prussians. In Paris a revolution broke out, Napoleon III had to flee and ended his days in England. France became a republic again.

戰爭持續了兩年（1870-71），結果如 Bismarck 所預見的，以 Prussia 人的勝利告終。在 Paris 爆發了革命，Napoleon 三世被迫逃亡，最終在 England 度過了餘生。France 再度成為共和國。

But while the Prussian troops were in Paris, Bismarck and the King of Prussia had made their quarters in the great palace of Versailles, once built as the pride of the Roi Soleil, Louis XV. And while they were at Versailles - the rulers of all the German states,

而當 Prussia 軍隊還在 Paris 時，Bismarck 和 Prussia 國王在偉大的 Versailles 宮殿——這座曾經是太陽王 Louis 十五的驕傲之作——設立了大本營。就在他們駐紮在 Versailles 期間——Germany 各邦的統治者，

[...原文此處因頁面斷裂而缺失...]

---

Chapter 49
The Turn of the Century

第四十九章
世紀之交

In the period from the end of the nineteenth to the beginning of the twentieth century there was what is sometimes called the second Industrial Revolution. From about 1880 onwards there was another great step forward which changed people's lives as much as or more than the first Industrial Revolution.

在十九世紀末到二十世紀初的這段時期，發生了所謂的第二次工業革命。大約從 1880 年起，又有一次巨大的躍進，它對人們生活的改變程度不亞於甚至超越了第一次工業革命。

The second Industrial Revolution was brought about by the introduction of two things: electricity and petrol.

第二次工業革命是由兩樣東西的引入所帶來的：電力和汽油。

With electricity, there came the possibility to send power over long distances through cables, so that the power station can be miles away from the house where electric light or heat is used. All that is required is a wire carrying the current from the station to the house.

有了電力，就有可能透過電纜把電能傳送到很遠的距離，因此發電站可以離使用電燈或電熱的房屋好幾英里遠。所需要的只是一條從發電站到房屋的電線來輸送電流。

And as the current can also be used for sound there came the telegraph and the telephone. Imagine how these things changed life.

而由於電流也可以用於傳送聲音，於是有了電報和電話。想像一下這些東西是如何改變了生活。

Thomas Edison invented the light bulb in 1879 - now one could have light at a turn of a switch. With the telegraph, which became popular in the 1840s, a written message could go across great distances in a few hours (taking down and repeating the message took the time). The telephone was invented by Alexander Graham Bell in 1876 and soon people could hear each other's voices over thousands of miles.

Thomas Edison 在 1879 年發明了燈泡——現在只要按一下開關就能有光。電報在 1840 年代開始普及，一則書面訊息可以在幾個小時內傳送到遙遠的地方（抄寫和轉發訊息需要時間）。電話由 Alexander Graham Bell 在 1876 年發明，很快人們就能在數千英里外聽到彼此的聲音。

And petrol came as a new source of power besides coal and steam. With the invention of the petrol engine by Karl Benz in 1885 came cars and vans and lorries, motor boats and aeroplanes. And the aeroplane made travelling faster than people had ever dreamed possible.

而汽油則成為除了煤和蒸汽之外的新動力來源。隨著 Karl Benz 在 1885 年發明了汽油引擎，汽車、貨車、卡車、汽艇和飛機相繼出現。飛機使旅行的速度快到超出人們曾經夢想的程度。

Now take just three things together: telegraph, telephone and aeroplane: they reduce distance. For a telegraph or a telephone call the distance from here to Australia is of no consequence. And by plane you can be in Australia in twenty-four hours.

現在只要把三樣東西放在一起想：電報、電話和飛機——它們縮短了距離。對一通電報或電話來說，從這裡到 Australia 的距離毫無影響。而搭飛機你可以在二十四小時內到達 Australia。

In ancient times the distance, let us say, between the Rome of the Caesars and China was so great that the Romans did not even know China existed, and the Chinese did not know about Rome. Nowadays you could telephone from Rome to Beijing, or fly the distance in a day. The earth has become small, distances have shrunk - that was the result of the second Industrial Revolution.

在古代，比方說 Caesar 時代的 Rome 和 China 之間的距離如此遙遠，以至於 Rome 人甚至不知道 China 的存在，China 人也不知道 Rome。如今你可以從 Rome 打電話到 Beijing，或者在一天之內飛完這段距離。地球變小了，距離縮短了——這就是第二次工業革命的結果。

But the question is, have the nations of the world really come nearer to each other in heart and soul through all this?

但問題是，透過這一切，世界上的國家在心靈和精神上真的彼此更加靠近了嗎？

We shall deal with this question by analysing what happened between the nations of the world while this second Industrial Revolution took place.

我們將透過分析第二次工業革命發生期間各國之間所發生的事情來探討這個問題。

To understand what happened, we must go back a few centuries, right back to Columbus, Pizarro, and Magellan, to the time of the great voyages.
