That was the time when Spain and Portugal were the first European nations to have colonies overseas. What was it that the Spaniards wanted most from their colonies? Gold, silver, treasure. And that was, for centuries, the only reason to have colonies. As long as they thought there was no gold there, the British Government was not even interested in Cook's discovery of Australia. It was just a place to send hardened criminals to.

要理解發生了什麼，我們必須回溯幾個世紀，一直回到 Columbus、Pizarro 和 Magellan 的時代，回到大航海時代。那是 Spain 和 Portugal 成為最早擁有海外殖民地的 Europe 國家的時代。Spain 人最想從殖民地得到什麼？金、銀、寶藏。而這在好幾個世紀裡，都是擁有殖民地的唯一理由。只要他們認為那裡沒有金子，British 政府連 Cook 發現 Australia 這件事都不感興趣。那只不過是一個流放重刑犯的地方。

But this simple idea of colonies had already changed with the first Industrial Revolution - for Britain with its cotton mills, a colony which grew cotton was not just useful, it was very important. And at the time of the second Industrial Revolution other things became important: copper for electrical cable, aluminium for planes, and of course, crude oil for petrol and diesel.

但這種對殖民地的簡單觀念在第一次工業革命時就已經改變了——對擁有棉紡廠的 Britain 來說，一個種植棉花的殖民地不只是有用，而是非常重要。到了第二次工業革命時期，其他東西也變得重要起來：製造電纜用的銅、製造飛機用的鋁，當然還有用來提煉汽油和柴油的原油。

The British, having been the first in the Industrial Revolution, were also the first to realize that there was wealth in colonies even if they did not have a scrap of gold or silver. And so Britain grabbed colonies where she could, especially in Africa; you never knew what special produce could be found or discovered that might one day become valuable.

British 人作為工業革命的先驅，也是最早意識到殖民地即使沒有一丁點金銀也蘊含著財富的人。因此 Britain 盡可能地搶佔殖民地，尤其是在 Africa；你永遠不知道什麼特殊的產物可能被發現，而有朝一日變得珍貴。

Of course, if there was a region in the world which did produce gold or diamonds - this too was to be taken, as you will see from the following story.

當然，如果世界上有個地方確實出產金子或鑽石——那也是要拿下的，正如你將從下面的故事中看到的。

In 1870, in the year Bismarck started the war between Prussia and France that ended with the defeat of France and with Germany becoming one nation, in that year a young Englishman, Cecil Rhodes, arrived in South Africa. Rhodes was an office clerk with very little education and very little money. He only came to South Africa because he had lung trouble, and the doctors had told him that the damp climate of Britain was bad for him; he should go to a dry, sunny climate, and so he went to South Africa. Rhodes, though he was not well educated, was clever, and he had that special cleverness that makes a good businessman. Shortly after his arrival in South Africa the first diamonds were found at Kimberly.

1870 年，就在 Bismarck 發動 Prussia 與 France 之間的戰爭——最終以 France 戰敗和 Germany 統一告終——的那一年，一個年輕的英國人 Cecil Rhodes 來到了 South Africa。Rhodes 是個辦公室小職員，受過很少的教育，也沒什麼錢。他來 South Africa 只是因為他有肺病，醫生告訴他 Britain 潮濕的氣候對他不好；他應該去乾燥、陽光充足的地方，於是他去了 South Africa。Rhodes 雖然教育程度不高，卻很聰明，而且他有那種能成為一個好商人的特殊精明。他抵達 South Africa 後不久，第一批鑽石就在 Kimberly 被發現了。

A "prospector" who had found a few diamonds and "registered his claim" had the right to mine on the little plot of land which he had registered. But such a prospector was never rich enough to buy machines or pay workers to mine deeper than three or four metres, and so he would sell his claim for a few hundred pounds and go on to look for more. And the man who went straight to Kimberly and bought dozens and dozens of these claims was Rhodes. He did not even have the money to buy, he borrowed the money. He took great risks for some plots he bought contained only a few tiny diamonds. He might have lost on his deals - but he did not.

一個「探礦者」如果發現了幾顆鑽石並「登記了他的礦權」，就有權在他登記的那小塊土地上開採。但這樣的探礦者從來沒有足夠的錢來購買機器或雇用工人挖掘超過三、四公尺深的地方，於是他會把礦權以幾百英鎊的價格賣掉，然後繼續去尋找。而那個直接跑到 Kimberly 買下一個又一個礦權的人就是 Rhodes。他甚至沒有錢來買，他是借錢的。他冒了很大的風險，因為他買的有些地塊裡只有幾顆小小的鑽石。他的交易可能會血本無歸——但他沒有。

As he now owned large areas he could get machinery to pump the water out the ever deeper holes and employ hundreds of men to continue digging deeper to find more diamonds. He could easily repay the borrowed money with interest and still have a fortune.

由於他現在擁有大片土地，他可以取得機器把越挖越深的坑裡的水抽出來，並雇用數百人繼續往更深處挖掘以尋找更多鑽石。他可以輕鬆地連本帶利償還借來的錢，而且仍然坐擁一筆財富。

These diamond-mines were in the British Cape Colony. But there were also two independent Boer Republics in South Africa, the Transvaal and the Orange Free State. The Boers were descendants of Dutch settlers.

這些鑽石礦位於 British 的 Cape Colony。但在 South Africa 還有兩個獨立的 Boer 共和國——Transvaal 和 Orange Free State。Boer 人是荷蘭移民的後裔。

It happened that gold was found in the Boer Republic of Transvaal, at Johannesburg. And thousands of British prospectors poured into the Boer Republic in search for gold. The Boers did not like this invasion - there was no end of trouble. Cecil Rhodes, who was by now a rich and very respected man, thought that the riches of Johannesburg should become British - the whole of South Africa should become British. At first he equipped - at his own expense - a little army and sent it into the Boer country, but the Boers drove the invaders out. And then Cecil Rhodes went to England, persuaded the British Government to make war against the Boers and to take possession of their lands.

事情是這樣的：在 Boer 共和國 Transvaal 的 Johannesburg 發現了金礦。成千上萬的 British 探礦者湧入 Boer 共和國尋找黃金。Boer 人不喜歡這種入侵——麻煩不斷。此時已經是富人且備受尊敬的 Cecil Rhodes 認為，Johannesburg 的財富應該歸 British 所有——整個 South Africa 都應該成為 British 的。起初他自掏腰包裝備了一支小軍隊並把它派進 Boer 人的國土，但 Boer 人把入侵者趕了出去。然後 Cecil Rhodes 前往 England，說服了 British 政府向 Boer 人開戰並奪取他們的土地。

And so in 1899 the Boer War started. With the British troops fighting against the Boers was a young English journalist, Winston Churchill, who had come to send reports and description of the battles to his newspaper in London. Being a journalist and not a soldier, Churchill should (like a Red Cross worker) not have taken part in fighting, nor should he have carried any weapon. But young Churchill did not much bother about rules and carried a revolver on him although he knew that if the Boers caught him and found the gun, they could shoot him for breaking the rules.

於是 1899 年，Boer 戰爭爆發了。在與 Boer 人作戰的 British 軍隊中，有一位年輕的英國記者 Winston Churchill，他是來為 London 的報社發回戰地報導和戰況描寫的。身為記者而非軍人，Churchill 本應（像紅十字會人員一樣）不參與戰鬥，也不應攜帶任何武器。但年輕的 Churchill 對規則不太在意，身上帶了一把左輪手槍，儘管他知道如果 Boer 人抓住他並找到那把槍，他們可以因為違規而槍斃他。

One day Churchill travelled with two companies of British troops in a train. Suddenly the train stopped with a crash and bullets came whistling through the windows, the train had run into a Boer ambush. The British found themselves surrounded on all sides by Boers and surrendered. Churchill too was taken prisoner and was brought before a Boer officer. At his command Churchill was searched and the revolver was found. The Boer officer would have been within his rights to have Churchill shot, but he took pity on the young man and spared his life. Churchill was sent to a prison camp.

有一天 Churchill 和兩連 British 軍隊一起乘坐火車。突然火車猛然停下，子彈從窗戶呼嘯而入——火車駛入了 Boer 人的埋伏。British 人發現自己被 Boer 人從四面八方包圍，只好投降。Churchill 也被俘虜了，被帶到一名 Boer 軍官面前。軍官下令搜身，左輪手槍被找到了。那名 Boer 軍官完全有權下令槍斃 Churchill，但他對這個年輕人動了惻隱之心，饒了他一命。Churchill 被送進了戰俘營。

Three weeks later Churchill escaped. But he was in enemy country, knew no word of their language and had no money. His only hope was to get out of the Boer country to a Portuguese colony in Africa. To get there he got into an empty truck on a train rolling in the right direction. All night he travelled, but in the morning the train rolled to a stop and Churchill quickly jumped off before he was discovered. He came to a farm and was lucky, for the farmer was English and kept him hidden for weeks in a rat-infested coal mine. At long last it was safe for Churchill to get into another empty truck on a train and, eventually, he came safely out of the Boer Republic and into the neutral Portuguese Colony. Four weeks later he was back with the British troops, but this time as an officer and to fight.

三週後 Churchill 逃脫了。但他身處敵國，一句他們的語言都不會說，也身無分文。他唯一的希望就是離開 Boer 人的國土，抵達 Africa 的一個 Portugal 殖民地。為了到達那裡，他爬上了一列朝著正確方向行駛的火車上的空車廂。他在夜裡旅行了整整一晚，但到了早上火車慢慢停了下來，Churchill 趕緊在被發現之前跳下車。他來到一座農場，很幸運，因為農場主人是英國人，把他藏在一個老鼠橫行的煤礦裡好幾個星期。終於等到安全的時候，Churchill 再次爬上另一列火車的空車廂，最終安全地離開了 Boer 共和國，進入了中立的 Portugal 殖民地。四個星期後他回到了 British 軍隊中，但這次是以軍官的身分，並且是來作戰的。

After a long and bitter struggle, the Boers lost the war, and their colony became a British colony. Many years later South Africa became a dominion - it remained British but had its own Prime Minister. The name of this first Prime Minister of South Africa was Jan Smuts, and he was the officer who had spared Churchill's life. He and Churchill became great friends and were allies in the two world wars that came.

經過漫長而慘烈的鬥爭，Boer 人輸掉了這場戰爭，他們的殖民地變成了 British 殖民地。多年後 South Africa 成為一個自治領——它仍然屬於 British 但擁有自己的總理。這位 South Africa 的第一任總理名叫 Jan Smuts，他就是當年那位饒了 Churchill 一命的軍官。他和 Churchill 成為了好朋友，並在後來爆發的兩次世界大戰中成為盟友。

For many years in South Africa, however, the Boers did not forgive the British for taking their colony by force of arms.

然而在 South Africa，Boer 人許多年來都無法原諒 British 人以武力奪走了他們的殖民地。

---

Chapter 50
The First World War

第五十章
第一次世界大戰

By the end of the nineteenth century, colonies became important for other products than gold, silver or diamonds; now copper, rubber, and oil were needed by the second Industrial Revolution. But there were other products too: coffee and tea became popular in Europe and a colony that produced coffee or tea was valuable.

到了十九世紀末，殖民地除了金、銀、鑽石之外，也因為其他產品而變得重要；第二次工業革命需要銅、橡膠和石油。但還有其他產品：咖啡和茶在 Europe 變得流行，一個生產咖啡或茶的殖民地就很有價值。

Marie Curie, a scientist, discovered a new element which no one had known existed, radium, which became much more valuable than gold. Radium is used for cancer treatment and used to be applied to watch numerals, as it shines in the dark (it was later found that this radioactive element was very dangerous to health, and so it is no longer used for watches). Some other rare metals, such as wolfram and tungsten, were found to be important for steel production, and aluminium, of which no one had taken notice before, became a metal much in demand, as it was strong and light.

科學家 Marie Curie 發現了一種以前沒人知道的新元素——鐳，它比黃金還要珍貴得多。鐳用於癌症治療，過去也被塗在錶面的數字上，因為它在暗處會發光（後來人們發現這種放射性元素對健康非常危險，因此不再用於手錶了）。其他一些稀有金屬，如鎢和鎢鋼，被發現對鋼鐵生產很重要，而以前沒有人注意到的鋁則成了一種需求量很大的金屬，因為它既堅固又輕便。

All these new things required by the second Industrial Revolution needed had to come from overseas, because they could not be found readily in Europe. As other countries in Europe became industrialized, they too wanted colonies to get all these raw materials. And, so other European nations rushed to colonise other lands and the people who lived there. France took large slices of north and west Africa and Indo-China, Germany got hold of parts of east and west Africa, Belgium got hold of a part of Central Africa, and Holland strengthened her hold on the Indonesian islands (Java, Sumatra) in Asia. In short, it was like a race, with everyone trying to catch up with Britain.

第二次工業革命所需的所有這些新事物都必須從海外取得，因為在 Europe 很難找到。隨著 Europe 其他國家工業化，它們也想要殖民地來獲取這些原材料。於是其他 European 國家紛紛搶著殖民其他地方和當地的人民。France 佔據了北非和西非的大片地區以及印度支那，Germany 拿下了東非和西非的部分地區，Belgium 佔據了中非的一部分，而 Holland 加強了對亞洲 Indonesia 群島（Java、Sumatra）的控制。簡而言之，這就像一場比賽，每個國家都想趕上 Britain。

It was the Industrial Revolution that was the driving force behind this grabbing of colonies, the Industrial Revolution with its need for all kinds of new raw materials.

工業革命是這場殖民地爭奪背後的驅動力，工業革命需要各式各樣的新原材料。

Britain had been the first in this race for colonies, with France following behind, and some way farther back came Germany.

在這場殖民地競賽中，Britain 是最先起跑的，France 緊隨其後，再後面一些是 Germany。

The British Government was not very pleased with all the other countries doing what the British had done. For nearly a century Britain had the largest colonial empire in the world. And Britain had also built up the greatest navy in the world. Now other nations not only acquired colonies and built large navies, becoming competitors, and a threat to Britain's wealth and power. Britain regarded Germany as a more dangerous threat than France.

British 政府對其他國家都在做 British 人做過的事並不太高興。將近一個世紀以來，Britain 擁有世界上最大的殖民帝國。Britain 也建立了世界上最強大的海軍。如今其他國家不僅取得了殖民地，還建立了龐大的海軍，成為了競爭者，並對 Britain 的財富和權力構成了威脅。Britain 認為 Germany 是比 France 更危險的威脅。

Ever since Bismarck's time, the Germans had continued to build up a strong army. German industries in the Ruhr and elsewhere were soon larger than Britain's, German colonies had been established in Africa, and then under Emperor William II, Germany began to build up a navy that might one day equal that of Britain.

自從 Bismarck 的時代起，Germany 人就一直在建設一支強大的軍隊。Ruhr 和其他地方的 Germany 工業很快就超過了 Britain，Germany 的殖民地已在 Africa 建立，接著在 William 二世皇帝的統治下，Germany 開始建設一支有朝一日可能與 Britain 匹敵的海軍。

Not only did the British Government regard Germany as a danger, but France too (still smarting since the lost war of 1870-71) feared the growing power of Germany, and the Tsar of Russia was afraid that Germany might attack her with her great army.

不只 British 政府視 Germany 為威脅，France（在 1870-71 年戰敗的傷痛仍未平息）也害怕 Germany 日益增長的力量，而 Russia 的沙皇則擔心 Germany 會用她的強大軍隊攻擊 Russia。

And so Britain, France and Russia formed a great alliance, the Entente Cordiale, agreeing that if any one of them was attacked, the others would come to that country's aid. Of course, the name of Germany was not even mentioned in this agreement, but they had no doubt who was meant.

於是 Britain、France 和 Russia 組成了一個偉大的同盟——友好協約，約定如果其中任何一國遭到攻擊，其他國家將前來援助。當然，在這份協議中甚至沒有提到 Germany 的名字，但他們心知肚明指的是誰。

But now the Germans felt threatened by this great alliance against them - they saw themselves threatened from east and west and north. But the Germans on their part also found an ally in the Austro-Hungarian Empire.

但現在 Germany 人感到被這個針對他們的大同盟所威脅——他們覺得自己從東面、西面和北面都受到了威脅。但 Germany 人也為自己找到了一個盟友——Austro-Hungarian 帝國。

And so, from the early years of this century onwards, there were two major powers in Europe; Britain, France, Russia on one side, Germany and Austria on the other. And in all these countries armies were strengthened and enlarged, navies were built up, and Europe became increasingly like a powder keg that just needed a spark to explode.

就這樣，從這個世紀初開始，Europe 形成了兩大陣營：一邊是 Britain、France、Russia，另一邊是 Germany 和 Austria。在所有這些國家裡，軍隊不斷壯大和擴充，海軍不斷建設，Europe 越來越像一個火藥桶，只需一個火花就會爆炸。

The spark came in 1914. The Crown Prince of Austria, the heir to the Austrian throne, was assassinated in Sarajevo. The murderer escaped to neighbouring Serbia. The Austrians demanded that the murderer should be handed over to them, and while the Serbian Government hesitated, the Austrian army marched into Serbia. But Serbia had an alliance with Russia, and so Russia declared war on Austria.

火花在 1914 年出現了。Austria 的皇太子——Austria 王位的繼承人——在 Sarajevo 被刺殺。兇手逃到了鄰國 Serbia。Austria 人要求將兇手交出，而當 Serbia 政府猶豫不決時，Austria 軍隊開進了 Serbia。但 Serbia 與 Russia 有同盟關係，因此 Russia 向 Austria 宣戰。

And now all the other alliances came in: Germany had to help Austria and declared war on Russia; France and Britain declared war on Germany and Austria, and so the First World War started. It became, indeed, a world war because it was fought not only in Europe, but in the colonies as well - the British and French colonies sent troops to the battlefields of Europe. It was a world war because, in the end, America, too, came in on the side of Britain and against Germany.

現在所有其他的同盟都被牽動了：Germany 必須幫助 Austria，向 Russia 宣戰；France 和 Britain 向 Germany 和 Austria 宣戰，第一次世界大戰就這樣開始了。它確實成為了一場世界大戰，因為戰場不僅在 Europe，也在殖民地——British 和 French 的殖民地派遣了軍隊到 Europe 的戰場。它之所以是世界大戰，也因為最終 America 也站在 Britain 一邊、反對 Germany 參戰了。

It was a terrible war - never before had human lives been sacrificed in war in such large numbers. In the two-day Battle of Passchendaele alone over half a million men were lost - and still the war went on. It was during this terrible First World War that aeroplanes were used for the first time, and for the first time tanks went into action. For the first time submarines attacked surface ships, and for the first time poison gas was used.

這是一場可怕的戰爭——在此之前，從未有過如此大量的人命在戰爭中被犧牲。僅僅在為期兩天的 Passchendaele 戰役中就有超過五十萬人喪生——而戰爭仍在繼續。正是在這場可怕的第一次世界大戰中，飛機第一次被用於戰爭，坦克第一次投入戰場。潛艇第一次攻擊水面船隻，毒氣也第一次被使用。

One could say, that in the First World War, the Industrial Revolution came to the armies and to the battlefield. What Leonardo da Vinci had feared: that machines would make war more terrible, became true in the First World War.

可以說，在第一次世界大戰中，工業革命來到了軍隊和戰場上。Leonardo da Vinci 曾經擔心的事——機器會使戰爭更加可怕——在第一次世界大戰中成為了現實。

Finally the First World War ended with the defeat of Germany and Austria in 1918. But before the end, while Germany was still fighting on, something happened which was, perhaps more important than the whole war. In 1917 Germany and Austria were still fighting on but already exhausted. Was there any way in which they could knock out at least one of their enemies, Russia? There was one way: causing a revolution. If there was a revolution against the Tsar in Russia, and civil war, the Russians would fight each other instead of Germany.

第一次世界大戰最終在 1918 年以 Germany 和 Austria 的戰敗告終。但在戰爭結束之前，當 Germany 還在繼續戰鬥時，發生了一件也許比整場戰爭還重要的事。1917 年，Germany 和 Austria 仍在作戰但已經精疲力竭。有沒有什麼辦法能至少擊敗他們的一個敵人 Russia？有一個辦法：引發一場革命。如果 Russia 爆發反對沙皇的革命和內戰，Russia 人就會互相打起來，而不是跟 Germany 打了。

The Russians hated the Tsar Nicholas who had plunged Russia into war that had already cost the lives of two million Russians. They hated the Tsar who would not allow more freedom, and, in fact, the Tsar was forced by his own generals to abdicate and a democratic government took over. But this new government continued the war against Germany.

Russia 人痛恨沙皇 Nicholas，他把 Russia 拖入了一場已經奪走兩百萬 Russia 人生命的戰爭。他們痛恨這個不允許更多自由的沙皇，而事實上，沙皇被他自己的將軍們逼迫退位，一個民主政府接管了政權。但這個新政府繼續對 Germany 作戰。

And now the Germans had to think how to start another revolution in Russia, a revolution against this democratic Government.

而現在 Germany 人必須想辦法在 Russia 再次引發一場革命——一場反對這個民主政府的革命。

There were two Russians living in Switzerland who were the leaders of the Russian Communists, followers of Karl Marx. Their names were Lenin (Vladimir Ilyitch Ulianov was his real name) and Trotsky. They had both fled from Russia before the War, but they were secretly in contact with fellow-Communists inside Russia.

有兩個住在 Switzerland 的 Russia 人是 Russia 共產黨的領袖，Karl Marx 的追隨者。他們的名字是 Lenin（Vladimir Ilyitch Ulianov 是他的本名）和 Trotsky。他們倆都在戰前逃離了 Russia，但他們秘密地與 Russia 國內的共產黨同志保持聯繫。

What the German generals thought was this: if we get Lenin and his friend Trotsky back to Russia, they will start a Communist revolution, and that will stop the Russians fighting against Germany.

Germany 將軍們的想法是這樣的：如果我們把 Lenin 和他的朋友 Trotsky 送回 Russia，他們就會發動共產革命，這樣 Russia 人就不會再跟 Germany 打仗了。

And this was what really happened; Lenin could not have gone to Russia without going through Germany; he could never have gone through Germany without the permission of the German Generals. It was the German Generals who offered Lenin and Trotsky a free passage through Germany to the Russian border. In sealed railway carriages the two Communist leaders passed through Germany and entered Russia via Finland in disguise. There they started the Communist revolution. Lenin promised peace, and the peasants, tired of war, followed him. On the night of November 6-7, 1917, the democratic government was thrown out by armed Communists, Lenin took power and Russia became the first Communist country in the world. The Tsar and his family were shot by the Communists.

事實正是如此。Lenin 不經過 Germany 就不可能回到 Russia；沒有 Germany 將軍們的許可，他絕不可能通過 Germany。正是 Germany 將軍們為 Lenin 和 Trotsky 提供了穿越 Germany 到 Russia 邊境的免費通行。在密封的火車車廂中，兩位共產黨領袖穿越 Germany，喬裝經由 Finland 進入了 Russia。在那裡他們發動了共產革命。Lenin 許諾和平，厭倦了戰爭的農民們跟隨了他。在 1917 年 11 月 6 日至 7 日的夜晚，民主政府被武裝的共產黨人推翻，Lenin 奪取了政權，Russia 成為世界上第一個共產主義國家。沙皇和他的家人被共產黨人槍殺了。

Nevertheless, in the end, a year later, Germany and Austria lost the war. But without the help of the German generals, there may not have been a Communist Russia, Lenin would have stayed in Switzerland, and Russia may have become a democratic country.

然而最終，一年之後，Germany 和 Austria 還是輸掉了這場戰爭。但如果沒有 Germany 將軍們的幫助，可能就不會有共產主義的 Russia，Lenin 會留在 Switzerland，而 Russia 可能會成為一個民主國家。

That was a significant outcome of the First World War, that one of the greatest countries in the world became Communist. The other result was that Germany and Austria were defeated and the defeat brought great changes to these two countries.

這是第一次世界大戰的一個重大結果——世界上最偉大的國家之一成為了共產主義國家。另一個結果是 Germany 和 Austria 戰敗了，而這場失敗給這兩個國家帶來了巨大的變化。

---

Chapter 51
The Rise of Nationalism

第五十一章
民族主義的興起

In the old days a war in Europe, let us say between France and Germany, meant conflict in Europe only. But with the Industrial Revolution came the need for raw materials and for colonies so any war in Europe also brought war in the colonies, and so became a world war.

在過去，一場發生在 Europe 的戰爭，比方說 France 和 Germany 之間的戰爭，只意味著 Europe 的衝突。但隨著工業革命帶來了對原材料和殖民地的需求，任何在 Europe 的戰爭也會把戰火帶到殖民地，從而變成世界大戰。

This is the other side of the Industrial Revolution. While railways, steamships, aeroplanes, telegraph and telephone made distance unimportant and brought countries closer together as if the earth had shrunk, it also meant that any conflict in one spot could spread rapidly over the whole globe.

這是工業革命的另一面。鐵路、蒸汽船、飛機、電報和電話使距離變得不再重要，讓各國彼此更加靠近，彷彿地球縮小了，但這同時也意味著任何一個地方的衝突都可能迅速蔓延到全球。

This is something people did not realize in 1914 when the First World War started, but it is high time that we know it and realize it. The modern means of communication have made the earth into one big village, and a fire that starts in one corner of that village can set all the huts aflame.

這是 1914 年第一次世界大戰爆發時人們還沒有意識到的事，但我們早該認識和理解這一點了。現代的通訊方式已經把地球變成了一個大村莊，而在這個村莊的一個角落燃起的火，可以燒光所有的房屋。

In the past people said that all humanity is one family, but it was just a beautiful idea. Today it is no longer an idea, it is a fact brought about by the means of mass communication. We are one family living in one village, called earth. It is a fact, not a hope or a dream.

過去人們說全人類是一家人，但那只是一個美好的理想。今天它不再是一個理想，它是大眾傳播方式帶來的事實。我們是一個家庭，住在一個叫做地球的村莊裡。這是事實，不是希望或夢想。

Today the thought: "My nation comes first, and never mind all the others" is alien and two hundred or three hundred years in the past. Nationalism, which means wanting advantages for your own nation without caring if others suffer, in our time, is just as outdated as people still wandering around wearing suits of armour.

今天，「我的國家優先，其他人無所謂」這種想法是陌生的，是兩三百年前的老觀念。民族主義——也就是只想為自己的國家謀取利益而不管別人是否受苦——在我們的時代，就像人們還穿著盔甲到處走一樣過時了。

But, unfortunately, after the First World War, the world had not yet learned this lesson, its nations became not less but more nationalistic. They became more selfish as nations, and so nationalism - national selfishness - prepared the way for another catastrophe: the Second World War.

但不幸的是，第一次世界大戰之後，世界還沒有學會這個教訓，各國不但沒有減少反而更加民族主義了。作為國家它們變得更加自私，而民族主義——國家的自私——為另一場災難鋪好了道路：第二次世界大戰。

Let us take one example of blind, selfish nationalism. Before the First World War, the Austro-Hungarian Empire was a union of several nationalities: there was one part where the people spoke German, there was one part where the people spoke Slavic languages, and another where the people spoke Hungarian, and there were still others. It was a great advantage to these small nationalities that they could live together in one great state and trade with each other. But in 1918 when Austria lost the First World War, revolutions broke out. The last Austrian Emperor had to flee, and instead of staying together in one great republic, each nationality set up their own republic and so came new states: Czechoslovakia, Hungary, Yugoslavia, Poland, and German-speaking Austria as it is today.

讓我們舉一個盲目、自私的民族主義的例子。第一次世界大戰之前，Austro-Hungarian 帝國是多個民族的聯合體：有一部分的人說德語，有一部分的人說斯拉夫語，另一部分的人說匈牙利語，還有其他民族。這些小民族能夠一起生活在一個大國家裡並互相貿易，這是一個巨大的優勢。但 1918 年當 Austria 在第一次世界大戰中戰敗時，革命爆發了。最後一位 Austria 皇帝被迫逃亡，各民族不是團結在一個大共和國裡，而是各自建立了自己的共和國，於是出現了新的國家：Czechoslovakia、Hungary、Yugoslavia、Poland，以及今天的說德語的 Austria。

All these little states only came into existence in 1918 after the First World War. And they did not work together but against each other, they were nationalistic and jealous of each other.

所有這些小國家都是在第一次世界大戰之後的 1918 年才出現的。而它們不是彼此合作，而是彼此對抗，它們都是民族主義的，而且互相嫉妒。

Take another example that was even worse. Italy, the land of Garibaldi, had been in the First World War on the side of Britain and France, but the Italian soldiers had suffered many defeats from the Austrians, and Italy had no reason to be proud when the war ended. There was great poverty in the land and many Italian factory workers became Communists. And this frightened the Italian capitalists. They were afraid that Italy would become Communist, like Russia and they would lose their factories and estates, they would lose their wealth. And just then a man appeared who claimed he could save Italy from Communism; he was a journalist by profession, and his name was Benito Mussolini.

再舉一個更糟糕的例子。Italy——Garibaldi 的故鄉——在第一次世界大戰中站在 Britain 和 France 一邊，但 Italy 士兵遭受了 Austria 人的多次打擊，戰爭結束時 Italy 沒有什麼值得驕傲的。國內極度貧困，許多 Italy 工廠工人成為了共產黨員。這嚇壞了 Italy 的資本家。他們害怕 Italy 會像 Russia 一樣變成共產主義國家，他們會失去工廠和莊園，失去財富。就在這時，一個人出現了，聲稱他可以把 Italy 從共產主義手中拯救出來；他的職業是記者，名字叫 Benito Mussolini。

Mussolini claimed that democracy, parliament and freedom, had spoiled and ruined the Italian people - that Italy needed one strong man, one leader with absolute power, a dictator and that this dictator would make Italy a world power as ancient Rome had been. Of course this great leader could be no one else but Mussolini himself.

Mussolini 聲稱民主、議會和自由已經腐化和毀壞了 Italy 人民——Italy 需要一個強人，一個擁有絕對權力的領袖，一個獨裁者，而這個獨裁者將使 Italy 像古代的 Rome 一樣成為一個世界強國。當然這個偉大的領袖除了 Mussolini 本人不可能是別人。

Mussolini as dictator would certainly not allow Communism, and so the capitalists of Italy supported him with large gifts of money. Mussolini used the money to arm and train a private army whose uniform was black - Blackshirts. Garibaldi, the fighter for freedom, had given his men red shirts. Mussolini, the fighter against freedom, gave his men black shirts. And in 1922 Mussolini marched his army of thirty thousand Blackshirts into Rome, and forced the Italian Parliament to give him absolute power. Mussolini became Dictator of Italy.

Mussolini 作為獨裁者當然不會允許共產主義，因此 Italy 的資本家用大量的金錢資助他。Mussolini 用這些錢武裝和訓練了一支穿黑色制服的私人軍隊——黑衫軍。Garibaldi，為自由而戰的鬥士，給他的部下穿紅衫。Mussolini，反對自由的鬥士，給他的部下穿黑衫。1922 年，Mussolini 率領他的三萬黑衫軍進軍 Rome，逼迫 Italy 議會賦予他絕對的權力。Mussolini 成為了 Italy 的獨裁者。

As dictator Mussolini made an end of all political parties in Italy. All parties were forbidden, the party leaders were imprisoned, and especially the Communists were ruthlessly persecuted. No paper or book could appear which criticized the dictator. All newspapers had to praise Mussolini and all newspapers had to preach wild, fanatical nationalism. In all schools children had to be drilled to look up to Mussolini with awe and reverence, and the whole Italian nation was drilled to fight for him and for the glory of Italy, as the greatest nation in the world. It was nationalism gone mad.

作為獨裁者，Mussolini 取締了 Italy 所有的政黨。所有政黨被禁止，黨的領袖被投入監獄，共產黨人尤其遭到殘酷的迫害。沒有任何報紙或書籍可以批評獨裁者。所有報紙都必須讚頌 Mussolini，所有報紙都必須宣揚狂熱的民族主義。在所有學校裡，孩子們都要被訓練成懷著敬畏和崇拜仰望 Mussolini，整個 Italy 民族都被訓練為他而戰、為 Italy 的榮耀而戰，因為 Italy 是世界上最偉大的國家。這是瘋狂到了極點的民族主義。

It seems strange now, but Britain and France were at first quite pleased with this enemy of freedom, the dictator Mussolini. After all, he kept the Communists down, and that was for the greater good. They did not realize that nationalism was a danger.

現在看來很奇怪，但 Britain 和 France 起初對這個自由的敵人——獨裁者 Mussolini——還相當滿意。畢竟他壓制了共產黨人，而這是為了更大的利益。他們沒有意識到民族主義才是一個危險。

The example of Mussolini caught on in Germany. Germany had lost the First World War, she had lost her colonies, her soldiers had died in vain. The poverty was even worse than in Italy, and hundreds and thousands of workers were out of jobs. In Germany, too, the Emperor had been chased away and the country was ruled by a parliament, but this German Parliament could do nothing to help the poverty and the mass unemployment.

Mussolini 的榜樣在 Germany 引起了效仿。Germany 輸掉了第一次世界大戰，失去了殖民地，她的士兵白白送了命。貧困比 Italy 還嚴重，成千上萬的工人失業。在 Germany，皇帝也被趕走了，國家由議會統治，但這個 Germany 議會對貧困和大規模的失業束手無策。

The victorious powers, Britain, France, America could have helped by giving Germany money, but they were too selfish, too nationalist, to help a former enemy. Quite the contrary, every year Germany had to pay large sums, millions of pounds, as a kind of punishment to the victorious nations.

戰勝國 Britain、France、America 本可以透過給 Germany 金錢來幫助她，但他們太自私、太民族主義了，不願幫助一個曾經的敵人。恰恰相反，每一年 Germany 都必須向戰勝國支付巨額賠款——數百萬英鎊——作為一種懲罰。

It is no wonder that the German people became desperate, and that in their despair, they were willing to listen to a man who promised to become a German Mussolini, a great leader who would once again make Germany a great and powerful nation. The name of this German leader was Adolf Hitler.

難怪 Germany 人民變得絕望，在絕望中他們願意聆聽一個承諾要成為 Germany 版 Mussolini 的人——一個將再次使 Germany 成為偉大而強盛國家的偉大領袖。這個 Germany 領袖的名字就是 Adolf Hitler。

If Mussolini's nationalism was mad, Hitler's brand of nationalism was an evil insanity. According to Hitler the Germans were chosen by destiny to be a master race and to rule the world. All other races and nations in the world were inferior, in fact they were hardly human at all. According to Hitler, people of colour were no better than animals and should be treated as such. But Hitler's special hatred and contempt was for the Jews, the Jews should be exterminated like vermin, like rats.

如果說 Mussolini 的民族主義是瘋狂的，那 Hitler 的民族主義品牌就是一種邪惡的瘋狂。根據 Hitler 的說法，Germany 人是被命運選中的優等種族，注定要統治世界。世界上所有其他種族和國家都是低等的，事實上他們幾乎算不上是人。根據 Hitler 的說法，有色人種跟動物沒什麼兩樣，應該被當作動物對待。但 Hitler 特別的仇恨和蔑視指向猶太人——猶太人應該像害蟲、像老鼠一樣被消滅。

It seems strange that people could fall for these mad ideas, after all the German Jews had fought as soldiers in the German army like every other German. But the fact is that Hitler did gain a large following in Germany and, in 1933, eleven years after Mussolini, he became Führer of Germany.

人們居然會相信這些瘋狂的想法似乎很奇怪，畢竟 Germany 的猶太人和每一個 Germany 人一樣都曾作為士兵在 Germany 軍隊中戰鬥過。但事實是 Hitler 確實在 Germany 獲得了大量追隨者，1933 年，在 Mussolini 之後十一年，他成為了 Germany 的元首。

In Germany, too, any opinion that was opposed to Hitler was suppressed - newspapers and books preached only the idea that the Germans were superior to other nations and races and that Hitler was a genius who could never be wrong. Having lost the First World War Germany was preparing for a second one which, led by Hitler, they thought they could not lose.

在 Germany，任何反對 Hitler 的意見也同樣被壓制——報紙和書籍只宣傳 Germany 人優於其他民族和種族、Hitler 是一個永遠不會犯錯的天才的思想。在輸掉第一次世界大戰後，Germany 正在準備第二次世界大戰，他們認為在 Hitler 的領導下不可能會輸。

Not all Germans fell for Hitler's nationalism - there were thousands who recognized the evil - but anyone who spoke out openly was sent to the concentration camps where inhuman conditions and cruel treatment brought a lingering death, so it was safer to keep silent. A number of Jews fled from Germany. Others, especially elderly people, stayed. They hoped Hitler would spare old people who could do no harm. They were mistaken.

並非所有 Germany 人都被 Hitler 的民族主義所蒙蔽——有數以千計的人看穿了這個邪惡——但任何公開發聲的人都被送進集中營，在那裡非人的環境和殘酷的對待帶來了緩慢的死亡，所以保持沉默更安全。一部分猶太人逃離了 Germany。其他人，尤其是老年人，留了下來。他們希望 Hitler 會放過不會造成傷害的老人。他們錯了。

Once Hitler had built up a vast army, he set out on his path of conquest. He was actually Austrian - and the first country he took was Austria (the German-speaking part was all that was left of the Austro-Hungarian Empire). There was no fighting - most Austrians were pleased; they thought it was a good thing to be a part of Hitler's Greater Germany. They were mistaken, but it was too late when they realized it.

一旦 Hitler 建立了龐大的軍隊，他就踏上了征服之路。他其實是 Austria 人——而他佔領的第一個國家就是 Austria（說德語的那部分是 Austro-Hungarian 帝國所剩下的全部）。沒有戰鬥——大多數 Austria 人很高興；他們認為成為 Hitler 大 Germany 的一部分是好事。他們錯了，但當他們意識到時已經太遲了。

Then Hitler and Mussolini, the two dictators, formed an alliance and the other European nations - Britain and France, but also the small nations, Czechoslovakia, Poland, Yugoslavia - realized that there was now a new and terrible power in Europe: a fanatical, mad nationalism led by ruthless dictators and in command of vast, well-armed and well-trained armies.

接著 Hitler 和 Mussolini 這兩個獨裁者結成了同盟，而其他 European 國家——Britain 和 France，以及小國 Czechoslovakia、Poland、Yugoslavia——都意識到 Europe 現在出現了一個新的可怕力量：由殘忍的獨裁者領導的狂熱、瘋狂的民族主義，掌控著龐大的、裝備精良且訓練有素的軍隊。

---

Chapter 52
The Second World War

第五十二章
第二次世界大戰

Britain and France were well aware that Hitler and Mussolini were getting ready for another war, but there were also people in the British Government who believed that Hitler would use his great armies to war against Russia only - against the Communists. And so they did nothing to stop him when he marched his armies into Czechoslovakia and took the Sudetenland, a large German-speaking slice of that country.

Britain 和 France 很清楚 Hitler 和 Mussolini 正在為另一場戰爭做準備，但 British 政府中也有人相信 Hitler 只會用他的大軍去攻打 Russia——攻打共產黨人。因此當他率軍進入 Czechoslovakia 並佔領了 Sudetenland——該國一大片說德語的地區——時，他們沒有採取任何行動去阻止他。

But Britain and France did warn Hitler that if he attacked any other country they would oppose him. Hitler was so certain that the British would not go to war that he ignored the warning and in 1939 German troops invaded Poland and conquered the country in a few days.

但 Britain 和 France 確實警告了 Hitler，如果他攻擊其他國家，他們將會反對他。Hitler 如此確信 British 人不會開戰，以至於他無視了警告，1939 年 Germany 軍隊入侵了 Poland，幾天之內就征服了這個國家。

By now Britain and France knew that there could be no peace with Hitler, no peace with his mad nationalism. They declared war on Germany and so in 1939 the Second World War began.

此時 Britain 和 France 知道與 Hitler 不可能有和平，與他瘋狂的民族主義不可能有和平。他們向 Germany 宣戰，1939 年第二次世界大戰就此開始。

At first the Germans won battle after battle - they conquered the whole of France; they struck north and took Norway by surprise. The cities of Britain were bombed night after night by the German air force.

起初 Germany 人一場接一場地打勝仗——他們征服了整個 France；他們向北突擊，出其不意地佔領了 Norway。Britain 的城市夜復一夜地遭受 Germany 空軍的轟炸。

It was in this dark and hopeless stage of the war that Winston Churchill became Prime Minister of Britain and kept the spirit of courage and defiance alive in the British people.

就在這場戰爭最黑暗、最絕望的階段，Winston Churchill 成為了 Britain 的首相，在 British 人民心中保持著勇氣和抗爭的精神。

It needed great courage not to give in, for the Germans and Italians occupied the whole Balkan peninsula - Yugoslavia, Romania, Greece, and crossed over to North Africa. Only a small British army in Egypt stood against them. On the seas the German submarines attacked the convoys, the fleets of ships which brought food to Britain, and troops and arms from Britain to the colonies.

不屈服需要巨大的勇氣，因為 Germany 人和 Italy 人佔領了整個巴爾幹半島——Yugoslavia、Romania、Greece，並且跨海到了北非。只有在 Egypt 的一支小型 British 軍隊在抵抗他們。在海上，Germany 潛艇攻擊護航船隊——那些為 Britain 運送食物、從 Britain 向殖民地運送軍隊和武器的船隊。

No one knows what would have happened if Hitler had decided to invade Britain. He was at the height of his power - except for Spain, and the neutral countries of Switzerland and Sweden, the whole of the European continent was in his power - when he decided to attack Russia. In 1942 the German armies marched into Russia. And now history repeated itself. What had happened to Napoleon and his Grande Armée also happened to the German Armies.

沒有人知道如果 Hitler 決定入侵 Britain 會發生什麼。他正處於權力的巔峰——除了 Spain 以及中立國 Switzerland 和 Sweden，整個 Europe 大陸都在他的掌控之下——這時他決定進攻 Russia。1942 年 Germany 軍隊開進了 Russia。而現在歷史重演了。曾經發生在 Napoleon 和他的大軍身上的事，也同樣發生在了 Germany 軍隊身上。

They marched on and on, the Russian armies went back before them but destroyed all the crops. Only this time the German armies did not enter Moscow: at Moscow the Russians made a stand, and the Germans could not break through the Russian defence. Just like Napoleon's soldiers the German armies were caught by the terrible Russian Winter, and although they did not go back (as Napoleon had done), they suffered terrible losses in the Russian winter.

他們一路挺進，Russia 軍隊在他們面前後撤，但摧毀了所有的莊稼。只是這一次 Germany 軍隊沒有進入 Moscow：在 Moscow，Russia 人堅守陣地，Germany 人無法突破 Russia 的防線。就像 Napoleon 的士兵一樣，Germany 軍隊被可怕的 Russia 嚴冬所困，雖然他們沒有撤退（不像 Napoleon 那樣），但在 Russia 的冬天中遭受了慘烈的損失。

While all this happened in Europe, the Japanese, another ally of Hitler struck in the East. Out of the blue and without warning the Japanese air force attacked the American fleet at Pearl Harbour in Hawaii, sinking nearly all the American ships there. The Japanese then invaded the Philippines and went on to take the British colonies of Hong Kong, Malaya and Singapore, and the Dutch colonies, Java and Sumatra (which later became Indonesia).

當這一切在 Europe 發生時，Hitler 的另一個盟友日本在東方發動了攻擊。在毫無預警的情況下，日本空軍突襲了停泊在 Hawaii 的 Pearl Harbour 的美國艦隊，擊沉了那裡幾乎所有的美國船艦。接著日本入侵了 Philippines，並繼續佔領了 British 殖民地 Hong Kong、Malaya 和 Singapore，以及荷蘭殖民地 Java 和 Sumatra（後來成為 Indonesia）。

However, now Britain was no longer alone, the two greatest world powers, America and Russia were on her side.

然而，現在 Britain 不再孤軍奮戰了，世界上兩個最強大的國家——America 和 Russia——站在她這一邊。

And Hitler, vast as the German army was, had not only to fight the Russians in the East, but to guard the whole coastline of Europe from Denmark to Greece, against a possible invasion from the sea.

而 Hitler，儘管 Germany 軍隊龐大，不僅要在東面對抗 Russia 人，還要守衛從 Denmark 到 Greece 的整個 Europe 海岸線，以防來自海上的入侵。

And the invasion came, first in the Mediterranean. The British forces had driven the Germans from North Africa, and together with the Americans, they crossed over to Italy. In Italy a revolution against Mussolini broke out and eventually he was shot by his own people. The Germans still had armies in Italy, but they were finally driven back.

入侵來了，首先是在地中海。British 部隊把 Germany 人趕出了北非，並與 America 人一起跨海進入 Italy。在 Italy 爆發了反對 Mussolini 的革命，最終他被自己的人民槍殺了。Germany 人在 Italy 仍有軍隊，但最終被擊退了。

In the meantime, British and American air forces bombed Germany creating much worse destruction than the Germans had ever inflicted on Britain. Eventually in 1944, combined British and American forces under the American General Eisenhower invaded France.

與此同時，British 和 American 空軍轟炸 Germany，造成的破壞遠比 Germany 人對 Britain 造成的嚴重得多。最終在 1944 年，在 American 將軍 Eisenhower 的指揮下，英美聯軍入侵了 France。

Attacked from west and south and east, the German armies fought on, but now the odds were against them. In 1945 the German war machines collapsed, and as the victorious Russians poured into Berlin, Hitler committed suicide in his bunker.

從西面、南面和東面受到攻擊，Germany 軍隊仍在繼續戰鬥，但現在形勢對他們不利了。1945 年 Germany 的戰爭機器崩潰了，當勝利的 Russia 軍隊湧入 Berlin 時，Hitler 在他的地堡裡自殺了。

The other German leaders were brought before a court in Nuremberg. They were found guilty of having ordered the mass-murder of millions of civilians in concentration camps. Six million Jews had been exterminated, as well as Poles, Russians, and anti-Hitler Germans. Most of these leaders were hanged, others received long prison sentences.

其他 Germany 領導人被帶到 Nuremberg 的法庭上受審。他們被認定犯有下令在集中營中大規模屠殺數百萬平民的罪行。六百萬猶太人被滅絕，還有 Poland 人、Russia 人和反 Hitler 的 Germany 人。這些領導人中大多數被絞死，其他人則被判處長期監禁。

Germany had suffered terribly in the war, her cities were rubble heaps, her sons lay on battlefields all over Europe, her industries were destroyed. That was the price Germany paid for nationalism.

Germany 在戰爭中遭受了巨大的苦難，她的城市變成了瓦礫堆，她的兒子們躺在 Europe 各地的戰場上，她的工業被摧毀了。這就是 Germany 為民族主義所付出的代價。

But, unfortunately the victorious allies were soon quarrelling amongst themselves - Russian on one side, America, Britain, France on the other. The result of this quarrel was that the Russians made the eastern part of Germany they had occupied a Communist state (the German Democratic Republic), and the western part of Germany, which was occupied by American, British and French troops, became the Federal Republic of Germany with a parliament in Bonn. Berlin, in the middle of eastern Germany, was similarly divided, leaving an island of western Germany in the east.

但不幸的是，勝利的盟國很快就開始互相爭吵——Russia 一邊，America、Britain、France 一邊。這場爭吵的結果是，Russia 人把他們佔領的 Germany 東部變成了一個共產主義國家（Germany 民主共和國），而被 American、British 和 French 軍隊佔領的 Germany 西部則成為了 Germany 聯邦共和國，議會設在 Bonn。位於東 Germany 中間的 Berlin 也被類似地劃分，留下一個西 Germany 在東方的孤島。

For the next fifty years, until 1989, Germany remained divided into these two states.

在接下來的五十年裡，直到 1989 年，Germany 一直被分裂為這兩個國家。

When Hitler's power in Europe collapsed, the Japanese in Asia were still fighting on. No doubt, in time, Britain, America and Russia could have invaded Japan. But in the meantime scientists (some of them Jews who had fled from Hitler) in America had developed the most terrible weapon the world had ever known: the atom bomb. It was not necessary to invade Japan and lose the lives of thousands of American and British soldiers, one demonstration would make Japan surrender.

當 Hitler 在 Europe 的權力崩潰時，日本人在亞洲仍在繼續作戰。毫無疑問，假以時日 Britain、America 和 Russia 可以入侵日本。但與此同時，在 America 的科學家們（其中一些是從 Hitler 手中逃出的猶太人）已經研製出了世界上前所未見的最可怕的武器：原子彈。沒有必要入侵日本而犧牲成千上萬的 American 和 British 士兵的生命，只要展示一次就能讓日本投降。

The demonstration came on August 9, 1945; on that day an atom bomb was dropped on Hiroshima and two days later another on Nagasaki. In a second these two cities were turned into rubble, tens of thousands of people were turned into dust so fine that it could not be seen, the glare of the explosion burned every eye that had seen it, and over the doomed cities rose the strange and terrible mushroom-shaped cloud.

展示在 1945 年 8 月 9 日到來了；那一天一顆原子彈被投到了 Hiroshima，兩天後另一顆投到了 Nagasaki。在一瞬間這兩座城市被化為廢墟，數萬人變成了細微到肉眼看不見的塵埃，爆炸的強光灼傷了每一雙看到它的眼睛，在這些劫難的城市上空升起了奇異而可怕的蘑菇狀雲朵。

There were people who survived the atom bomb explosion in Hiroshima and Nagasaki. But the terrible thing was that many died later, slow and painful deaths resulting from the radioactive fallout. And worse was to come - years later when these survivors had children, some were born blind, or without arms, or otherwise horribly damaged.

有些人在 Hiroshima 和 Nagasaki 的原子彈爆炸中倖存了下來。但可怕的是，許多人後來死去了——死於放射性塵降所導致的緩慢而痛苦的死亡。更糟糕的還在後面——多年以後，當這些倖存者有了孩子，有些孩子生下來就是瞎的，或者沒有手臂，或者有其他可怕的缺陷。

Japan surrendered, and the Second World War came to an end in 1945. Realizing that in a world that had become a village, wars were madness, the nations of the world set up a council to settle all disputes peacefully: the United Nations, the UN. What really came was neither peace nor war, but the so-called Cold War.

日本投降了，第二次世界大戰在 1945 年結束。各國意識到在一個已經變成村莊的世界裡，戰爭是瘋狂的，於是世界各國建立了一個和平解決一切爭端的機構：聯合國。但真正到來的既不是和平也不是戰爭，而是所謂的冷戰。

America, which believed in a free market and in everybody making as much money as possible, and Russia, which believed in Communism and control of all things by the state, had never trusted each other, not even when they were allies during the war. As soon as the war against Hitler was over, they quite openly became enemies.

America 信奉自由市場和每個人盡可能多賺錢，Russia 信奉共產主義和國家對一切事物的控制——兩國從未信任過彼此，即使在戰爭期間他們是盟友時也不曾信任。一旦對 Hitler 的戰爭結束，他們就相當公開地成為了敵人。

At first the Americans thought that having the atom bomb made them stronger than Russia, that only the Americans knew how to make an atom bomb. But some scientists who had worked on the atom bomb were secretly Communists, and betraying the Americans, they gave the method of making atom bombs to the Russians.

起初 America 人認為擁有原子彈使他們比 Russia 更強大，認為只有 America 人知道如何製造原子彈。但一些參與過原子彈研製的科學家秘密地是共產黨員，他們背叛了 America 人，把製造原子彈的方法交給了 Russia 人。

Since then, America and Russia have both developed even more terrible bombs - each now having sufficient weaponry to kill all life on earth. And since then, many more countries have developed nuclear capabilities.

從那以後，America 和 Russia 都研製出了更加可怕的炸彈——如今各自擁有足以殺死地球上所有生命的武器。從那以後，更多的國家也發展了核武能力。

As long as there is nationalism, countries will not reach agreements to scrap these terrible weapons. But the Second World War has not only bequeathed us the atom bomb, but something else.

只要民族主義存在，各國就不會達成銷毀這些可怕武器的協議。但第二次世界大戰不僅給我們留下了原子彈，還留下了其他東西。

The people in the colonies were no longer willing to be under the rule of the white men. They demanded freedom, they demanded equality, fraternity, and Britain and France had to give up their colonies, one after another. The great colonial empires of the nineteenth century disappeared, and in their place came new independent states.

殖民地的人民不再願意生活在白人的統治之下。他們要求自由，要求平等、博愛，Britain 和 France 不得不一個接一個地放棄他們的殖民地。十九世紀的偉大殖民帝國消失了，取而代之的是新的獨立國家。

---

Chapter 53
Prospects

第五十三章
展望

In the fifty years following the Second World War, the Cold War divided not only America and Russia but the whole world into two camps. On the one side the western countries - America, Britain, France, western Germany - believed in free enterprise, they believed that each person should be free to think as they like, to work as they like and to have as much property as they can acquire.

在第二次世界大戰之後的五十年裡，冷戰不僅分裂了 America 和 Russia，也把整個世界分成了兩個陣營。一邊是西方國家——America、Britain、France、西 Germany——相信自由企業，相信每個人都應該自由地思考、自由地工作、擁有他們能獲取的財產。

In the East, Russia and Poland and Yugoslavia, in China, there was the Communist system which believed that the whole community, the state should lay down what each person should think, how and where they should work and that no one should own property such as houses, factories, or land. Only the state, the whole community, could own property.

在東方，Russia、Poland、Yugoslavia，以及 China，實行的是共產主義制度，這個制度認為整個社會、國家應該規定每個人應該想什麼、應該怎樣以及在哪裡工作，而且沒有人應該擁有像房屋、工廠或土地那樣的財產。只有國家、整個社會才能擁有財產。

In the West, there was a stronger belief in freedom, in liberty, and people expected to have freedom in everything: in thinking, in writing, but also in business, in economics.

在西方，人們更加信仰自由，人們期待在所有事情上都擁有自由：思想的自由、寫作的自由，同時也包括商業和經濟的自由。

In the East, in the Communist countries, there was a much greater feeling for brotherhood, for fraternity, for people working for the whole community. But they wanted this community in everything, not only in the work people did, but also in what they thought. And so, in the Communist countries, no book or newspaper could be printed, no teacher could teach, without the approval of the government.

在東方，在共產主義國家裡，有一種更強烈的兄弟情誼、博愛的感受，人們為整個社會而工作。但他們要求在所有事情上都實行這種集體主義，不僅是在人們所做的工作上，也包括在人們的思想上。因此在共產主義國家裡，沒有政府的批准，任何書籍或報紙都不能印刷，任何教師都不能教書。

The western countries, the capitalist countries as the Communists called them, put too many things in one basket called freedom. And the eastern countries, the Communist countries, put too many things in one basket called brotherhood, fraternity.

西方國家——共產黨人稱之為資本主義國家——把太多東西放進了一個叫做「自由」的籃子裡。而東方國家——共產主義國家——則把太多東西放進了一個叫做「博愛」的籃子裡。

Today we can see two tendencies in the world. On the one hand countries are forming alliances, such as the European Union, usually beginning from an economic viewpoint, but then, as we have seen with Europe, spreading to all aspects of life.

今天我們可以在世界上看到兩種趨勢。一方面，各國正在組成聯盟，比如歐洲聯盟，通常從經濟的角度開始，但隨後，如我們在 Europe 所看到的，擴展到了生活的各個層面。

On the other we see more and more countries splitting and falling apart, often violently, into fiercely nationalistic and ethnic groupings.

另一方面，我們看到越來越多的國家分裂和瓦解，往往是以暴力的方式，分裂成激烈的民族主義和族群團體。

And there will be no peace and no real progress in the new states around the world until nationalism is recognized as something that does not belong to our time, and until liberty, equality, fraternity are each put in their right place in life.

除非民族主義被認識到是一種不屬於我們時代的東西，除非自由、平等、博愛各自被放到生活中正確的位置上，否則世界上的新興國家就不會有和平，也不會有真正的進步。

Our own future will very much depend on how these questions are solved. No matter how well we do in our job, the world is only one big village and any spot of trouble or fighting in one corner can lead to a world-wide catastrophe, that destroys our work and our hopes. But by knowing the right place for liberty, the right place for equality and the right place for fraternity, we can contribute something towards a better world, a world in which children can grow up without the dark cloud of war and destruction hanging over them. Don't think that a single person can do nothing; it is not what Garibaldi thought, and not what Henri Dunant thought.

我們自己的未來在很大程度上取決於這些問題如何被解決。無論我們在自己的工作中做得多好，世界只是一個大村莊，任何一個角落的麻煩或戰鬥都可能導致一場世界性的災難，摧毀我們的工作和希望。但透過認識自由的正確位置、平等的正確位置和博愛的正確位置，我們可以為一個更美好的世界做出一些貢獻——一個孩子們可以在沒有戰爭和毀滅的烏雲籠罩下成長的世界。不要認為一個人什麼都做不了；Garibaldi 不是這麼想的，Henri Dunant 也不是這麼想的。

So we have come to the end of our history lessons. They started with the five sons of Pandu in ancient India,\* and that was the time when men hardly felt at home on earth and longed to go back to heaven. Then in the Persian times gods still appeared in dreams and gave men their fine inventions, like the plough. We came then to the times of ancient Greece when the dreams disappeared and men began to think for themselves. Then there was the rise and fall of the Roman Empire - and that was the time when Jesus Christ told men that they were all brothers - sons of the Father in Heaven.

我們的歷史課就到此結束了。它從古代 India 的 Pandu 五子開始，\*那是人們在地球上幾乎感覺不到自在、渴望回到天上的時代。接著在 Persia 時代，神靈仍會在夢中顯現，賜予人們精巧的發明，比如犁。然後我們來到了古 Greece 時代，夢境消失了，人們開始獨立思考。接著是 Roman 帝國的興衰——那是 Jesus Christ 告訴人們他們都是兄弟——天父之子——的時代。

Then the warlike Germanic tribes destroyed the Roman Empire and set up new kingdoms, like the Angles and Saxons who came to Britain. These wild tribes became Christians - and their fighting spirit became tamed in the rules of knighthood.

接著好戰的日耳曼部落摧毀了 Roman 帝國，建立了新的王國，就像來到 Britain 的 Angles 和 Saxons。這些野蠻的部落成為了基督徒——他們的好戰精神在騎士制度的規範中被馴化了。

The rise of Islam amongst the Arabs was followed with the wealth and power of Baghdad and the other Arab cities. And the Crusades, which failed to keep Jerusalem Christian, brought new knowledge to Europe and made people curious about far-away lands. Spices became highly desirable and ships began to sail out to India, the land of spices. And so Columbus sailed West to reach India and, instead, discovered America.

伊斯蘭教在阿拉伯人中崛起，隨之而來的是 Baghdad 和其他阿拉伯城市的財富與權力。而十字軍東征雖然未能讓 Jerusalem 保持基督教信仰，卻為 Europe 帶來了新的知識，使人們對遙遠的土地產生了好奇。香料變得備受渴求，船隻開始航向 India——那個香料之國。於是 Columbus 向西航行以到達 India，結果卻發現了 America。

Then followed Leonardo, the Renaissance genius, and Luther and the Reformation. Then came the wars of religion, and the Civil War in Britain between the Roundheads and Cavaliers, and in Scotland the last Stuart King, Bonnie Prince Charlie.

接著是文藝復興天才 Leonardo，以及 Luther 和宗教改革。然後是宗教戰爭，Britain 的圓顱黨與保皇黨之間的內戰，以及 Scotland 最後一位 Stuart 國王——英俊王子 Charlie。

Then came the history of France - from the proud Roi Soleil, Louis XIV, to the French Revolution and Napoleon. That was the time when the ideas of liberty, equality, fraternity were introduced to humanity.

接著是 France 的歷史——從驕傲的太陽王 Louis 十四，到法國大革命和 Napoleon。那是自由、平等、博愛的理念被引入人類的時代。
